Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
beginner
8 min
Definition and Virtue of Jihad in Hanafi Fiqh
Introduction to Kitab al-Siyar defining Jihad and its virtues with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define jihad and ribat according to Hanafi fiqh, and state the relative virtue of jihad among good deeds as established by prophetic hadiths.

Core Idea
Jihad is expending full capacity for Allah's cause; its virtue is third only to prayer and parental obedience.

This passage opens the chapter on Jihad (Kitab al-Siyar) by clarifying its meaning and emphasizing its merit. While the term 'jihad' is often narrowly understood as armed combat, the Hanafi tradition expands it to include support with wealth, counsel, and moral backing. The author then underscores its rank through two authentic hadiths, placing it just after faith and prayer in virtue. Understanding this foundation is key before studying the specific rules of jihad.

Guided Path
1
Define Siyar lexically and technically
Siyar is the plural of sirah, meaning a method; in Shari'ah it specifically refers to the Prophet's conduct in his military expeditions.
The book title 'Kitab al-Siyar' thus sets the context for rules of jihad and international conduct.
2
Define Jihad and its forms
Jihad is calling to the true religion and fighting those who reject it; its definition includes expending all capacity (personal combat, financial aid, advice, increasing numbers) in Allah's cause.
The commentator emphasizes that even non-combat support is part of jihad.
3
Define Ribat as subordinate to Jihad
Ribat is guarding the frontier between Islamic territory and the abode of disbelief; it is a chosen view (qawl mukhtar).
Ribat derives its merit from being a form of sustained readiness for jihad.
4
Analyze the hadith evidence for Jihad's virtue
Two hadiths from Bukhari and Muslim rank jihad third after prayer and parental obedience (Ibn Mas'ud) or second after faith (Abu Hurayrah). The commentator reconciles by considering faith as encompassing all obligations.
The 'greater jihad' (internal struggle) is mentioned as more difficult than external combat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
كِتَابُ السِّيرِ
ترجمہ یہ کتاب سیر کے بیان میں ہے السیر کا لغوی اور شرعی معنی
ليرُ جَمْعُ سِيرَةِ وَهِيَ الطَّرِيقَةُ فِي الْأُمُورِ وَ فِي الشَّرْعِ تَخْتَصُّ بِسِيرِ النَّبِي عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِي مَغَازِيهِ ترجمه سیر سیرۃ کی جمع ہے اور وہ کاموں میں ایک طریقہ کو کہتے ہیں اور شریعت میں اس مخصوص طریقہ کو کہتے ہیں جو رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنے جہاد میں برتا ہو۔
تشریح شریعت میں جہاد دین حق کی طرف بلانے اور جو اسے قبول نہ کرے اس سے قتال کرنے کو کہتے ہیں۔ اور ظاہر یہ ہے کہ عرب کے سوا جو شخص مطیع ہونے اور جزیہ دینے پر بھی راضی نہ ہو اس سے بھی قتال کرنا۔ اس جہاد کی تعریف یہ ہے یعنی پوری صلاحیت کو اللہ کے راستہ میں قتال کرنے میں صرف کر دینا۔ خواہ اس طرح کہ خود اپنی ذات سے قتال کرنا یا قتال کرنے والے غازیوں کی مدد کرنا خواہ مال سے ہو یا رائے اور مشورے دے کر ہو۔ یا ان کی جمعیت اور بھیڑ بڑھا کر ہو یا کسی بھی دوسری صورت سے ہو ۔ ( ابن الکمال ) جہاد کے تابع رباط ہے۔ رباط کے معنی ہیں اسلام کے اس سرحد پر جس کے بعد دار الکفر ہو وہاں پر قیام کرنا ۔ یہی قول مختار ہے۔ جہاد کی فضیلت بہت زیادہ ہے۔ کیوں نہ ہو کہ آدمی اللہ کی رضا مندی حاصل کرنے کے لئے بہت سی مشقتوں کو برداشت کرتے ہوئے اپنی جان اور مال سب کچھ فدا کر دیتا ہے۔ اس سے بھی زیادہ مشکل بات یہ ہے کہ ظاہر اور باطن خوشی اور غمی ہر حالت میں اپنے نفس کو اللہ تعالٰی کی عبادت پر قائم رکھے اسی لئے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایک مرتبہ ایک جہاد سے لوٹتے وقت فرمایا کہ ہم چھوٹے جہاد سے بڑے جہاد کی طرف لوٹے۔ اسی لئے حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ کی حدیث میں ہے کہ میں نے عرض کیا۔ یا رسول اللہ (صلى الله عليه وسلم) اعمال میں کون ساعمل افضل ہے؟ فرمایا کہ نماز کو اپنے وقت پر پڑھنا۔ میں نے عرض کیا پھر؟ آپ نے فرمایا والدین کی فرمان برداری کرنا۔ میں نے عرض کیا پھر ؟ فرمایا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کی راہ میں جہاد کرنا۔ اور اگر میں آپ سے اور زیادہ پوچھتا تو زیادہ ہی فرماتے۔ (رواہ البخاری) اور حضرت ابو ہریرہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کی حدیث میں ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے پوچھا گیا کہ کونسا کام افضل ہے فرمایا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ اور اس کے رسولوں پر دل سے سچا یقین رکھنا۔ عرض کیا گیا کہ پھر کو سب عمل افضل ہے۔ فرمایا اللہ تعالیٰ کی راہ میں جہاد کرنا عرض کیا گیا کہ پھر کونسا عمل سے فرمایا کہ حج مبرور۔ (رواہ البخاری و مسلم)
اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اللہ تعالیٰ اور اس کے رسول پر ایمان لانا۔ نماز، روزہ اور زکوۃ کو شامل تھا۔ یعنی جب سچا یقین کر لیا تو اس کے بعد نماز ترک کرنا ممکن نہیں رہے گا۔ اس لئے حضرت معاذ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کی حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے قسم کے ساتھ نماز فریضہ کے بعد
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The Book of Siyar. Translation: This book is about Siyar. The lexical and Shari' meaning of al-siyar: Siyar is the plural of sirah, which means a method in matters. In Shari'ah, it is specifically applied to the Prophet's (peace be upon him) conduct in his military expeditions. Explanation: In Shari'ah, jihad is to call to the true religion and to fight those who do not accept it. And apparently, besides the Arabs, whoever is not satisfied with submission and paying jizyah, fighting them is also jihad. The definition of jihad is to expend all capacity in fighting in the way of Allah, whether by fighting oneself, or by assisting the fighters, whether with wealth, or by giving opinions and advice, or by increasing their numbers, or in any other way. (Ibn al-Kamal). Subordinate to jihad is ribat. Ribat means staying on that frontier of Islam beyond which is the abode of disbelief. This is the chosen view. The virtue of jihad is immense. Why not? A person endures many hardships to gain Allah's pleasure and sacrifices his life and wealth. More difficult than that is to keep one's soul constant in worship of Allah in all states, outwardly and inwardly, in happiness and sorrow. That is why the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said once when returning from a jihad: 'We have returned from the lesser jihad to the greater jihad.' Similarly, in the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him): I asked, 'O Messenger of Allah, which action is most virtuous?' He said, 'Prayer at its appointed time.' I asked, 'Then what?' He said, 'Obedience to parents.' I asked, 'Then what?' He said, 'Jihad in the way of Allah.' And if I had asked more, he would have said more. (Narrated by Bukhari). And in the hadith of Abu Hurayrah (may Allah be pleased with him): The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was asked, 'Which action is most virtuous?' He said, 'Having sincere belief in Allah and His Messengers.' It was asked, 'Then which action?' He said, 'Jihad in the way of Allah.' It was asked, 'Then which action?' He said, 'An accepted Hajj.' (Narrated by Bukhari and Muslim). Its meaning is that believing in Allah and His Messenger includes prayer, fasting, and zakat. That is, when one has true conviction, then neglecting prayer becomes impossible. Therefore, in the hadith of Mu'adh (may Allah be pleased with him), the Prophet swore that after the obligatory prayer...
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and virtue-oriented introduction to Kitab al-Siyar. It begins by explaining the term 'Siyar' linguistically as a method or conduct, and in Shari'ah it specifically refers to the Prophet's conduct in his military campaigns (maghazi). The commentator then defines 'jihad' as calling to the true religion and fighting those who reject it, with a note that non-Arabs who refuse submission and jizyah are also fought. Jihad is expending all capacity in fighting for Allah's sake, whether physically, by assisting fighters with wealth, opinion, or numbers. Subordinate to jihad is 'ribat', meaning guarding the Islamic frontier facing the abode of disbelief. The author then extols the virtue of jihad, quoting two hadiths from Bukhari and Muslim. The first, from Ibn Mas'ud, ranks jihad third after prayer on time and obedience to parents. The second, from Abu Hurayrah, ranks jihad after faith. The commentator clarifies that faith includes the obligatory acts, making the ranking consistent. The passage ends with a reference to Mu'adh's hadith about prayer being the most important after faith.

Key Terms
السير (al-siyar): Plural of sirah; in this text, it refers to the Prophet's conduct in his military expeditions.
الجهاد (al-jihad): Expending all capacity in fighting for Allah's cause, including personal combat, assistance, or support.
الرباط (al-ribat): Stationing at the Islamic frontier facing the abode of disbelief to guard the borders.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (RA) mentioned in the passage, which act is the most virtuous after praying on time?
A) Jihad in the way of Allah
B) Obedience to parents
C) Hajj mabroor
D) Fasting in Ramadan

Key Takeaway
Jihad is a broad concept in Hanafi fiqh, encompassing various forms of support, and its virtue is highly emphasized in the Prophet's hadiths.

Jihad as Fard Kifayah: Proofs and Rationale
Ruling with proof: jihad as fard kifayah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jihad as fard kifayah and explain the proof from Quran, hadith, and qiyas to funeral prayer.

Core Idea
Jihad is fard kifayah because its purpose (elevating religion) can be achieved by some, not each individual.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, the author establishes that jihad is a collective obligation (fard kifayah). We will examine the Quranic verse (9:36), the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him), and the key reasoning (ta'lil) that distinguishes it from a personal obligation. The analogy to funeral prayer and returning greetings clarifies why the duty falls from the rest when a sufficient number undertakes it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage opens by stating that jihad is fard kifayah. This means if a group undertakes it, the obligation is waived from others.
Contrast this with fard ayn, which each individual must personally perform.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The author cites Quran 9:36: 'Fight the polytheists all together as they fight you all together.' The word 'kaffah' (all together) is key.
The word implies a collective command, not an individual one.
3
Analyse the hadith proof
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Jihad will continue until the Day of Judgment.' The author interprets this as an enduring obligation.
Ongoing obligation does not specify each individual, so it is collective.
4
Understand the ta'lil (purpose-based reasoning)
Jihad is not prescribed for its own sake (since fighting involves corruption), but to elevate Allah's religion and repel evil. When that objective is achieved by some, the duty drops from others.
This is the core rationale for it being fard kifayah.
5
Study the qiyas (analogy)
The author draws an analogy to funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) and returning greetings (radd al-salam), which are also fard kifayah.
In both cases, the purpose is fulfilled by some, so the rest are absolved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جہاد کا حکم
(اطرافی)
قَالَ الْجِهَادُ فَرْضٌ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ إِذَاقَامَ بِهِ فَرِيقٌ مِنَ النَّاسِ سَقَطَ عَنِ الْبَاقِينَ أَمَّا الْفَرْضِيَّةُ فَلِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فَاقْتُلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ كَافَةَ كَمَا يُقَاتِلُونَكُمْ كَافَةَ وَلِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الْجِهَادُ مَاضٍ إِلى يَوْمِ الْقِيمَةِ وَأَرَادَ بِهِ فَرْضًا بَاقِيًّا وَ هُوَ فَرْضٌ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ لِأَنَّهُ مَا فُرِضَ لِعَيْنِهِ إِذْ هُوَ إِفْسَادٌ فِي نَفْسِهِ وَإِنَّمَا فُرِضَ لِإِعْزَازِ دِينِ اللَّهِ وَدَفْعِ الشَّرِّ عَنِ الْعِبَادِ فَإِذَا حَصَلَ الْمَقْصُودُ بِالْبَعْضِ سَقَطَ عَنِ الْبَاقِينَ كَصَلَاةِ الْجَنَازَةِ وَرَدِّ السَّلَامِ
The ruling on Jihad
(From the margins)
He said: Jihad is a collective obligation (fard kifayah). When a group of people undertakes it, it is waived from the rest. As for its being obligatory, it is due to His statement (the Most High): 'And fight the polytheists all together as they fight you all together' (Quran 9:36), and due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Jihad will continue until the Day of Judgment' and he meant by it an enduring obligation. And it is a collective obligation because it was not prescribed for its own sake, since it is corruption in itself, but rather it was prescribed to elevate Allah's religion and to repel evil from the servants. So when the objective is achieved by some, it is waived from the rest, like the funeral prayer and returning greetings.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is the ruling from the matn of Al-Hidayah, stating that jihad is fard kifayah (collective obligation). The author first states the ruling, then provides two proofs: (1) the Quranic verse 'fight the polytheists all together' which implies a collective duty, and (2) the hadith 'jihad will continue until the Day of Judgment' indicating it is an enduring obligation. However, it is fard kifayah, not fard ayn, because its purpose is to elevate Allah's religion and repel evil from people. If that objective is achieved by some, the obligation falls from the rest. The reasoning (ta'lil) is: jihad is not obligatory for its own sake (since fighting involves corruption), but for a higher purpose. When that purpose is fulfilled by a sufficient number, the obligation on others drops. This is analogous to funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) and returning greetings (radd al-salam), which are also collective obligations. The Hanafi school emphasizes that jihad's obligatory status depends on the need. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
فَرْضٌ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ (fard kifayah): A collective obligation; if performed by a sufficient number, it is waived from others.
كَافَة (kaffah): All together; in the verse it implies the whole community collectively.
إِعْزَازِ دِينِ اللَّهِ (i'zaz dinillah): To elevate Allah's religion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school classify jihad as fard kifayah rather than fard ayn?
A) Because the Quran commands fighting all polytheists
B) Because jihad is prescribed for a purpose (elevating religion) that can be achieved by some
C) Because the Prophet said jihad will continue until Judgment Day
D) Because fighting always involves corruption

Key Takeaway
Jihad is a collective obligation (fard kifayah) in the Hanafi school, derived from the Quranic command 'fight all together', the hadith of its continuity, and a purpose-driven analysis that distinguishes it from individual duties.

Virtues of Jihad and Ribat: Spiritual Foundations
Narrating hadiths on the virtue of jihad and ribat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the virtues of jihad and ribat as mentioned in the hadiths and explain why these narrations serve as motivational prelude to the legal rulings in the Hanafi chapter on Jihad.

Core Idea
Jihad and ribat are immensely virtuous deeds, with rewards exceeding regular worship.

This passage presents a series of hadiths that underscore the immense spiritual merit of Jihad and Ribat. The author gathers these narrations before delving into the legal rulings, aiming to inspire the reader. Understanding these virtues is crucial for appreciating the significance of the subsequent fiqh discussions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key hadiths and their narrators
List the Companions from whom these hadiths are reported: 'Imran ibn Husayn, Abu Hurayrah, Salman, Abu Umamah. Note the hadith sources (Tirmidhi, Hakim, Bukhari, Muslim, etc.) even if some are uncertain due to OCR.
The OCR may have corrupted names (e.g., 'al-Tirmidhi' rendered as 'al-Tarandi'). This does not affect the legal content.
2
Summarize the virtue mentioned in each hadith
For each hadith, extract the comparison or reward. Example: 'Standing in Jihad ranks is better than a year of worship' (Imran ibn Husayn). 'A mujahid is like one who fasts continuously and prays all night' (Abu Hurayrah). 'One day of Ribat is better than a month of fasting and night vigil' (Salman).
3
Analyze the rhetorical purpose
Notice the author's technique: presenting hadiths of extreme reward before legal rules. This is common in fiqh texts to encourage the reader. The passage does not derive legal rulings; it establishes spiritual context.
In Hanafi fiqh, these hadiths are not used as primary evidence for legal obligations but as motivators (targhib).
4
Connect to the chapter's overall structure
Recognize that this is a front-matter section. The chapter (Kitab al-Siyar) will later detail conditions, obligations, and rules of Jihad. These hadiths ensure the reader approaches with reverence and willingness.

Source Text

كتاب السير
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هشتم
جہاد فی سبیل اللہ کو قرار دیا ۔ (رواه الترندی)
معلوم ہونا چاہئے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے ساتھ جتنے صحابہ کرام جہاد کرتے تھے وہ بخوبی نماز اور دوسرے تمام فرائض کے پابند تھے ۔ اسی لئے حضرت عمران بن حصین کی حدیث میں آیا ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ جہاد کی صف میں آدمی کا کھڑا ہونا۔ اس کے ساتھ برس کی عبادت سے افضل ہے۔ (رواہ الحاکم)
رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے وقت میں جہاد ایک اہم امر اور فرض عین تھا۔ یہاں تک کہ فتح مکہ ہو گیا۔ اسی لئے حضرت ابو ہر سیر و رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کی حدیث میں ہے کہ جب یہ سوال کیا گیا کہ یا رسول اللہ (صلى الله عليه وسلم) کون سا عمل ایسا ہے جو جہاد کی برابری کرے؟ فرمایا کہ تم اس کو نہیں کر سکو گے۔ یہ بات کئی بار عرض کی گئی اور آپ ہر بار یہی ارشاد فرماتے رہے۔ پھر فرمایا کہ مجاہد فی سبیل اللہ کی مثال ایسے شخص کی سی ہے جو برابر روزے رکھے اور رات بھر نمازیں پڑھتا رہے۔ کسی وقت بھی نماز اور روزہ میں سستی نہ کرے یہاں تک کہ مجاہد واپس آ جائے۔
( رواه البخاری ومسلم )
اور حضرت ابو ہریرہ رضی اللہ عنہ کی حدیث میں ہے کہ جس نے اللہ تعالیٰ پر ایمان لایا اور اس کے وعدوں کو سچا مان کر اپنا گھوڑا اللہ تعالی کے راستہ میں وقف کر دیا تو اس کا دانہ اور پانی سے سیراب ہونا اور اس کی لید اور پیشاب کرنا قیامت کے دن اس کے اعمال خیر کی میزان ہوگا۔ (رواہ البخاری)
اور جہاد کے تابع رباط بھی ہے۔ اس رباط کی فضیلت کے بارے میں بہت سی حدیثیں ہیں چنانچہ حضرت سلمان رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کی حدیث میں ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم فرماتے تھے کہ اللہ کی راہ میں ایک دن کا رباط کرنا ایک مہینہ کے روزے اور شب بیداری سے بہتر ہے۔ اور اگر اس حالت میں مر گیا تو جتنے بھی نیکی کے کام کرتا تھا وہ سب برابر جاری رہیں گے۔ اور اس پر اس کا رزق بھی جاری رہے گا۔ اور وہ فتنوں سے محفوظ ہو گیا۔ (رواه مسلم) اور وہ قیامت کے دن شہید کی حیثیت سے اٹھایا جائے گا۔ اور قیامت کے فزع اکبر (سب سے زیادہ گھبرا دینے والی چیز ) سے محفوظ ہو گیا۔ ( رواه ابن ماجه والظهر انی) اور ابوامامہ کی حدیث میں ہے کہ مرابط کی ایک نماز پانچ سو نمازوں کے برابر ہے اور ایک دینار یا درہم کا خرچ کرنا سات سو اشرفیوں کے صدقہ کرنے سے بہتر ہے۔
Book of Siyar. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 8. He declared Jihad in the path of Allah. (Narrated by al-Tirmidhi). It should be known that all the Companions who performed Jihad with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) were fully committed to prayer and all other obligations. For this reason, in the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: A person standing in the ranks of Jihad is better than a year of worship. (Narrated by al-Hakim). In the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), Jihad was an important matter and fardh 'ayn until the conquest of Makkah occurred. For this reason, in the hadith of Abu Hurayrah (may Allah be pleased with him), when asked: O Messenger of Allah, which deed is equal to Jihad? He said: You cannot do it. He was asked several times and each time he said the same. Then he said: The example of a mujahid in the path of Allah is like a person who fasts continuously and prays all night, never slackening in prayer and fasting until the mujahid returns. (Narrated by Bukhari and Muslim). And in the hadith of Abu Hurayrah (may Allah be pleased with him): Whoever believes in Allah and considers His promises true, and dedicates his horse in the path of Allah, then its feeding and watering, its dung and urine will be on the scale of his good deeds on the Day of Resurrection. (Narrated by Bukhari). And associated with Jihad is Ribat. There are many hadiths about the virtue of Ribat. In the hadith of Salman (may Allah be pleased with him): The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to say: One day of Ribat in the path of Allah is better than a month of fasting and night vigil. If he dies in that state, all the good deeds he used to do will continue, his provision will continue, and he will be protected from trials. (Narrated by Muslim). He will be raised as a martyr on the Day of Resurrection, and will be protected from the greatest terror (al-Faza' al-Akbar). (Narrated by Ibn Majah and al-Daraqutni [?]). And in the hadith of Abu Umamah: One prayer of a Murabit is equal to five hundred prayers, and spending one dinar or dirham is better than giving seven hundred dinars in charity.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a collection of narrations (ahadith) related to the virtues of Jihad and Ribat. It serves as an introductory motivation for the chapter on Jihad (Kitab al-Siyar). The author gathers hadiths from various sources to highlight the immense reward and excellence of Jihad and guarding the frontiers (Ribat). The section emphasizes that Jihad was a communal obligation in early Islam, and its reward is vast, even comparing one standing in the ranks of Jihad to a year of worship, and a mujahid to one who continuously fasts and prays. Ribat (frontier guard duty) is also extolled: one day of Ribat is better than a month of fasting and praying, and its rewards continue even after death. The hadiths are presented without extensive legal analysis, serving as spiritual encouragement for the reader to understand the significance of Jihad before delving into its legal rulings.

Key Terms
جهاد (jihad): Struggling or fighting in the path of Allah to elevate His word and defend the faith.
رباط (ribat): Stationing oneself at a frontier post to guard Islamic territory against enemy attack.
مرابط (murabit): A person performing ribat, stationed at a frontier for the defense of Muslim lands.

Jihad as Fard Kifayah: The Hanafi Ruling and Its Proofs
Ruling with proof: jihad as fard kifayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of jihad as fard kifayah, identify its Quranic and hadith proofs, and explain the analogy with funeral prayer and greeting response.

Core Idea
Jihad is a collective obligation: if some fulfill it, the rest are absolved; if none do, all are sinful.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on jihad as stated by Imam al-Quduri. The passage establishes that jihad is fard kifayah, not fard 'ayn, using Quranic and prophetic proofs and an analogy with other communal obligations. We will unpack the reasoning behind this classification and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What does al-Quduri say about the legal status of jihad? He states it is fard kifayah, meaning if some undertake it the obligation drops from the rest.
This is the foundational statement.
2
Locate the two proofs
The passage cites the Quranic verse 'Fight the polytheists all together' and the hadith 'Jihad continues until the Day of Resurrection' as evidence for the obligation.
These are the primary textual evidences (dalil naqli).
3
Analyse the reasoning
Jihad is not obligatory for its own sake because it involves destruction. It is prescribed to elevate Allah's religion and remove fitnah. Therefore, if the objective is achieved by a group, the rest are absolved.
This is the rationale (ta'lil) behind fard kifayah.
4
Understand the analogy
Jihad is compared to funeral prayer and responding to greetings, which are also communal obligations. If some perform them, the obligation drops from the others.
This is qiyas, strengthening the ruling.
5
Apply the nuance
The obligation is primarily on those closest to the enemy. If they fail, it extends to others, potentially becoming fard 'ayn on all necessitating personal participation.
This dynamic shows the ruling is not absolute but conditional.

لِأَنَّ الْوُجُوبَ عَلَى الْكُلَّ وَلانَّ فِي اشْتِغَالِ الْكُلَّ بِهِ قَطعَ مَادَّةِ الجِهَادِ
Ruling of Jihad. (Margin) He said: Jihad is a collective obligation (fard kifayah). If a group of people undertake it, it falls from the rest. As for its obligation, it is due to His statement: 'Fight the polytheists all together as they fight you all together,' and due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Jihad continues until the Day of Resurrection' and he meant by it an enduring obligation. And it is a collective obligation because it was not made obligatory for its own sake, as in itself it involves corruption (destruction). Rather, it was made obligatory to elevate the religion of Allah and to repel evil from the people. So if the purpose is achieved by some, it falls from the rest, like the funeral prayer and the response to greeting. Page 21 (of the Urdu text) ... Translation: al-Quduri said: Jihad is fard kifayah, meaning if some people perform jihad, the obligation is lifted from the rest. The proof for its obligatory nature is the command of Allah: 'Fight the polytheists all together...' and the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Jihad continues...' meaning jihad is ongoing until the Day of Resurrection. The Prophet's intent here is not that people will continue to perform jihad, but that jihad is an enduring obligation that will never be abrogated. It is fard kifayah because jihad was not made obligatory for its own sake, as it inherently involves corruption (killing, destruction). Rather, it was made obligatory to grant honor to Allah's religion and to remove the trials of shirk and corruption from the people. Thus, if this objective is achieved by some, there is no need to keep the obligation on the rest; it drops from them, like the funeral prayer and the response to greeting. Now, if not a single group performs jihad, then all are sinful because the obligation is on everyone. (The meaning of fard kifayah is that it is obligatory on all, but if some fulfill it, the sin of not doing it is removed from the rest. However, the reward is only for those who performed it.) Explanation: He said: Jihad is fard kifayah, similar to the funeral prayer and responding to greeting. If some people pray the funeral prayer, it is fulfilled for all and its obligation drops. Similarly, if someone in a gathering responds to a greeting, the obligation to respond drops from the rest. If no one prays the funeral prayer and the deceased is buried without it, or no one responds to a greeting, then all are sinful for abandoning an obligatory act. Similarly, the objective of jihad is to remove corruption, evils, trials of shirk and kufr, and to establish tawheed and justice of Allah. So if this objective is achieved by the effort of a few, the obligation drops from the rest. But if no one performs jihad, all are sinful. Rather, the more apparent view is that all the people of that country who, upon hearing [the call], did not participate in jihad without an excuse, are sinful. In Durr al-Mukhtar it is narrated: Do not think that if the people of Syria begin jihad, its obligation drops from the people of India. Rather, it is obligatory on those who are closest to the disbelievers, then on those next closest, then on those further away, until if those near cannot fully accomplish the task, it becomes obligatory on those further away. If the need arises for all obligated Muslims, then jihad becomes fard 'ayn on each individual like prayer and fasting. It is also written that if slaves and women come forward and they are sufficient, they suffice for everyone. In conclusion, the meaning of fard kifayah is that if some people fulfill the duty and participate, the obligation is lifted from those who did not participate. The sin of abandoning jihad: If no one undertakes it, then all the people become sinful due to abandoning it, because the obligation is on all, and because if all engage in it, the matter of jihad would be cut off (i.e., everyone would be engaged).
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm with dalil) from the Hanafi school, specifically from the matn of al-Quduri. It establishes that jihad is fard kifayah (collective obligation), not fard 'ayn (individual obligation). The author provides two primary proofs: the Quranic verse 'Fight the polytheists all together' and the hadith 'Jihad continues until the Day of Resurrection.' The verse commands collective fighting, indicating communal obligation. The hadith shows jihad is an enduring obligation, but the author clarifies that the Prophet's intent is that the obligation remains, not that every individual must always fight. The rationale for it being fard kifayah is that jihad involves killing and destruction, which is not desirable in itself; it is only prescribed as a means to achieve the higher purpose of honoring Allah's religion and removing fitnah. Therefore, if the purpose is achieved by a sufficient number, the obligation drops from the rest. The author analogizes jihad to two other collective obligations: funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) and responding to greetings (radd al-salam). If some perform these, others are absolved. Conversely, if no one performs jihad, all are sinful because the obligation initially rests on everyone. The commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah elaborates on the nuances: the obligation is primarily on those closest to the enemy, then on successive circles. If the nearest cannot suffice, it becomes fard 'ayn on all. It also notes that women and slaves can participate and if they suffice, they discharge the duty. The passage concludes with a reminder that fard kifayah means the obligation is on all collectively but drops upon sufficient performance.

Key Terms
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A communal obligation: if some Muslims perform it, the obligation is lifted from the rest; if none perform it, all are sinful.
جهاد (jihad): Armed struggle against non-believers to establish the supremacy of Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, what is the primary evidence that jihad is a collective obligation?
A) The hadith 'Jihad continues until the Day of Resurrection'
B) The Quranic verse 'Fight the polytheists all together'
C) The analogy with zakat
D) The ijma of the Sahaba

Key Takeaway
Jihad is fard kifayah: a communal obligation that, if sufficiently fulfilled by some, absolves the rest; otherwise, all are sinful.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate

Rational Proof for Jihad as Fard Kifayah
Ruling with rational proof and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rational proof for why jihad is fard kifayah and identify the condition when it becomes fard 'ayn.

Core Idea
If everyone fights, no one supplies weapons—so jihad must be communal, not individual.

In this passage, the author reinforces the ruling that jihad is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) by providing a rational proof rooted in the preservation of the means of war. He also clarifies an important exception: when an enemy launches a surprise attack, jihad becomes an individual duty (fard 'ayn) on every capable person in the affected area. Understanding this nuance prevents the misconception that jihad can never be individually obligatory.

Guided Path
1
State the sin of total abandonment
Identify the ruling: if no one performs jihad, all are sinful because the obligation initially falls on everyone collectively.
This establishes the baseline: jihad is wajib on the community.
2
Analyze the rational proof
The author argues: if all Muslims were to engage directly in combat, no one would remain to produce weapons, breed horses, or provide logistics. Therefore, it is necessary that only a sufficient number fight while others support.
Proof type: qiyas based on maslaha (preservation of jihad itself).
3
Identify the exception for fard 'ayn
When the enemy attacks a Muslim territory without warning, jihad becomes fard 'ayn on the inhabitants of that land, and successively on those nearby if needed.
This exception overrides the default communal classification.
4
Note the person who intends but is prevented
A person who intends to go but stays due to others not going or the sultan forbidding is not sinful.
Clarifies that sin attaches to total abandonment, not individual inability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترک جہاد کا گناہ
فَإِن لَّمْ يَقُمْ بِهِ اَحَدَائِمَ جَمِيعُ النَّاسِ بِتَرْكِهِ لِأَنَّ الْوُجُوبَ عَلَى الْكُلَّ وَلانَّ فِي اشْتِغَالِ الْكُلَّ بِهِ قَطعَ مَادَّةِ الجِهَادِ
مِنَ الْكَرَاعِ وَالسَّلَاحِ فَيَجِبُ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ
ترجمہ اس لئے اگر کسی نے بھی نہیں کیا تو قرض چھوڑنے کے جرم میں سب کے سب گنہگار ہوں گے اور فرض کفایہ ہونے کی ایک دلیل یہ بھی ہے کہ اگر سارے مسلمان ہی جہاد میں مشغول ہو جائیں تو جہاد کا سامان یعنی گھوڑے اور ہتھیار مجاہدین کو کہاں سے ملیں گے۔ وہ سب نا پید ہو جائیں گے۔ اس لئے یہ جہاد فرض کفایہ کے طور پر لازم ہوا۔
تشريح وَلَانَّ فِي اشتغال الكل .. الخ اور جہاد کے فرض کفایہ ہونے کی ایک عقلی دلیل یہ بھی ہے کہ اگر سارے مسلمان ہی عملی طور سے جہاد میں مشغول ہو جائیں تو کوئی بھی ہتھیار بنانے والا نہ ملے گا اور گھوڑوں اور سواری کے لئے ان کی نسل یا دوسرے اسباب نہیں پائے جائیں گے۔ اسی لئے فرض کفایہ ہوا۔ لیکن یہ بات مخفی نہ رہے کہ جو لوگ جہاد کے واسطے ہتھیار بنا ئیں یا گھوڑوں کی نسل بڑھائیں یا زراعت کر کے جہاد کرنے والوں اور ان کے مددگاروں کی غذا اور اس کا انتظام کریں گے وہ سب اس جہاد میں شامل ہوں گے۔ اس کے علاوہ ہر ایک پر فرض عین ہونے سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا ہے کہ شہروں سے سارے شہری ایک ساتھ ہی شرکت کے لئے نکل جائیں۔ بلکہ انتظام کے ساتھ کبھی ایک جماعت جائے اور کبھی دوسری جماعت نکلے۔ اس طرح معاشی حالت بھی متاثر نہیں ہوسکتی ہے۔ پھر یہ پوری تفصیل اس صورت میں ہوگی جب کہ عام طور پر سب کی شرکت کے لئے نہ بلایا گیا ہو۔ مثلاً دشمنوں نے مسلمانوں کے کسی ملک پر اچانک حملہ کر دیا تو وہاں کے ہر شخص پر جہاد فرض عین ہے۔ خواہ پکارنے والا عادل ہو یا فاسق ہو۔ اسی صورت میں اس شہر کے سب لوگوں پر فرض ہوگا کہ وہاں جا کر جہاد میں شریک ہوں۔ اور اگر یہ لوگ دشمن کے مقابلہ کے لئے کافی نہ ہوں تو ان کے قریب کے لوگوں پر بھی فرض ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر وہ بھی کافی نہ ہوں تو ان کے قریب والوں پر فرض ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح یہ حکم پھیلتا اور بڑھتا جائے گا۔ یہاں تک کہ شرق و مغرب کے تمام مسلمانوں پر فرض ہو جائے گا۔ پھر یہ بھی معلوم ہونا چاہئے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے جہاد میں جانے کا ارادہ کیا مگر اس لئے بیٹھ گیا کہ دوسرے لوگ نہیں جا رہے ہیں یا خود سلطان نہیں جا رہا ہے یا اس نے منع کر دیا ہے تو وہ شخص گنہ گار نہ ہوگا۔ خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ جہاد فرض کفایہ ہے۔
The heading: Sin of Abandoning Jihad. Arabic text: 'For if no one performs it, all people are sinful by its abandonment, because the obligation is upon all, and because if all were occupied with it, the means of war (horses and weapons) would be cut off, so it is obligatory on a sufficiency basis (kifayah).' Translation: So if no one does it, all are sinful for leaving the duty, and one proof that it is fard kifayah is that if all Muslims become engaged in jihad, the equipment like horses and weapons would be unavailable to the mujahidin; they would be lost. Therefore, jihad is imposed as fard kifayah. Explanation: The rational proof is that if all Muslims practically engage in jihad, no one would be left to make weapons, breed horses, or provide supplies. So it is fard kifayah. However, note that those who make weapons, breed horses, or manage agriculture to support mujahidin are included in jihad. Also, from the fact that it is not fard 'ayn, it does not necessitate that all citizens leave together; rather, groups go in turns so the economy is not affected. This is when there is no general mobilization. Example: if the enemy suddenly attacks a Muslim land, then jihad becomes fard 'ayn on every person there, regardless of whether the caller is just or sinful. If they are insufficient, then those near them, and so on until all Muslims of East and West become obligated. Also, if someone intends to go but stays because others are not going or the sultan is not going or forbids, he is not sinful. Summary: Jihad is fard kifayah.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage continues with two points. First, it restates that if no one performs jihad, all are sinful. This is because the obligation is on everyone initially. Second, it provides a rational proof for why jihad is fard kifayah rather than fard 'ayn: if all Muslims were to directly engage in combat, there would be no one left to produce weapons, raise horses, or provide logistical support. Therefore, it is necessary that only a sufficient number engage directly, while others support. The passage then gives an important exception: when the enemy attacks unexpectedly, jihad becomes fard 'ayn on the inhabitants of that land and those nearby until it spreads to all Muslims. However, if a person intends to go but is prevented because others are not going or the sultan forbids, he is not sinful. The overall ruling remains that jihad is fard kifayah in normal circumstances.

Key Terms
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): Communal obligation; if some perform it, the obligation falls from others.
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): Individual obligation; each person must perform it.
كراع (karā'): Military equipment, especially horses and beasts of burden.
سلاح (silāḥ): Weapons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the rational proof given in the passage for jihad being fard kifayah?
A) The Quran commands it as fard kifayah.
B) If all Muslims fight, the production of weapons and horses would cease.
C) The Prophet said that jihad is only for a few.
D) The consensus of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
Jihad is fard kifayah to preserve resources; but it becomes fard 'ayn when the enemy attacks a Muslim land directly.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
beginner
6 min
Jihad Becomes Fard 'Ayn During General Mobilization
States exception when jihad becomes fard 'ayn during general conscription

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which jihad becomes fard 'ayn and explain the Quranic proof and rationale for this ruling.

Core Idea
When the imam calls for general mobilization, jihad becomes fard 'ayn on every capable Muslim.

In the normal course, jihad is a fard kifayah—an obligation on the community as a whole. But this lesson introduces a critical exception: when the Muslim ruler declares a general mobilization (nafir 'am), the obligation becomes individual (fard 'ayn). The passage draws on the Quranic verse 'Go forth, whether light or heavy' and the authority of Imam Muhammad in Al-Jami' al-Saghir. Understanding this shift is essential for grasping the Hanafi legal framework on collective vs. individual obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling and the exception
Note that the default ruling for jihad is fard kifayah. The passage begins with 'except when' indicating an exception: general mobilization makes it fard 'ayn.
Default: fard kifayah. Exception: general mobilization.
2
Locate the Quranic proof and analyze its implication
The proof is Quran 9:41: 'Go forth, whether light or heavy.' The imperative 'infiru' indicates obligation, and 'khifafan wa thiqalan' emphasizes that all should go, supporting individual obligation.
The verse is used to prove wujub (obligation) on all.
3
Interpret Imam Muhammad's statement from Al-Jami' al-Saghir
Imam Muhammad says jihad is wajib but Muslims have leeway until needed. The author interprets this: the first part refers to fard kifayah, the latter part to general mobilization.
This reconciles the default and the exception.
4
Understand the rationale
When the purpose (repelling the enemy) cannot be achieved without everyone's participation, the obligation becomes individual.
Rationale: necessity makes it 'ayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تفسیر عام کے وقت جہاد کا حکم
إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ النَّفِيرُ عَامًا فَح يَصِيرُ مِنْ فُرُوضِ الْأَعْيَانِ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى انْفِرُوْا خِفَا فَاوَّثِقَا لَا الْآيَةَ وَقَالَ فِي الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ الْجِهَادُ وَاجِبٌ إِلَّااَنَّ الْمُسْلِمِينَ فِي سَعَةٍ حَتَّى يُحْتَاجَ إِلَيْهِمْ فَأَوَّلُ هَذَا الْكَلَامِ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى الْوُجُوبِ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ وَاخِرُهُ إِلَى النَّفِيرِ الْعَامِ وهذا لأنَّ المَقْصُودَ عِندَ ذَالِكَ لَا يَتَحَصْلُ إِلَّا بِإِقَامَةِ الْكُلِّ فَيَفْتَرِضُ عَلَى الْكُلَّ
ترجمہ البتہ اگر عام طور پر لوگوں کو امیر کی طرف سے بلایا جائے تو اس وقت جہاد فرض عین ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے انشروا خفافًا و ثقالا یعنی تم لوگ خواہ ہلکے ہو یا بھاری نکل جاؤ اور روانہ ہو جاؤ ۔ ( یعنی سوار ہو یا پیدل ہو ۔ خواہ فقیر ہو یا دولت مند ہو ) الحاصل جب عام طور پر سب کی پکار ہو تو بالا جماع فرض عین ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور اس میں بیمار و بوڑھے بھی جائیں ۔ تا کہ تعداد کی زیادتی سے دشمن پر خوف طاری ہو جائے ) اور امام محمد نے کہا ہے جامع صغیر میں کہ جہاد واجب (لازم) ہے۔ البتہ مسلمانوں کو گنجائش ہے یہاں تک کہ ان کی ضرورت پیش آئے۔ اس کلام کے پہلے حصے میں اس بات کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ جہاد فرض کفایہ ہے۔ اور آخری جملہ
Heading: Ruling when general mobilization occurs. Arabic text: 'Except when the mobilization is general, then it becomes from the individual obligations due to His statement: 'Go forth, whether light or heavy...' And it is said in Al-Jami' al-Saghir: Jihad is wajib, but Muslims have leeway until they are needed. The first part of this statement indicates obligation on a sufficiency basis, and the latter part refers to general mobilization. This is because the purpose at that time cannot be achieved except by the performance of all, so it becomes obligatory on all.' Translation: If the leader calls people generally, then jihad becomes fard 'ayn because Allah said: 'Go forth, whether light or heavy' meaning whether on foot or mounted, rich or poor. So when there is a general call, it becomes fard 'ayn by consensus. Even the sick and elderly should go to increase numbers to frighten the enemy. Imam Muhammad said in Al-Jami' al-Saghir: Jihad is wajib, but Muslims have leeway until they are needed. The first part of this statement indicates fard kifayah, and the last part indicates general mobilization.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage addresses an exception to the general rule of fard kifayah. When the ruler (imam) calls for a general mobilization (nafir 'am), jihad becomes fard 'ayn on every capable Muslim, including the sick and elderly (to boost numbers). The proof is the Quranic verse 'Go forth, whether light or heavy.' The author then quotes Imam Muhammad from Al-Jami' al-Saghir, who describes jihad as 'wajib' (using the Hanafi term distinct from fard), but says Muslims have leeway until they are needed. The author interprets this as: the first part ('wajib') refers to fard kifayah, and the last part ('until they are needed') refers to general mobilization. Thus, when needed, the obligation becomes individual. The reason is that the purpose (repelling the enemy) cannot be achieved unless everyone participates.

Key Terms
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): Individual obligation that must be performed by every capable Muslim; omission is sinful without excuse.
النفير العام (al-nafir al-'amm): General mobilization called by the imam when the Muslim community is under threat.
الجامع الصغير (Al-Jami' al-Saghir): The book by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, one of the six sources of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what triggers jihad becoming fard 'ayn?
A) When the enemy attacks any Muslim land.
B) When the ruler issues a general call for mobilization.
C) When all other Muslims refuse to fight.
D) When the mosque announces it.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, jihad becomes fard 'ayn only when the imam declares a general mobilization; otherwise it remains fard kifayah.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules

Jihad as Fard Kifayah: The Rational Proof
Explaining that jihad is fard kifayah using rational analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that jihad is fard kifayah, explain the rational proof from Al-Hidayah, and distinguish when jihad becomes fard 'ayn.

Core Idea
Jihad is fard kifayah, not fard 'ayn, to preserve the community's economic and military support system.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes jihad as a collective obligation using both textual and rational proofs. The commentator expands on the rational argument: if everyone fought, no one would make weapons or grow food. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling being proven
The core claim is that jihad is fard kifayah (obligation of sufficiency). Note that this means if enough people fulfill it, the rest are absolved; otherwise all are sinful.
2
Locate the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The proof: if all Muslims went to jihad, no one would remain to produce weapons, breed horses, or grow food. This would cause the collapse of the support system necessary for jihad itself.
3
Understand the logical chain
Because the support roles are essential, the obligation cannot be individual (fard 'ayn) but must be communal so that some people stay behind to sustain the effort.
4
Note the exception
When the enemy suddenly attacks (invasion) or the ruler issues a general call (nafir 'amm), jihad becomes fard 'ayn on those directly affected and expands outward.
This is the pivot from collective to individual obligation.
5
Apply the Hanafi position
In ordinary circumstances, jihad is fard kifayah. This balances military action with economic stability. The mufta bihi position follows the above reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مِنَ الْكَرَاعِ وَالسَّلَاحِ فَيَجِبُ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ
ترجمہ اس لئے اگر کسی نے بھی نہیں کیا تو قرض چھوڑنے کے جرم میں سب کے سب گنہگار ہوں گے اور فرض کفایہ ہونے کی ایک دلیل یہ بھی ہے کہ اگر سارے مسلمان ہی جہاد میں مشغول ہو جائیں تو جہاد کا سامان یعنی گھوڑے اور ہتھیار مجاہدین کو کہاں سے ملیں گے۔ وہ سب نا پید ہو جائیں گے۔ اس لئے یہ جہاد فرض کفایہ کے طور پر لازم ہوا۔
تشريح وَلَانَّ فِي اشتغال الكل .. الخ اور جہاد کے فرض کفایہ ہونے کی ایک عقلی دلیل یہ بھی ہے کہ اگر سارے مسلمان ہی عملی طور سے جہاد میں مشغول ہو جائیں تو کوئی بھی ہتھیار بنانے والا نہ ملے گا اور گھوڑوں اور سواری کے لئے ان کی نسل یا دوسرے اسباب نہیں پائے جائیں گے۔ اسی لئے فرض کفایہ ہوا۔ لیکن یہ بات مخفی نہ رہے کہ جو لوگ جہاد کے واسطے ہتھیار بنا ئیں یا گھوڑوں کی نسل بڑھائیں یا زراعت کر کے جہاد کرنے والوں اور ان کے مددگاروں کی غذا اور اس کا انتظام کریں گے وہ سب اس جہاد میں شامل ہوں گے۔ اس کے علاوہ ہر ایک پر فرض عین ہونے سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا ہے کہ شہروں سے سارے شہری ایک ساتھ ہی شرکت کے لئے نکل جائیں۔ بلکہ انتظام کے ساتھ کبھی ایک جماعت جائے اور کبھی دوسری جماعت نکلے۔ اس طرح معاشی حالت بھی متاثر نہیں ہوسکتی ہے۔ پھر یہ پوری تفصیل اس صورت میں ہوگی جب کہ عام طور پر سب کی شرکت کے لئے نہ بلایا گیا ہو۔ مثلاً دشمنوں نے مسلمانوں کے کسی ملک پر اچانک حملہ کر دیا تو وہاں کے ہر شخص پر جہاد فرض عین ہے۔ خواہ پکارنے والا عادل ہو یا فاسق ہو۔ اسی صورت میں اس شہر کے سب لوگوں پر فرض ہوگا کہ وہاں جا کر جہاد میں شریک ہوں۔ اور اگر یہ لوگ دشمن کے مقابلہ کے لئے کافی نہ ہوں تو ان کے قریب کے لوگوں پر بھی فرض ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر وہ بھی کافی نہ ہوں تو ان کے قریب والوں پر فرض ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح یہ حکم پھیلتا اور بڑھتا جائے گا۔ یہاں تک کہ شرق و مغرب کے تمام مسلمانوں پر فرض ہو جائے گا۔ پھر یہ بھی معلوم ہونا چاہئے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے جہاد میں جانے کا ارادہ کیا مگر اس لئے بیٹھ گیا کہ دوسرے لوگ نہیں جا رہے ہیں یا خود سلطان نہیں جا رہا ہے یا اس نے منع کر دیا ہے تو وہ شخص گنہ گار نہ ہوگا۔ خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ جہاد فرض کفایہ ہے۔
From the horses and weapons, it becomes obligatory as a sufficiency. Translation: Therefore, if no one does it, all are sinful for abandoning it, and one proof of it being fard kifayah is that if all Muslims were to engage in jihad, where would the equipment, i.e., horses and weapons, come from? They would all disappear. Hence, jihad is obligated as fard kifayah. Explanation: "And because if all engage... etc." Another rational proof that jihad is fard kifayah is that if all Muslims were practically engaged in jihad, no one would be left to make weapons, and for horses and mounts, their breeding or other means would not be found. Therefore, it became fard kifayah. But it should not remain hidden that those who make weapons for jihad, or breed horses, or cultivate to provide food and manage provisions for the fighters and their helpers, all of them are included in this jihad. Moreover, if it were fard 'ayn on everyone, it would not necessitate that all city dwellers leave together for participation. Rather, with management, one group goes and another group goes; in this way, the economic condition cannot be affected. This entire detail applies when there is no general call for everyone's participation. For example, if enemies suddenly attack a Muslim country, then jihad becomes fard 'ayn on every person there, whether the caller is just or sinful. In that case, it becomes obligatory on all the people of that city to go and partake in jihad. If they are insufficient to face the enemy, then it becomes obligatory on those near them. If they too are insufficient, it becomes obligatory on those near them. Thus, this ruling spreads and expands until it becomes obligatory on all Muslims of East and West. Also, it should be known that if a person intended to go for jihad but sat down because others are not going, or the sultan himself is not going, or he prohibited, then that person is not sinful. In summary, jihad is fard kifayah.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining that jihad is an obligation of sufficiency (fard kifayah). The Arabic matn quotes from Al-Hidayah: 'From the horses and weapons, it becomes obligatory as a sufficiency.' The commentator first provides a rational proof: if all Muslims were to engage in jihad actively, there would be no one left to manufacture weapons, breed horses, or produce food. Thus, for the community to sustain itself, it is necessary that only a sufficient number go for jihad, making it fard kifayah. The commentary then clarifies that those who support jihad through making weapons, breeding horses, or agriculture are also included in the reward. It further explains that this ruling of fard kifayah applies when there is no general mobilization. If the enemy suddenly attacks, jihad becomes fard 'ayn on the residents of that area, expanding outward as needed. Finally, it notes that if a person intends to go but refrains because others are not going or the ruler is not going, he is not sinful, as the obligation is upon the community collectively.

Key Terms
جهاد (jihād): I.e., qital (fighting) against disbelievers to elevate the word of Allah.
فرض كفاية (farḍ kifāyah): An obligation that, if performed by a sufficient number, absolves the rest; otherwise all are sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which circumstance does jihad become fard 'ayn in the Hanafi school?
A) When the ruler issues a general call for mobilization
B) When a person has a slave or wife
C) When the enemy is peaceful
D) When there is enough equipment

Key Takeaway
Jihad is fard kifayah to balance military effort with economic sustainability, becoming fard 'ayn only when the enemy directly attacks or the ruler calls for general mobilization.

Offensive Jihad Is Wajib Even Without Aggression
Ruling with proof on offensive jihad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that fighting disbelievers is wajib even if they do not initiate aggression and explain the basis in general Quranic and hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Jihad is obligatory even without enemy aggression; the general command is unconditional.

This passage from Al-Hidayah states a key Hanafi position: fighting disbelievers (qital al-kuffar) is wajib (obligatory) even if they do not take the initiative. This is derived from general proof texts (al-‘umūmāt) — Quranic verses and hadiths that command jihad to elevate Allah's word and remove disbelief. The obligation is a collective duty (fard kifayah) when the Muslim community has the capability under a legitimate ruler.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'fighting the disbelievers' (qitāl al-kuffār). The ruling is 'wajib' (obligatory).
Note the term qital — this is armed combat, not merely preaching.
2
Identify the hukm level
The text explicitly says 'wājib'. In Hanafi usul, wajib is a binding obligation, but the proofs behind it may make it fard kifayah (collective duty).
Wajib is between fard and sunnah in Hanafi typology.
3
Locate the dalil
The passage states the ruling is 'due to the general proofs' (lil-‘umūmāt). These refer to general Quranic verses (e.g., 2:193) and hadiths commanding jihad.
The proof is not quoted but gestured to as known to the reader.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The general commands are unconditional — they do not specify defensive or offensive. Therefore, they cover both scenarios.
This is the core argument: 'amm implies obligation in all instances unless specific takhsis exists.
5
Note the madhhab context
The Hanafi school holds this ruling, but many scholars consider it fard kifayah (collective), not individual. It applies under a legitimate ruler with capability.
Understanding fard kifayah vs. fard ‘ayn is crucial for correct application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقِتَالُ الْكُفَّارِ وَاجِبُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَدْعُوا لِلْعُمُومَاتِ
ترجمہ اور کافروں سے قتال کرنا واجب ہے اگر چہ وہ پیش قدمی نہ کریں کیونکہ اس بارے میں آیات و احادیث عام ہیں۔ یعنی احادیث و آیات سے یہ حکم نکلتا ہے کہ کافروں سے جہاد کرو تا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا کلمہ بلند ہو۔ اور عدل قائم ہو اور فساد و کفر وظلم دور ہو۔ خواہ یہ كفار پیش قدمی کریں یا نہ کریں۔
And fighting the disbelievers is obligatory even if they do not call (initiate), due to the general proofs. Translation: And fighting the disbelievers is wajib even if they do not take the initiative, because the verses and hadiths on this are general. That is, from the hadiths and verses, this ruling is derived: fight the disbelievers so that the word of Allah is exalted, justice is established, and corruption, disbelief, and oppression are removed, whether these disbelievers take the initiative or not.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a concise ruling with proof stating that offensive jihad against disbelievers is obligatory (wajib) even if they do not attack first. The Arabic matn from Al-Hidayah says: 'Fighting the disbelievers is wajib even if they do not call (initiate), due to the general proofs.' The commentary explains that this is based on general Quranic verses and hadiths commanding jihad to elevate Allah's word and remove disbelief. The obligation is not contingent on enemy aggression; it is an ongoing duty to spread justice.

Key Terms
قتال (qitāl): Fighting, specifically against disbelievers in jihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only if Muslims are strong

Key Takeaway
Offensive jihad is wajib in the Hanafi school based on general Quranic and hadith commands, though it is a collective obligation (fard kifayah) under a legitimate ruler with capability.

Exemptions from Jihad: Who Is Not Obligated
Listing individuals exempt from the obligation of jihad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the categories of people exempt from the obligation of jihad and explain the reason for each exemption.

Core Idea
Jihad is a collective duty, but prior duties or incapacity excuse specific individuals.

Jihad is a collective obligation (fard kifayah) upon the Muslim community, but not everyone is required to participate. Islamic law recognizes that certain individuals have overriding duties or physical limitations that exempt them from this obligation. In this lesson, we examine the classical Hanafi rulings on who is exempt and under what conditions they may still volunteer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exempt categories
Read the matn and list the six categories: child, slave, woman, blind, bedridden, amputee.
The Arabic states: 'ṣabiyy, ‘abd, imra’ah, a‘mā, muq‘ad, aqṭa‘.'
2
Understand the reason for each exemption
For each category, note the reason: children are objects of mercy; slaves and women have prior rights (master/husband); the disabled are physically incapable.
The commentary explains: 'ḥaqq al-mawlā wa al-zawj' and 'ajz'.
3
Note the conditional exception
If the master or husband gives permission, jihad becomes fard kifayah on the slave or woman. This shows the exemption is not absolute.
The permission transforms the ruling.
4
Recognize additional exemptions from commentary
The commentary adds debtors (with immediate debt need creditor permission), guarantors, and a scholar who is the sole fatwa authority in the region.
These are based on the principle of overriding duties.
5
Apply the rule
Given a scenario, determine if a person is exempt based on the categories and conditions.
Practice with the tasks below.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجِبُ الْجِهَادُ عَلَى الصَّبِيِّ لِأَنَّ الصَّبِيَّ مَحَلُّ الْمَرْحَمَةِ وَلَا عَبْدٍ وَلَا امْرَأَةٍ لِتَقَدُّمِ حَقِّ الْمَوْلَى وَالزَّوْجِ وَلَا أَعْمَى وَلَا مُقْعَدِ وَلَا أَقْطَعَ لِعَجْزِهِمْ
ترجمہ اور بچہ پر جہاد کرنا واجب نہیں ہوتا ہے کیونکہ وہ محل رحمت ہوتے ہیں۔ اسی طرح غلام اور عورت پر بھی واجب نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ غلام پر اس کے مولی کا حق اور عورت ( بیوی ) پر اس کے شوہر کا حق مقدم ہوتا ہے۔ اور اندھے ولنگڑے اور پاؤں کٹے ہوئے پر بھی واجب نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ لوگ عاجز اور مجبور ہوتے ہیں۔
تشريح وَلَا عَبْدٍ وَلَا امْرَأَةَ الخ۔ مجبور لوگوں پر اولاً جہاد فرض نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے غلام پر اس بناء پر فرض نہیں ہوتا ہے کہ اس کے مولی کا حق اس پر مقدم ہوتا ہے۔ اس سے اسے فرصت نہیں مل سکتی ہے۔ اسی طرح بیوی پر اس کے شوہر کی خدمت کا حق مقدم ہوتا ہے اس لئے یہ بھی معذور کبھی جاتی ہے۔ البتہ اگر مولی نے اپنے غلام کو یا شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کو جہاد میں جانے کی اجازت دیدی ہو تو ان پر بھی فرض کفایہ ہونا چاہئے۔ اسی طرح قرض خواہ کی اجازت کے بغیر قرض دار پر واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر قرض دار کی اجازت سے کوئی قرض کا لفیل ہو جائے خواہ وہ مال کا کفیل ہو یا جان کا کفیل ہو تو اس سے بھی اجازت لینی شرط ہے۔ یہ حکم اس صورت میں ہے جب کہ قرض فی الحال ادا کرنے کی بات ہوئی ہو۔ اور اگر میعادی ہو تو اس کی اجازت کے بغیر بھی جانا صحیح ہے بشرطیکہ اس بات کا یقین ہو کہ اس وقت کے آنے سے پہلے اس کی واپسی ہو جائے گی۔ (الذخیرہ)
اور ایسے عالم پر بھی جہاد میں جانا فرض نہیں ہے جس سے کوئی بڑا عالم اس علاقہ میں نہ ہو ( کہ مسائل اور فتاوی شرعیہ کا صحیح جواب دے سکے )۔ (السراجيد)
And jihad is not obligatory on the child because the child is a place of mercy; nor on a slave nor a woman due to the precedence of the right of the master and the husband; nor on the blind, nor the bedridden, nor the amputee due to their incapacity. Translation: And jihad is not wajib on the child because they are objects of mercy. Similarly, not on the slave and woman because the right of the master and husband takes precedence. And not on the blind, lame, and amputee because they are incapable. Explanation: "Nor on a slave nor a woman etc." First, jihad is not obligatory on incapacitated people. Therefore, it is not obligatory on a slave because the right of his master takes precedence over him, so he does not have leisure. Similarly, the right of serving her husband takes precedence over the wife, so she is also considered excused. However, if the master permits his slave or the husband permits his wife to go for jihad, then it should be fard kifayah on them as well. Similarly, it is not wajib on a debtor without the permission of the creditor. And if a person becomes a guarantor (kafil) for a debt with the permission of the debtor, whether guarantee for property or life, then permission is also required from him. This ruling applies when the debt is due immediately. If it is a time-bound debt, then going without his permission is valid on condition that it is certain he will return before the due date. (Al-Dhakhirah) And also, it is not obligatory for a scholar to go for jihad if there is no other major scholar in that region (who can correctly answer issues and give legal rulings). (Al-Sirajiyya)
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement listing categories of people who are exempt from the obligation of jihad. The Arabic matn from Al-Hidayah specifies: children (because they are objects of mercy), slaves and women (because their masters/husbands have prior rights), and the blind, bedridden, and amputees (due to incapacity). The commentary expands: exemption is because these individuals have overriding duties (like serving the husband) or lack physical ability. However, if the master or husband gives permission, then jihad becomes fard kifayah on them. The commentary also adds debtors: they cannot go without the creditor's permission if the debt is immediately due; if time-bound, they can go if certain to return before the deadline. Additionally, a scholar who is the sole authority for fatwa in a region is exempt, as his remaining is necessary for the community.

Key Terms
صبي (ṣabiyy): A minor who has not reached puberty.
عبد (‘abd): A slave who is owned by a master.
امرأة (imra’ah): A married woman or generally a woman (as wife).
أعمى (a‘mā): A blind person.
مقعد (muq‘ad): A person bedridden or unable to walk.
اقطع (aqṭa‘): A person with an amputated limb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If they are wealthy
B) If their master or husband gives permission
C) If the enemy attacks their city
D) Never, they are always exempt

Key Takeaway
Jihad is a collective duty, but individuals with prior obligations or physical incapacity are exempt, though they may participate if permitted.

Jihad Becomes Fard Ayn When Enemy Attacks
Ruling on jihad becoming fard ayn with women and slaves permitted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when jihad becomes fard ayn and explain why women and slaves may participate without permission.

Core Idea
When enemy attacks, jihad becomes fard ayn, overriding even the rights of husband and master.

This lesson examines a crucial Hanafi ruling on the obligatory nature of defensive jihad. The passage establishes that when an enemy directly attacks a Muslim city, repelling them becomes an individual duty (fard ayn) on every capable person. This elevated obligation temporarily suspends certain personal rights, allowing women to go out without their husband's permission and slaves without their master's permission. The reasoning is based on qiyas (analogy) with other fard ayn acts like prayer and fasting, where such permissions are also irrelevant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering condition
Find the event that transforms jihad from a collective duty (fard kifayah) to an individual duty (fard ayn). The passage states: 'If the enemy attacks a city' (فَإِنْ هَجَمَ الْعَدُوُّ عَلَى بَلَدٍ).
This is a direct attack, not a distant expedition.
2
State the ruling for all people
The passage says 'repelling them becomes obligatory upon all people' (وَجَبَ عَلَى جَمِيعِ النَّاسِ الدَّفْعُ). This means every capable Muslim must participate.
This overrides normal exemptions.
3
Identify the exception to normal permissions
Normally, a woman needs husband's permission to leave home, and a slave needs master's permission. Here, they may go without permission because it is fard ayn.
The ruling explicitly mentions both.
4
Trace the qiyas (analogy)
The author compares this to prayer and fasting, which are also fard ayn. In those acts, women and slaves do not need permission. The 'illa (effective cause) is that the act is fard ayn.
Qiyas jaliy: clear analogy based on the shared attribute of being fard ayn.
5
Distinguish from before the general levy
Before the call to arms (nafir), women and slaves cannot go without permission because there are enough free men. Only when necessity demands (enemy attack) does the right become universal.
This is a limitation on the exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ هَجَمَ الْعَدُوُّ عَلَى بَلَدٍ وَجَبَ عَلَى جَمِيعِ النَّاسِ الدَّفْعُ، تَخْرُجُ الْمَرْأَةُ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِ زَوْجِهَا وَالْعَبْدُ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِ الْمَوْلَى، لِأَنَّهُ صَارَ فَرْضَ عَيْنٍ، وَمِلْكُ الْيَمِينِ وَرِقُ النِّكَاحِ لَا يَظْهَرُ فِي حَقِّ فُرُوضِ الْأَعْيَانِ كَمَا فِي الصَّلَاةِ وَالصَّوْمِ، يُخَالِفُ مَا قَبْلَ النَّفِيرِ، لِأَنَّ بِغَيْرِهِمَا مُقْنِعٌ فَلَا ضَرُورَةَ إِلَى إِبْطَالِ حَقِّ الْمَوْلَى وَالزَّوْجِ.
If the enemy attacks a city, repelling them becomes obligatory upon all people; the woman goes out without her husband's permission, and the slave without the master's permission, because it has become fard ayn. The right of ownership and the restraint of marriage do not appear in the case of fard ayn duties, just as in prayer and fasting. This differs from before the general levy, because without them there is sufficient, so there is no need to nullify the right of the master and husband.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on jihad when the enemy directly attacks a Muslim city. It states that repelling the enemy becomes fard ayn (individual obligation) upon all people. Consequently, the usual restrictions are overridden: a woman may go out without her husband's permission, and a slave without his master's permission. The reasoning is that fard ayn duties like prayer and fasting are not subject to such permissions. Before the general call to arms (nafir), the situation is different because the Muslims are sufficient without women and slaves, so the rights of husband and master are preserved. This ruling illustrates the Hanafi principle that collective religious obligations take precedence over personal rights when necessity demands.

Key Terms
فَرْضُ عَيْنٍ (fard 'ayn): An individual obligation binding on every Muslim who meets the conditions; non-performance is a sin.
مِلْكُ الْيَمِينِ (milk al-yamin): Ownership by right hand, meaning the master's right over a slave.
رِقُ النِّكَاحِ (riqq al-nikah): The restraint of marriage, referring to the husband's authority over his wife.
نَفِير (nafir): The general call to arms or general levy for jihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the Imam declares jihad
B) When the enemy attacks a Muslim city
C) When the woman volunteers
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Jihad becomes fard ayn upon enemy attack, nullifying the rights of husband and master over women and slaves for the purpose of defense.

Ruling on Ju'l When Bayt al-Mal Has Wealth
Ruling on the dislike of ju'l when state treasury has funds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ju'l and apply the condition of treasury funding to determine whether it is makruh or permissible.

Core Idea
Ju'l for jihad is makruh when bayt al-mal is funded; permissible when treasury is empty to repel greater harm.

This passage addresses a practical question: can Muslims collect funds to support fighters when the Islamic state already has a treasury? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer, balancing the need for mutual help against unnecessary duplication. The ruling is conditional on the state of the public treasury.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The passage rules on 'al-ju'l' – compensation collected specifically for jihad. The default ruling is makruh (disliked) when the treasury has funds.
The ruling is not absolute; it depends on a condition.
2
Identify the condition that changes the ruling
The condition is the presence or absence of funds in bayt al-mal. If funds exist, ju'l is makruh; if the treasury is empty, ju'l becomes permissible.
The reason given: treasury funds are already allocated for Muslim affairs, so there is no need for extra collection.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The principle is repelling a greater harm (enemy attack) with a lesser harm (financial loss). When treasury is empty, the greater harm of weakness justifies the lesser harm of collecting funds.
This principle is stated explicitly in the passage.
4
Analyze the evidence provided
The passage cites two precedents: the Prophet (saw) took armor from Safwan during Hunayn, and Umar provided horses and organized unmarried men for battle. These show that accepting help is allowed when needed.
These are acts of the Prophet and a Caliph, indicating permissibility not obligation.
5
Synthesize the conditional ruling
Combine: ju'l is makruh (not haram) when treasury is funded, because it resembles wages and lacks necessity. It is permissible (jā'iz) when treasury is empty, as mutual strengthening becomes necessary.
The ruling is not a blanket prohibition but a context-sensitive guideline.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُكْرَهُ الْجُعْلُ مَادَامَ لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ [فِي بَيْتِ الْمَالِ] مَالٌ، لِأَنَّهُ يُشْبِهُ الْأَجْرَ وَلَا ضَرُورَةَ إِلَيْهِ، لِأَنَّ مَالَ بَيْتِ الْمَالِ مُعَدٌّ لِأُمُورِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ، فَإِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ فَلَا بَأْسَ بِأَنْ يُقَوِّيَ بَعْضُهُمْ بَعْضًا، لِأَنَّ فِيهِ دَفْعَ الضَّرَرِ الْأَعْلَى بِالْحَاقِ الْأَدْنَى، يُؤَيِّدُهُ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَخَذَ دُرُوعًا مِنْ صَفْوَانَ، وَعُمَرُ كَانَ يُغْزِي الْأَعْرَبَ عَنْ ذِي الْحَلِيلَةِ وَيُعْطِي الشَّاحِصَ فَرَسًا.
And it is disliked to take compensation as long as the Muslims have wealth in the public treasury, because it resembles wages, and there is no need for it, for the public treasury's wealth is prepared for the affairs of the Muslims. If it is not present, then there is no harm in some of them strengthening others, because in that is repelling the greater harm with the lesser harm. This is supported by the fact that the Prophet (peace be upon him) took armor from Safwan, and Umar used to send unmarried men and give a horse to the one going forth.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi ruling on collecting funds specifically for jihad (ju'l) when the Islamic state treasury (bayt al-mal) is funded. It opens with the ruling: it is disliked (makruh) to collect such funds as long as the treasury has money, because it resembles hiring for wages and there is no necessity. The treasury is meant for such needs. However, if the treasury is empty, then it is permissible for Muslims to help each other financially for jihad, because this involves repelling a greater harm (the enemy) by accepting a lesser harm (financial loss). The passage supports this with a Prophetic precedent: the Prophet (saw) took armor from Safwan during the Hunayn expedition, and Umar used to send unmarried men to fight and would provide horses to those going to battle. The Hanafi school thus balances the principle of avoiding unnecessary collection with the permissible cooperation when needed.

Key Terms
الْجُعْل (al-ju'l): Compensation or reward given for performing jihad, specifically here referring to funds collected from people to support fighters.
بَيْتُ الْمَالِ (bayt al-mal): The public treasury of the Islamic state, managed by the ruler for the welfare of Muslims.
الْحَاقُ الْأَدْنَى (al-haq al-adna): The lesser harm, which is accepted to repel a greater harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, when is it disliked (makruh) to collect funds specifically for jihad?
A) When the enemy attacks
B) When the public treasury (bayt al-mal) has sufficient funds
C) When the fighters volunteer
D) Always

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on ju'l is conditional: it is disliked when the Islamic treasury has funds, but permissible when the treasury is empty, based on the principle of repelling greater harm.

Calling Enemies to Islam Before Fighting
Ruling that besieged enemies must be invited to Islam before combat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that besieged enemies must be invited to Islam before combat, and explain the hadith proof that establishes this sunnah.

Core Idea
Jihad begins with da'wah: calling to Islam is a prophetic practice before any attack.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a key rule in the conduct of jihad: Muslims are not to initiate fighting without first inviting the enemy to embrace Islam. This reflects the prophetic sunnah and the ultimate purpose of jihad — to establish the word of Allah, not to shed blood. Understanding this ruling helps distinguish legitimate jihad from mere aggression.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'calling the enemy to Islam before fighting'. According to the Hanafi school, this is a sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
It is not fard or wajib; it is a strongly recommended practice.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas: the Prophet never fought a people until he called them to Islam.
This hadith is a sound (hasan) narration, classified as ahad.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'until he called them' indicates that calling to Islam is a prerequisite to fighting. The Prophet's practice sets the rule.
The command is derived from action (fi'li) rather than verbal command.
4
Note the consequence
If the enemy accepts the call, Muslims refrain from fighting because the objective is achieved. If they refuse, then fighting may proceed.
Jizyah may be offered after refusal, but that is not covered here.
5
Consider the broader principle
The ultimate goal of jihad is to establish tawhid, as shown by the hadith 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say la ilaha illa Allah'.
This reinforces that da'wah is the first step, not immediate warfare.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ كَيْفِيَّةِ الْقِتَالِ. وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ دَارَ الْحَرْبِ فَحَاصَرُوا مَدِينَةً أَوْ حِصْنًا دَعَوْهُمْ إِلَى الْإِسْلَامِ، لِمَا رَوَى ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَا قَاتَلَ قَوْمًا حَتَّى دَعَاهُمْ إِلَى الْإِسْلَامِ. فَإِنْ أَجَابُوا كَفُّوا عَنْ قِتَالِهِمْ لِحُصُولِ الْمَقْصُودِ، وَقَدْ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: أُمِرْتُ أَنْ أُقَاتِلَ النَّاسَ حَتَّى يَقُولُوا لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ.
Chapter on the manner of fighting. When Muslims enter the abode of war and besiege a city or fort, they call them to Islam, due to what Ibn Abbas narrated: that the Prophet (peace be upon him) never fought a people until he called them to Islam. So if they respond, they (the Muslims) refrain from fighting them, because the objective is achieved. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say 'La ilaha illa Allah'.'
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on the manner of fighting (qital) in jihad. The Hanafi ruling is clear: before initiating combat, Muslims must invite the enemy to embrace Islam. This is based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet never fought any people without first calling them to Islam. If they accept the call, fighting ceases because the objective of jihad (establishing Islam or submission) is attained. The passage also quotes the famous hadith: 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say la ilaha illa Allah,' which sets the ultimate purpose. The Hanafi school emphasizes this da'wah as a necessary step in jihad, reflecting the prophetic sunnah.

Key Terms
دَارُ الْحَرْبِ (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule not in treaty with Muslims; land of war.
حِصْن (hisn): Fortress or fortified place.
دَعْوَةُ الْإِسْلَامِ (da'wat al-islam): Invitation to embrace Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must Muslims do before attacking a besieged city in dar al-harb?
A) Immediately attack
B) Call the inhabitants to Islam first
C) Demand jizyah only
D) Wait for reinforcements

Key Takeaway
Calling enemies to Islam before fighting is an emphasized sunnah established by the Prophet's practice, underscoring the primacy of da'wah in jihad.
