Taking Contributions for Jihad When Treasury is Empty
Explains ruling on taking donations for jihad with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking contributions for jihad when the treasury is empty, identify the supporting hadith proofs, and explain the condition that changes the ruling.

Core Idea
When the treasury is empty, it is permissible to take contributions from the community for jihad.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on funding jihad from private contributions. While the default is to use public treasury, necessity opens the door for community support. We will explore the hadith evidence that establishes this permissibility and the ethical considerations involved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Taking contributions (ja'l) from people for jihad. What is the hukm? Permissible (mubah) when treasury is empty.
The default is not to take if treasury has funds.
2
Locate the dalil
What evidence does the author cite? Hadith of Prophet (peace be upon him) taking weapons from Safwan at Hunayn, and hadith of reward for those who assist mujahideen.
Also practice of Umar (radi allahu anhu).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? The Prophet's action shows permissibility; the reward hadith encourages assistance, implying it is allowed and meritorious.
The principle of preventing greater harm (kafir domination) justifies taking wealth.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement? Yes, other schools may require treasury only. The Hanafi school allows community funding when needed.
The text cites Ibn al-Humam for the relied-upon position.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The Hanafi position is mufta bihi, supported by Prophetic practice and necessity.
Ibn al-Humam affirms that the imam should command mutual help.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۵
كتاب السير
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہفتم لئے ہے کہ مسلمانوں کے حوادث میں کام آئے ۔ البتہ اگر بیت المال میں جمع کچھ نہ ہو تو لینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ تا کہ ایک دوسرے کی مدد کر کے دین کو مضبوط کریں۔ کیونکہ ایسا کرنے میں تھوڑا سا نقصان برداشت کر کے بڑے نقصان یعنی کافروں کے نقصان کو دور کرنا ہوتا ہے۔ جس کی تائید اس واقعہ سے ہوتی ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جنگ حنین میں صفوان سے چند زر ہیں لی تھیں ۔ اس کی روایت ابو داؤد، النسائی اور احمد نے کی ہے۔ اسی طرح حضرت عمر رضی اللہ عنہ بیوی والے مردوں کی طرف سے ان مردوں کو بھیج دیتے جن کی بیویاں نہ ہوتیں ۔ اور جو شخص جہاد میں جانے کے قابل نہ ہوتا اس کا گھوڑا جہاد میں جانے والے کو دے دیتے ۔ تشریح جہاد کے لئے اس صورت میں جب کہ بیت المال میں مال موجود ہو دوسروں سے مال نہیں لینا چاہئے ۔ البتہ اگر ضرورت پیش آ جائے تو ایک کو دوسرے کی مدد کرنی چاہئے ۔ چنانچہ حضرت عبد اللہ بن عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ سے مروی حدیث میں ہے کہ رسول اللہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ جہاد کرنے والے کے لئے اپنا ثواب ہے۔ اور مال سے اس کی مدد کرنے والوں کو اپنے مال اور اس مجاہد دونوں کا ثواب ہے۔ رواہ ابو داؤد ۔ یہاں جعل سے مراد یہ ہے کہ غازیوں کے لئے لوگوں سے مال لینا۔ تا کہ ان کو قدرت حاصل ہو۔ اور شیخ ابن الہمام نے کہا ہے کہ امام مسلمین لوگوں کو حکم کرے کہ وہ ایک دوسرے کی سامان سفر گھوڑے اور ہتھیار نے مدد کریں۔ تحقیق يُغر افزاء سے کہا جاتا ہے اُغْرَى الأمير الجيش - امیر نے لشکر کو مقابلہ کے لئے بھیجا۔ اعزب و شخص جس کی ۔ نے بیوی نہ ہو ۔ حلیله : مرد کی بیوی الشاخص اسم فاعل ایک جگہ سے دوسری جگہ بلندی میں جانا یہاں دشمن کی طرف جانے والا مراد ہے۔ انوار الحق قاسمی
Detailed explanation: For jihad, when wealth is present in the treasury, one should not take from others. But if need arises, one should help another. Thus, in the hadith narrated from Abdullah ibn Umar, the Messenger of Allah said: 'For the one who performs jihad is his reward, and for those who assist him with their wealth is the reward of both his wealth and the mujahid.' Reported by Abu Dawud. Here, 'ja'l' means taking wealth from people for the mujahideen so that they may have capability. And Shaykh Ibn al-Humam said that the Muslim imam should command people to help one another with provisions, horses, and weapons.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sunnah. It addresses the issue of funding jihad when the state treasury (bayt al-mal) lacks resources. The default ruling is that jihad should be funded from the public treasury. However, if the treasury is empty, it becomes permissible to solicit contributions from the Muslim community. This is supported by the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) taking weapons from Safwan during the battle of Hunayn, and the general principle that preventing a greater harm (the dominance of disbelief) justifies a smaller loss (giving wealth). The commentary also cites the practice of Umar radi allahu anhu of sending unmarried men and lending horses. It emphasizes that those who assist mujahideen share in their reward, as narrated by Abu Dawud. The author also quotes Ibn al-Humam saying the imam should organize mutual assistance among Muslims.

Key Terms
جعل (ja'l): In this text, it refers to wealth taken from people to support the mujahideen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is it permissible to take contributions from people for jihad?
A) Always, irrespective of the treasury's condition
B) Only when the bayt al-mal is empty and there is a need
C) Only with the permission of the ruler
D) Never, as jihad must be funded solely by the state

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of taking contributions for jihad depends on the state of the treasury; when empty, it is permissible and recommended.

The Obligatory Sequence: Call to Islam Before Fighting
Ruling on the sequence of calls during siege with proof from Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sequence of calls during siege and explain the proof from the hadith of Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Fighting is not permitted until the enemy has been called to Islam and then to jizya.

This lesson covers a key ruling in Hanafi siyar (law of war): before engaging in battle, the imam must follow a specific sequence of invitations. Based on the explicit practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him), the Hanafi school holds that calling the enemy to Islam is an obligation (wajib), not merely recommended. Understanding this sequence is essential for ensuring that military action is legally justified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the imam's duty to call the enemy to Islam before initiating hostilities. According to the text, this call is obligatory (wajib).
The ruling is derived from the hadith's negation: 'He never fought until he called them.'
2
Locate the primary proof
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) never fought a people until he called them to Islam.' This is also supported by the hadith 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say La ilaha illa Allah...'
The hadith is narrated by Abd al-Razzaq and al-Hakim, and is considered hasan.
3
Analyze the legal indication (wajh al-dalalah)
In Hanafi usul, a negation of an action until a condition is met implies that the condition is a prerequisite. Since fighting is negated until the call, the call is obligatory before fighting.
This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that al-amr (command) indicates obligation, and here the negation of fighting indicates the obligation of the call.
4
Apply the next step: jizya offer
If the enemy refuses Islam, the next obligatory step is to call them to pay jizya. However, this only applies to those from whom jizya is accepted (ahl al-kitab and non-Arab idol worshippers). Apostates and Arab idol worshippers are not offered jizya; they must accept Islam or face fighting.
The Quranic verse 'they fight you until they submit or become Muslim' (Surah Al-Fath: 16) is cited to support the exclusion for Arab idol worshippers.
5
Note the consequence of jizya acceptance
If jizya is paid, the dhimmis gain the same rights and protections as Muslims regarding life and property, based on the saying of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him).
This establishes the legal status of dhimmis in Islamic law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بابُ كَيْفِيَّةِ الْقِتَالِ
ترجمہ: قتال کی کیفیت کے بیان میں
مسلمان دار الحرب سے کسی شہر یا قلعہ کا محاصرہ کر لیں تو دعوت اسلام دیں محصورین کے قبول کر لینے پر قتال ترک کردیں
وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ دَارَ الحَرْبِ فَحَاصَرُوا مَدِينَةً أَوْ حِصْنًا دَعَوْهُمْ إِلَى الْإِسْلَامِ لِمَا رَوَى ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَا قَاتَلَ قَوْمًا حَتَّى دَعَاهُمْ إِلَى الْإِسْلَامِ
ترجمہ: جب مسلمان دار الحرب میں جا کر کسی شہر یا کسی قلعہ کا محاصرہ گھراؤ کر لیں تو سب سے پہلے ان کافروں کو اسلام کی طرف بلائیں اور دعوت دیں۔ کیونکہ حضرت ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہ سے روایت ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کسی قوم کو بھی جب تک کہ اسلام کی طرف دعوت نہیں دی اس وقت تک ان سے جہاد اور قتال نہیں کیا۔ اس کی روایت عبد الرزاق اور حاکم نے سند صحیح سے کی ہے۔ دعوت اسلام قبول کرنے پر قتال ترک کردیں
فَإِنْ أَجَابُوا كَفُّوا عَنْ قِتَالِهِمْ لِحُصُولِ الْمَقْصُودِ وَقَدْ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: أُمِرْتُ أَنْ أُفَاتِلَ النَّاسَ حَتَّى يَقُولُوا لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ... (البخاری ومسلم)
دوسرے مرحلہ پر جزیہ کا مطالبہ كريں
وَإِن امْتَنَعُوا دَعَوْهُمْ إِلَى أَدَاءِ الْجِزْيَةِ بِهِ أَمَرَ رَسُولُ اللهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أُمَرَاءَ الْجُيُوشِ وَلِأَنَّهُ أَحَدُ مَا يَنْتَهِي بِهِ الْقِتَالُ عَلَى مَا نَطَقَ بِهِ النَّصُّ وَهَذَا فِي حَقِّ مَنْ يُقْبَلُ مِنْهُ الْجِزْيَةُ وَمَنْ لَا تُقْبَلُ مِنْهُ كَالْمُرْتَدِّينَ وَعَبَدَةِ الْأَوْثَانِ مِنَ الْعَرَبِ لَا فَائِدَةَ فِي دُعَائِهِمْ إِلَى قُبُولِ الْجِزْيَةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُقْبَلُ مِنْهُمْ إِلَّا الْإِسْلَامُ قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: تُقَاتِلُونَهُمْ أَوْ يُسْلِمُونَ
ترجمہ: اور اگر كافروں نے اسلام لانے سے انکار کر دیا تو ان کو جزیہ دینے کے لئے کہا جائے ۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے لشکروں کے سرداروں کو یہی حکم فرمایا۔ اور نص کے مطابق جن چیزوں سے قتال ختم ہوتا ہے ان میں یہ بھی ایک چیز ہے اور یہ حکم ایسے کافروں کے بارے میں ہے جن سے جزیہ قبول کیا جا سکتا ہو ۔ کیونکہ جن لوگوں سے جزیہ قبول نہیں کیا جا سکتا ہو جیسے مرتد ہو جانے والے ۔ اور عرب کے بت پرست لوگ تو ان کو جزیہ قبول کرنے کی دعوت دینا ہی بے فائدہ ہے۔ کیونکہ ان سے اسلام قبول کرنے کے سوا دوسری کوئی چیز مقبول نہیں ہوگی ۔ جیسا کہ فرمان باری تعالی ہے: تُقَاتِلُونَهُمْ أَوْ يُسْلِمُونَ۔
تشریح: قَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى: تُقَاتِلُونَهُمْ أَوْ يُسْلِمُونَ (الفتح) اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ تم ان سے قتال كرو يہاں تک کہ وہ مسلمان ہو جائیں۔ اور حضرت بریدہ کی حدیث میں ہے کہ جب رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کسی لشکر یا نمازیوں کی جماعت پر کسی کو سردار بناتے تو اس کو اپنے ذاتی معاملات میں اللہ تعالیٰ سے تقویٰ رکھنے کی اور اپنے ساتھی مسلمانوں سے بھلائی کرنے کی وصیت فرماتے ۔ پھر کہتے کہ اللہ تعالی کے نام پر جہاد کرو اللہ تعالیٰ کی راہ میں قتال کرو۔ جس نے اللہ تعالیٰ سے كفر کیا تم اس سے جہاد کرو ۔ اور خیانت یا غدر مت کرو اور مقتول کفار کا مثلہ نہ کرو یعنی اس کے ہاتھ پاؤں ناک کان وغیرہ نہ کاٹو اور سی بچہ کو تل نہ کرو اور جب تمہارا مشرک دشمنوں سے مقابلہ ہونے لگے تو تم انہیں پہلے تین باتوں میں سے ایک بات کی طرف دعوت دو الخ۔ یہ حدیث صحیح مسلم وغیرہ میں موجود ہے۔ اور حدیث میں ہے کہ میں جزیرہ عرب سے یہود و نصاری کو نکال دونگا۔ یہاں تک کہ اس میں مسلمانوں کے سوا کسی کو بھی نہیں چھوڑوں گا۔ اس کی روایت مسلم، احمد اور ترمذی رحمۃ اللہ علیہم نے کی ہے۔
جزیہ پر رضامند ہو جائیں تو كيا كيا جائے
فَإِن بَذَلُوهَا فَلَهُمْ مَا لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ وَعَلَيْهِمْ مَا عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ لِقَوْلِ عَلِيٍّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ: إِنَّمَا بَذَلُوا الْجِزْيَةَ لِيَكُونَ دِمَاؤُهُمْ كَدِمَائِنَا وَأَمْوَالُهُمْ كَأَمْوَالِنَا
When Muslims enter the land of war and besiege a city or fortress, they call them to Islam. If they respond, they refrain from fighting. If they refuse, they call them to pay jizya. This is for those from whom jizya is accepted; for apostates and Arab idol worshippers, only Islam is accepted. If they pay jizya, they have the same rights and duties as Muslims, based on Ali's saying that their blood becomes like our blood and their wealth like our wealth.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sunnah regarding the procedure of siege (hukm al-muhasara). The Hanafi school holds that the imam must first invite the enemy to Islam, based on the explicit practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who never fought a people until he invited them. If they accept, fighting is stopped. If they refuse, the next step is to call them to jizya, but only if they belong to a category from which jizya is accepted (ahl al-kitab and non-Arab idol worshippers). Apostates and Arab idol worshippers are not offered jizya; they must either accept Islam or be fought. The passage further states that if jizya is paid, the dhimmi enjoy the same protection of life and property as Muslims, as stated by Ali radi allahu anhu. The commentary explains the hadith of Buraidah about the instructions given to army commanders, including the prohibition of treachery, mutilation, and killing children.

Key Terms
جزیة (jizya): A tax levied on non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) in lieu of military service and as a symbol of submission to Islamic rule.
مرتد (murtad): One who renounces Islam after having accepted it. Jizya is not accepted from them; they must return to Islam or be fought.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the first step Muslims must take when besieging a city in enemy territory?
A) Immediately attack the city
B) Call the inhabitants to Islam
C) Demand jizya
D) Offer a peace treaty

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates calling the enemy to Islam before fighting, based on the Prophet's consistent practice.

Permissibility of Using Siege Weapons and Burning Enemy Property in Jihad
Explains the ruiling on mangonels and burning enemy property with prophetic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using mangonels and burning enemy property, and explain the prophetic evidence from the Banu Nadir incident.

Core Idea
Military necessity permits destroying enemy property; the Prophet's burning date palms sets the precedent.

In the context of jihad, the Hanafi school permits the use of any weapon that achieves victory, including siege engines like mangonels and cannons. But what about burning enemy property? This lesson examines the prophetic precedent from the Banu Nadir campaign and clarifies the limits of destruction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Using mangonels (and by analogy, cannons) and burning enemy date palms. The ruling is permissibility (mubah) for military necessity.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of the Prophet burning and cutting the date palms of Banu Nadir, reported by Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action (fi'l) shows that destroying enemy property to weaken them is permissible. The Hanafi school interprets this as a general permission for military necessity, not limited to trees.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider burning trees as makruh/haram based on hadiths prohibiting destruction. This is a legitimate scholarly difference.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the specific action of the Prophet over general prohibitions against destruction, as military necessity overrides the general rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منجنیق میم کو کسرہ کے ساتھ واحد سے جمع مجانیق ۔ مجانیق منجیقات۔ فلاخن .. ایک بڑا گو پھیا جس سے قلعوں پر پتھر مار کر اسے توڑنے کی کوشش کی جاتی تھی ۔ اور وہی کام اب تو پوں سے لیا جاتا ہے جس کی وجہ سے وہ تقریبا متروک ہو گیا ہے۔ لیکن حدیث سے اس بات کی دلیل ہوتی ہے کہ تو پوں سے حملہ کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔ اور بویرہ کے جلانے کی حدیث یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے یہود اور نبی نضیر کے کھجوروں کے درخت جلوا دئیے اور کٹوا ڈالے تھے ۔ رواہ البخاری ومسلم اس حدیث سے یہ ثابت نہیں ہوتا ہے کہ خود کفار کو بھی جلانا جائز ہے لیکن ان کے فساد دور کرنے کے لئے قتل کرنے کی طرح ان کا جلانا بھی جائز ہے۔
Mangonel: with a kasra on the meem, singular to plural Majaniq, Majaniq, Manjaniqat. Darchin... a large wooden device by which stones are thrown at forts to break them. That same work is now done by cannons, due to which it has become almost obsolete. But the hadith indicates that attacking with cannons is also permissible. And the hadith for burning (al-Buwaira) is that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) burned and cut down the date palms of the Jews of Banu Nadir. Narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. This hadith does not prove that it is permissible to burn the infidels themselves, but to remove their mischief, burning them is also permissible like killing them.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the permissibility of using heavy siege engines (mangonels) and burning enemy property during jihad. The author begins by defining 'manjaniq' as a large device for throwing stones at forts, now replaced by cannons. He cites a hadith of the Prophet burning date palms of Banu Nadir, reported by Bukhari and Muslim, as evidence that such destructive acts are permissible. However, he clarifies that this does not justify burning living persons directly; rather, just as killing is allowed to eliminate their mischief, so is burning when it serves the same purpose. The Hanafi position is that any means that breaks the enemy's strength and leads to victory is permissible, provided it does not involve gratuitous cruelty. The hadith provides a precedent for targeting property (trees) but not for direct burning of persons, hence the distinction.

Key Terms
منجنیق (manjanīq): A large siege engine for throwing stones at forts; in modern context, includes cannons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The consensus of the Companions
B) The Prophet's burning of the date palms of Banu Nadir
C) A verse from the Quran commanding destruction
D) The principle of reciprocity

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits destroying enemy property, including using siege weapons and burning, based on the prophetic precedent at Banu Nadir, as long as it serves military necessity.

Destroying Enemy Property in Jihad: Permissibility and Limits
States ruling on destroying enemy water sources, trees, and crops

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on flooding, cutting trees, and destroying enemy crops during jihad, and identify the condition that renders destruction prohibited.

Core Idea
Destroying enemy resources is permissible to weaken them, but becomes forbidden when victory is imminent.

In the heat of battle, commanders may be tempted to use every means to defeat the enemy. The Hanafi school provides a balanced ruling: actions like flooding, cutting trees, and destroying crops are allowed if they inflict grief and break enemy power, but only as long as victory is not yet assured. Once victory is imminent, the land and its resources become prospective Muslim property, and destruction is no longer lawful. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the critical condition from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Actions and Ruling
List the three actions mentioned: releasing water, cutting trees, and destroying crops. The base ruling is that these are prescribed (mashru') and permissible (mubah) because they serve the purpose of weakening the enemy.
2
Understand the Rationale (Talil)
The legal reasoning is given: these acts cause grief (kabt) and anger (ghayz), break the enemy's power (shawkah), and scatter their assembly. This rationale forms the illa (effective cause) for permissibility.
The term 'ilhaq al-kabt' refers to inflicting mental distress.
3
Note the Qualification for Imminent Victory
The commentary adds a crucial condition: if there is a strong presumption (ghalabah al-zann) that Muslim victory is imminent, then cutting fruit-bearing trees and destroying crops becomes forbidden (haram). Because the land will soon be Muslim property, destruction would waste community assets.
This shows the Hanafi consideration of future benefit (maslahah).
4
Recognize the Hanafi Balance
The ruling balances military necessity with preservation of resources. Destruction is permissible when the enemy is strong, but not when victory is near. This reflects the Hanafi principle that actions are judged by their outcomes and purposes.
Compare with other schools that may have stricter limits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پانی چھوڑنے ، درخت کاٹنے اور کھیتی اجاڑنے کا حکم
قَالَ وَأَرْسَلُوا عَلَيْهِمُ المَاءَ وَقَطَعُوا أَشْجَارَهُمْ وَأَفْسَدُوا رُرُوعَهُمْ لِأَنَّ فِي جَمِيعِ ذَالِكَ إِلْحَاقَ الْكَبْتِ وَالْغَيْظِ بِهِمْ وَكَسْرَ شَوْكَتِهِمْ وَتَفْرِيْقَ جَعِهِمْ فَيَكُونُ مَشْرُوعًا
ترجمہ اور قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ اور کافروں اور دشمنوں پر پانی کا سیلاب رواں کر دیں یعنی اگر موقع ملے تو ان کو پانی میں ڈبو دیں۔ اور ان کے درخت کاٹ دیں۔ اور ان کی کھیتیاں خراب کر دیں کیونکہ ان تمام کاموں سے کافروں کی ذلت اور ان کی بربادی اور ان کو غم میں ڈالنا اور ان کی طاقت کو کچلنا اور ان کی جماعت کو متفرق اور تتر بتر اور منتشر کرنا ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے ان میں کا ہر فعل جائز ہوگا۔ (اور اگر غالب گمان ہو کہ اب اسلام کی فتح ہوگی تو ایسی صورت میں پھل دار درختوں کا نا شنا اور کھیتی کو نقصان پہنچا نا کر وہ ہوگا)۔
Ruling on releasing water, cutting trees, and destroying crops. He (al-Quduri) said: And they release water upon them, and cut their trees, and spoil their crops, because in all of that is causing them grief and anger, breaking their strength, and scattering their assembly, so it is prescribed. Translation: And al-Quduri has said: They cause a flood of water to flow over the infidels and enemies, i.e., if an opportunity arises, drown them in water. And cut their trees, and destroy their fields, because in all these actions is the humiliation of the infidels, their destruction, causing them grief, crushing their power, and scattering and dispersing their group. Therefore, every action among them will be permissible. (And if it is the dominant opinion that victory of Islam will soon occur, then in such a case cutting fruit-bearing trees and damaging crops is forbidden).
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, a foundational Hanafi text, on the permissibility of destroying enemy resources during jihad. It lists three actions: flooding, cutting trees, and destroying crops. The legal reasoning (talil) is that these acts inflict grief, anger, and defeat on the enemy, breaking their power and dispersing their forces. Therefore, they are prescribed (mashru'). However, the commentary adds an important qualification: if victory is imminent and the land will soon come under Muslim control, then it is forbidden to destroy fruit-bearing trees and crops, as they would become assets of the Muslim state. This shows the Hanafi principle of balancing military necessity with preservation of resources. The ruling is based on the general principle of harming the enemy to achieve victory, but with a view to future benefit.

Key Terms
إلحاق الكبت (ilḥāq al-kabt): Inflicting grief and mental distress upon the enemy.
الغَيْظ (al-ghayẓ): Anger or rage; here, inducing anger in the enemy to destabilize them.
الشَّوْكَة (al-shawkah): Military power or might; breaking the enemy's shawkah means crushing their strength.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the given passage, in which situation is it forbidden to cut fruit-bearing trees and destroy crops?
A) When the enemy is weak
B) When there is a strong presumption that Muslim victory is imminent
C) When the trees are owned by individuals
D) When the enemy has not started fighting

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of destroying enemy resources in jihad is conditioned by the principle of necessity and future benefit; when victory is imminent, destruction becomes prohibited.

Shooting at Enemies Despite Muslim Prisoners
Ruling on attacking an enemy fortress with Muslim captives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on attacking an enemy fortress containing Muslim captives and explain the rationale based on istihsan and the principle of repelling general harm.

Core Idea
Protecting the Muslim community overrides incidental killing of Muslim captives in jihad.

This lesson examines a challenging scenario in jihad: an enemy fortress holds Muslim captives or traders. Can the Muslim army attack, knowing some co-religionists may die? The Hanafi school permits it, prioritizing the defense of the entire community over specific individual harm. This ruling exemplifies istihsan (juristic preference) over strict analogy, a hallmark of Hanafi methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is shooting arrows or projectiles at an enemy fortress. The Hanafi ruling is that it is permissible (la ba'sa) even if Muslim captives or traders are inside. Identify the hukm level: mubah (permissible).
The ruling is conditional on the intention of targeting only the infidels.
2
Locate the rationale: general vs. specific harm
The text states that the purpose is to 'repel general harm from the egg of Islam' (baydat al-Islam). General harm to the community is outweighed by specific harm to the captives. Understand the distinction between daf' al-darar al-'amm (repelling general harm) and darar khass (specific harm).
The 'egg of Islam' metaphor represents the core Muslim entity.
3
Analyze the istihsan reasoning
The author uses a supplementary argument: if we refrained due to the possibility of a Muslim being inside, the door of jihad would be closed. This is istihsan—a departure from strict qiyas to achieve a broader public good. Recognise that the dalil here is not textual but based on juristic preference balancing harms.
Istihsan overrides the qiyas that would otherwise forbid killing a Muslim.
4
Note the condition of intention
The commentary adds that one must intend only the killing of the infidels, even if Muslims are killed incidentally. This condition validates the act and distinguishes it from intentional murder.
Without this condition, the act could be considered forbidden.
5
Apply to modern analogous scenarios
Consider modern military operations where collateral damage may involve Muslim civilians. This ruling provides a framework: permissible if the operation is to defend the community and the intention is against the enemy, not the civilians.
The principle of proportionality and necessity still apply; this ruling does not grant blanket permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کفار کے پاس مسلمان قیدی ہوں ان پر تیر اندازی کا حکم
وَلَا بَأْسَ بِرَمِّيهِمْ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِمْ مُسْلِمُ أسير أو تاجِرُ لَا فِي الرَّمْي دَفَعَ الضَّرَرِ الْعَامِ بِالذَّتِ عَنْ بَيْضَةِ الإِسْلَامِ وَقَتْلُ الأَسِيرِ وَالتَّاجِرِ ضَرَرٌ حَاصٌ وَ لأَنَّهُ فَكَمَا يَحْلُو حِصْنَ عَنْ مُسْلِمٍ فَلَوِ امْتَعَ بِاعْتِبَارِهِ لَا نُسَدَّ بَابَةً
ترجمہ اور کا فردشمنوں پر پتھر برسانے میں بھی کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اگر چہ ان میں مسلمان قیدی یا تاجر بھی موجود ہوں۔ کیونکہ ان پر پتھر برسانے میں مسلمانوں کی بڑی جماعت سے عمومی طریقہ سے نقصان دہ چیزوں سے بچانا مقصود ہوتا ہے اور چند یا ایک دو مسلمان یا تاجر کا مر جانا صرف اسی ایک دو فرد کا قتل ہو جانا یہ شخصی نقصان ہوتا ہے۔ اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ ایسی صورت کم ہی ہوتی ہے کہ کوئی قلعہ مسلمان سے بالکل خالی ہوتا ہو۔ اس لئے اگر مسلمان کا خیال کر کے ایسا کرنا منع کر دیا جائے تو جہاد کا دروازہ ہی بند ہو جائے گا۔ (اسی طرح اگر کافروں کے قلعہ میں چند مسلمان خواہ قیدی یا تاجر کسی طرح کے ہوں تو قلعہ کے اندر تو یوں کے گولے گرانا بھی جائز ہوگا ۔ البتہ اس صورت میں صرف کافروں کے قتل کی نیت ہونی چاہئے ۔ اگر چہ ضمنا مسلماں بھی مارے جائیں۔)
Ruling on shooting arrows at the infidels when Muslims are captives among them. And there is no harm in shooting them even if among them there is a Muslim captive or trader— no, in shooting, it is to repel general harm from the egg of Islam (the core Muslim community). And killing the captive and trader is a specific harm. And because it is as rare that a fortress is empty of a Muslim, so if we avoid it out of consideration for him, we would close the door of jihad. Translation: And there is no harm in raining stones upon the enemies even if there are Muslim captives or traders among them. Because in raining stones upon them, the intention is to protect the large group of Muslims from harm in a general way, and the death of a few or one or two Muslims or traders is only the killing of that one or two individuals—this is a personal harm. And also due to the proof that such a case is rare that a fortress is completely empty of a Muslim. Therefore, if such action is forbidden out of consideration for the Muslim, then the door of jihad would be closed. (Similarly, if there are a few Muslims, whether captives or traders, in the fortress of the infidels, then dropping cannonballs into the fortress is also permissible. However, in that case, one should intend only the killing of the infidels, even if Muslims are also killed incidentally.)
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and its rationale from the Hidayah. The ruling is that it is permissible to shoot arrows or projectiles at an enemy fortress even when Muslim captives or traders are inside. The legal reasoning is based on prioritizing the general public interest ('beydat al-Islam' - the core Muslim entity) over specific private harm. The death of a few Muslim individuals is a specific harm (darar khass), while defending the entire Islamic community is a general benefit. The argument also uses the principle that if we were to refrain because of the possibility of a Muslim being inside, the entire practice of jihad would be obstructed, since it is rare that a fortress is completely empty of Muslims. The commentary adds that in such cases, one must intend only the infidels, though Muslims may be killed incidentally. This is a classic Hanafi application of istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas, which might otherwise forbid killing a Muslim.

Key Terms
بيضة الإسلام (bayḍat al-islām): The core or stronghold of Islam; the Muslim community as a whole.
دفع الضرر العام (dafʿ al-ḍarar al-ʿāmm): Repelling general harm; a principle that justifies actions to prevent widespread harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the Hanafi school permits shooting at enemies even when Muslim captives are among them?
A) Because the captives have already lost their lives
B) To repel general harm from the Muslim community (دفع الضرر العام)
C) Because the captives are considered non-Muslims
D) Because the enemy will release them after the attack

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on attacking a fortress with Muslim captives is permissibility based on istihsan, prioritizing community protection over individual harm, contingent on correct intention.

8 min
Attack on Enemies Using Muslim Shields: No Liability for Incidental Muslim Deaths
Ruling on continued attack and exemption from liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on attacking enemies using Muslim shields and explain why no diyah or kaffarah is due.

Core Idea
No liability for killing Muslim shields in jihad: fard duties are not coupled with penalties.

This passage addresses a grim scenario where enemies use Muslim children or captives as human shields. The Hanafi school permits continued attack, with no diyah or kaffarah for Muslim deaths, based on the principle that liabilities are not attached to fard duties. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the key distinction from the case of extreme hunger (makhmasa).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is attacking enemies who shield themselves with Muslim children or captives. The ruling is that the attack must continue (mubah), and if Muslims are killed, no diyah (blood money) or kaffarah (expiation) is due.
The passage explicitly says 'they should not abstain from shooting them' and 'no blood-money nor expiation'.
2
Examine the condition of intention
The attacker must intend to kill the infidels (qasd al-kuffar), even if actual discrimination between Muslim and infidel is impossible. Intention suffices because obedience is required only to the extent of capacity.
The text: 'if actual discrimination is impossible, intention is possible'.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The primary proof is the maxim 'liabilities are not attached to fard duties' (الغرامات لا تقترن بالفرائض). Jihad is a fard kifayah, and imposing penalties would deter participation, thus defeating the purpose of a collective obligation.
The passage states: 'because jihad is a fard and liabilities are not attached to fard duties'.
4
Distinguish from makhmasa (extreme hunger)
In makhmasa, a person may eat another's property to save their own life, but compensation is due because it benefits the individual. In jihad, the benefit is communal (destroying the enemy), and fear of liability would prevent the attack, harming the common good.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the difference in ruling.
5
Confirm the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require diyah/kaffarah for Muslims killed accidentally in jihad, analogizing to makhmasa. The Hanafi position is that no liability attaches, which encourages participation in jihad.
The Hanafi view is considered mufta bihi.

کفار مسلمانوں کے بچوں اور مسلمان قیدیوں کو ڈھال بنا ئیں تب بھی تیر برسائے جائیں
وَإِن تَتَرَّسُوا بِصِبْيَانِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ أَو بِالأَسَارِى لَمْ يَكُفُّوا عَنْ رَمِّيهِمْ لِمَا بَيْنَا وَيَقْصُدُونَ بِالرَّمِي الْكُفَّارَ لِأَنَّهُ إِنْ تَعَدَّرَ السَّمِيرُ فَعْلًا فَلَقَدْ امْكَنَ قَصْدَا وَ الطَّاعَةُ بِحَسْبِ الطَّاقَةِ وَمَا آصَابُوا مِنْهُمْ لَا دِيَّةَ عَلَيْهِمْ وَلَا كَفَّارَةَ لأنَّ الْجِهَادَ فَرْضُ وَالْغَرَامَاتُ لَا تَقرِن بِالفُرُوضِ بِخِلَافِ حَالَةِ الْمَخْمَصَةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَمْتِنِعُ مَخَافَةَ الصَّمَانِ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنَ
إِحْيَاءِ نَفْسِهِ أَمَّا الْجِهَادُ فَمَبْنِيٌّ عَلَى اتَّلَافِ النَّفْسِ فَيَمْتَنَعَ حَذَرَ الضَّمَانِ
ترجمہ اگر مسلمانوں کے حملہ کے وقت دشمنوں نے مسلمانوں کے بچوں یا مسلمان قیدیوں کو ڈھال بنا کر اپنے آگے کر لیا تب بھی مجاہدین ان دشمنوں کو تیر یا پتھر مارنے سے نہ رکیں۔ کیونکہ عام مسلمانوں کے نقصان کو دور کرنے کے لئے ان قیدیوں یا بچوں کے نقصان کو برداشت کرنا ہوگا۔ البتہ تیر یا پتھر مارتے وقت صرف دشمنوں کی ہلاکت کی نیت کریں اور اپنے مسلمان قیدیوں یا بچوں کو مارنے کی نیت نہ کریں کیونکہ اگر تیر مارتے وقت مقابل کے مسلمانوں اور کافروں کے درمیان تمیز کرناممکن نہ ہو تو کم از کم نیت میں یہ امتیاز کرنا ممکن ہے اور فرمانبرداری اسی حد تک واجب ہوتی ہے جہاں تک بندہ کی وسعت میں ہو۔ پھر اس تیر یا پتھر مارنے سے مسلمانوں کے بچوں یا قیدیوں کو جس قسم کی بھی چوٹ لگے گی اس کی وجہ سے ان مسلمانوں پر نہ دیت لازم آئے گی اور نہ ان کے قتل سے کفارہ قتل ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جہاد فرض ہے اور فرائض ادا کرنے کا تعلق تاوان سے نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ بخلاف مخمصہ (جن کنی) کی حالت کے کیونکہ اس حالت میں تاوان کے خوف سے باز نہ رہے گا کیونکہ اس حالت میں غیر کے مال سے اپنی جان کو زندہ رکھنا ہوتا ہے۔ مگر جہاد میں تو کافروں کو ہلاک کرنا ہوتا ہے۔اسلئے اس جہاد میں تاوان لازم کرنے سے کوئی بھی ان پر حملہ نہیں کرے گا۔
تشریح بِخِلَافِ حَالَةِ الْمَخْمَصَةِ الخ مقاتلہ کے وقت اگر مسلمانوں سے مسلمان قیدی مارے بھی جائیں جب بھی ان پر ضمان لازم نہیں آتا ہے بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ اپنی جان جانے کے خطرہ کی صورت میں غیر کا مال کھا لینے سے اس مال کا منمان دینا پڑتا ہے۔ اس مسئلہ کی توضیح یہ ہے کہ اگر بھوک کی زیادتی سے آدمی کی حالت مرنے کی جیسی ہو جائے یعنی اگر غیر کا مال اس وقت نہ کھائے تو مر جانے کا خوف ہو اور غیر کے اس مال کے سوا اپنا کوئی مال جان بچانے کے لائق نہ ہو تو اس پر واجب ہے کہ ضرورت کے مطابق غیر کا مال کھا کر اپنی جان بچانے کی کوشش کرے۔ مگر جو کچھ کھائے گا اس کا منعمان بھی دینا واجب ہوگا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ فرض کی ادائیگی کی صورت میں بھی تاوان واجب ہوتا ہے اس لئے جہاد کی صورت میں مسلمان کے قتل پر اس کی جان کا ضمان لازم ہونا چاہئے ۔ اسی طرح اس جگہ بھی باوجودیکہ جہاد فرض ہے اگر مجاہدین کے تیر یا پتھر یا بندوق یا تلوار سے کوئی مسلمان قیدی یا مسلمان کا بچہ جس کو کافروں نے اپنے آگے رکھ کر ڈھال کا کام لیا تھا وہ مارا گیا تو چاہئے کہ کافروں کو مغلوب کرنے کے لئے اسے مارنا جائز ہو ۔ لیکن مسلمان مقتول کے بدلہ دیت یا کفار قتل بھی لازم ہو ۔ مگر مصنف نے دونوں صورتوں میں فرق بیان کیا کہ مخمصہ کی صورت میں اس وجہ سے تاوان برداشت کرنا ہوگا کہ خود اس کی اپنی جان بچتی ہے اور جہاد کی صورت میں تاوان برداشت نہیں کرے گا۔ کیونکہ یہاں تو کافروں کو ہلاک کرنا ہے پس اگر کافروں کے ہلاک کرنے میں اس پر دیت یا کفارہ قتل لازم آئے تو وہ جہاد سے پر ہیز کرے گا۔ حالانکہ دارالکفر میں ہر قلعہ کے اندر کوئی نہ کوئی مسلمان موجود ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے ہمیشہ اپنی جان بچانے کے لئے اسے آگے بڑھا دینگے تا کہ مجاہدین اپنے جہاد اور حملہ سے باز
And if they shield themselves with Muslim children or captives, they [the Muslims] should not abstain from shooting them, for the reason we have mentioned. And they should intend by shooting the infidels, because if actual discrimination is impossible, intention is possible, and obedience is according to capacity. And whatever injury they cause to them, they are not liable for blood-money nor expiation, because jihad is a fard and liabilities are not attached to fard duties—unlike the situation of extreme hunger (makhmasa), because he does not abstain for fear of liability, since in it there is preservation of his own life. As for jihad, it is based on the destruction of life, so he would abstain out of fear of liability. Translation: If at the time of the Muslim attack, the enemies place Muslim children or captives as shields in front of them, then the mujahideen should not stop shooting arrows or stones at the enemies. Because to remove harm from the general Muslims, they must bear the harm to those captives or children. However, at the time of shooting, they should intend only the killing of the enemies, not the killing of the Muslim captives or children, because if actual discrimination between the Muslims and infidels is impossible, at least this distinction in intention is possible, and obedience is required to the extent of one's capacity. Then, from this shooting, whatever injury befalls the Muslim children or captives, they will not be liable for blood-money nor expiation for killing, because jihad is a fard and the performance of fard duties is not connected with penalty. Unlike the situation of makhmasa (extreme hunger), because in that situation he will not refrain out of fear of liability, since in it he is preserving his own life. But in jihad, the aim is to destroy the infidels. Therefore, if in destroying the infidels he is made liable for blood-money or expiation, he would avoid jihad—whereas in the abode of disbelief, every fortress contains some Muslim. So they will always push him forward to save their own lives, so that the mujahideen may desist from their jihad and attack. Commentary: 'Unlike the situation of makhmasa...' During battle, even if Muslim captives are killed by Muslims, they are not liable, unlike the case where one is in danger of death and eats another's property—then he must pay compensation. The explanation of this issue is that if a person is near death due to extreme hunger—if he does not eat the property of another he fears death, and he has no property of his own sufficient to save his life—then it is obligatory for him to save his life by eating the other's property as needed. But whatever he eats, he must pay compensation. This shows that even in performing a fard, compensation is due. Therefore, in jihad, if a Muslim is killed, it should be that compensation for his life is due. Similarly, here even though jihad is fard, if a Muslim captive or child placed as a shield by the infidels is killed by the arrows, stones, guns, or swords of the mujahideen, then it should be permissible to kill him to overcome the infidels, but blood-money or expiation for killing should be due. However, the author distinguished between the two cases: in the case of makhmasa, he will bear compensation because his own life is saved, but in jihad, he will not bear compensation because here the aim is to destroy the infidels—if destroying infidels imposed blood-money or expiation on him, he would avoid jihad, whereas in the abode of disbelief, every fortress contains some Muslim. Therefore, they will always push him forward to save their own lives, so that the mujahideen desist from their attack.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This is a ruling on the permissibility of attacking enemies when they use Muslim children or captives as human shields. The Hanafi position is that the attack continues without stopping. The rationale is the same as the previous lesson: the general harm to the Muslim community outweighs the specific harm to the individuals used as shields. The passage adds important conditions: (1) The intention must be only to kill the infidels, even if actual discrimination is impossible; intention suffices because obedience is only required to the extent of capacity. (2) If such Muslims are killed, there is no diyah (blood money) or kaffarah (expiation) on the attackers. The reason is that jihad is a collective fard (farḍ kifāyah), and the general principle is that liabilities (gharamat) are not attached to fard duties. To support this, the passage contrasts with the situation of makhmasa (extreme hunger) where a person may eat another's property to save his own life but must pay compensation. In that case, compensation is due because he is saving his own life (a personal benefit). In jihad, the aim is to destroy the infidels (benefit for the community), and imposing liability would deter people from performing this crucial duty, thus closing the door of jihad. The commentary ('tashrih') further elaborates on the distinction, emphasizing that in jihad, no liability is incurred because the nature of jihad involves loss of life, and fear of penalty would discourage participation.

Key Terms
مخمصة (makhmasa): Extreme hunger that threatens one's life; a situation of necessity.
إتلاف النفس (itlāf al-nafs): Destruction of life; jihad is based on this principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is there no diyah or kaffarah for killing a Muslim captive used as a shield during jihad?
A) Because the captive is considered a traitor
B) Because liabilities are not attached to fard duties (الغرامات لا تقترن بالفرائض)
C) Because the enemy is solely responsible
D) Because the Muslim warrior made a vow

Key Takeaway
Liabilities are not attached to fard duties; thus, no diyah or kaffarah for Muslims killed as shields in jihad.

Module 2 · Lesson 19

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
8 min
No Diyah or Kaffarah When Muslim Shields Are Hit in Jihad
Ruling on attacking enemies shielding with Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when enemies use Muslim children or prisoners as shields, explain why no diyah or kaffarah is due, and apply the principle that obligations override penalties.

Core Idea
No diyah or kaffarah when Muslim shields are hit in jihad because obligations override penalties.

This lesson addresses a critical scenario in jihad: the enemy uses Muslim children or prisoners as human shields. According to the Hanafi school, the mujahideen must continue their attack, aiming at the enemy, and no compensation (diyah or kaffarah) is due for accidental Muslim deaths. The reasoning draws on the principle that performance of obligatory duties is not attached to penalties, and the greater harm to the Muslim community must be averted. You will examine the legal proof, contrast with a similar case (extreme hunger), and understand the rationale behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The enemy uses Muslim children or prisoners as shields. The Hanafi ruling: Mujahideen must continue attacking, they should intend the enemy, and no diyah or kaffarah is due for accidental killing of Muslim shields.
This is a clear exception from the usual rules of accidental killing.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is a rational argument (dalil aqli): 'jihad is a fard, and penalties are not attached to obligations' (لِأَنَّ الْجِهَادَ فَرْضُ وَالْغَرَامَاتُ لَا تَقرِن بِالفُرُوضِ). Also the principle that obligation is according to capacity: intention suffices when precise action is impossible.
The proof is not textual but rational, derived from the nature of obligations.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
The statement directly links the duty (jihad) to the absence of penalties. If diyah/kaffarah were due, it would discourage Muslims from fulfilling the fard, causing greater harm to the Ummah. The impossibility of distinguishing targets in action is compensated by intention, as 'obligation is according to capacity.'
The contrast with the makhmasa case strengthens the argument.
4
Contrast with the case of extreme hunger (makhmasa)
In makhmasa, a person may eat another's property without permission but must compensate. There, the motive is self-preservation. In jihad, the motive is destruction of the enemy, and imposing compensation would lead to abandonment of jihad, causing general harm to Islam. Thus, no compensation is due.
The distinction is based on the intended outcome: personal benefit vs. communal obligation.
5
Confirm the Hanafi position
The ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah is that no diyah or kaffarah is due. This is the operative position (mufta bihi) for fatwa. Despite potential disagreement from other schools, the Hanafi view is relied upon.
The passage does not detail other schools, but the cross-madhhab status is 'mukhtalaf fih.'

If they shield themselves with Muslim children or prisoners, the Muslims are not to stop shooting them for what we have mentioned. And they should aim at the disbelievers because if precise distinction in action is impossible, it is possible in intention. Obligation is according to capacity. And whatever they hit of them, there is no blood-money on them and no expiation because jihad is a fard, and penalties are not associated with duties. Unlike the case of famine because he does not refrain due to fear of liability since there is preservation of his own life. As for jihad, it is based on destruction of life, so he would refrain for fear of liability. Translation: If at the time of the Muslims' attack, the enemies have placed Muslim children or prisoners as shields in front of them, still the mujahideen should not refrain from shooting them with arrows or stones. Because to avert the general harm to Muslims, the harm to these prisoners or children must be tolerated. However, at the time of shooting, they should intend only the destruction of the enemies and not intend to kill the Muslim prisoners or children, because if it is not possible to distinguish between Muslims and disbelievers in action, at least it is possible to make this distinction in intention. And obedience is only obligatory to the extent of one's capacity. Then, whatever injury occurs to the Muslim children or prisoners from this shooting, neither diyah nor kaffarah for killing will be obligatory upon these Muslims, because jihad is a duty and fulfillment of duties is not connected with penalties. Unlike the case of famine (extreme hunger), because in that situation he will not refrain due to fear of liability since in that situation he is preserving his own life with the property of another. But in jihad, the aim is to destroy the disbelievers. Therefore, if imposing liability in this jihad would cause everyone to refrain from attacking them. Elaboration: The case of famine… It becomes known that even in performing a duty, compensation is obligatory, so in the case of jihad, liability for the life of a Muslim should be due. Similarly, here, despite jihad being a duty, if a mujahid’s arrow kills a Muslim prisoner or child used as a shield, it is permissible to kill them to overcome the disbelievers. But diyah or kaffarah should be due. However, the author distinguished between the two cases: in famine, compensation is borne because his own life is saved; in jihad, he will not bear compensation because here the aim is to destroy the disbelievers. If diyah or kaffarah were imposed, he would avoid jihad, whereas in dar al-kufr, every fortress contains some Muslims, so they would always put them forward to make the mujahideen abstain from attacking, causing general harm to Islam. Thus, it is proven that diyah is not due. And it should be known that taking Qur’an and women to dar al-kufr is prohibited for fear they will fall into enemy hands and be disgraced.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter of siyar (jihad) addressing the situation when the enemy uses Muslim children or prisoners as human shields. The ruling states that the mujahideen must continue their attack; they are not to stop due to the presence of these shields. The proof is rational: jihad is a collective obligation (fard kifayah), and the greater harm to the entire Muslim community must be prevented even if it results in accidental killing of some Muslims. The intention must be directed at the enemy, and if precise distinction is impossible in action, it is sufficient in intention. No diyah (blood-money) or kaffarah (expiation) is due for the accidental killing of Muslim shields because penalties are not attached to the performance of obligatory duties. The passage contrasts this with the case of extreme hunger (makhmasa), where a person in danger of death may eat another's property without permission but must compensate, because there the aim is self-preservation. In jihad, the aim is the destruction of the enemy, and imposing compensation would discourage participation, harming the general interest of Islam. The commentary emphasizes that this is based on the principle that duties are fulfilled according to capacity, and that the potential loss of Muslim shields is outweighed by the benefit of repelling the enemy's aggression.

Key Terms
تترسوا (tatarrasu): The act of using something as a shield; here, the enemy using Muslim children or prisoners as human shields.
دية (diyah): Financial compensation paid to the heirs of a person killed unintentionally or accidentally.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for killing a believer by mistake; includes freeing a slave or fasting two months.
مخمصة (makhmasa): Extreme hunger or famine that threatens life.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on diyah and kaffarah if a Muslim child used as a shield is accidentally killed during a jihad attack?
A) Both diyah and kaffarah are required because killing a Muslim always requires compensation.
B) Diyah is required but kaffarah is not, because the attacker intended the enemy.
C) Neither diyah nor kaffarah is required because jihad is a fard and penalties are not attached to obligations.
D) Kaffarah is required but diyah is waived to encourage participation in jihad.

Key Takeaway
When enemies use Muslim children or prisoners as shields, the Hanafi school rules that accidental killing of these shields does not incur diyah or kaffarah, because the obligation of jihad overrides normal penalties to prevent greater harm to the Muslim community.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules

Taking Women and Quran Copies on Military Expeditions
Rules for taking women and Quran copies with the army depending on size and safety

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on taking women and Quran copies on military expeditions, distinguishing between large armies and small raiding parties, and identify the correct interpretation of the hadith 'La tusafiru bil-Qur'an fi ardi al-'aduw'.

Core Idea
Safety determines permissibility: a large army allows women and Quran; a small raiding party forbids them due to risk of desecration.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical jihad question: when may Muslim forces take women and copies of the Quran on expeditions? The Hanafi school examines the level of risk. In a large army where safety is likely, it is permissible; in a small sariyyah where the enemy might prevail, it is disliked. The hadith prohibiting travel with the Quran to enemy land is interpreted narrowly, applying only when desecration is feared.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its contextual ruling
The act is taking women and Quran copies on military expeditions. Identify the ruling (hukm) for two contexts: large army ('askar 'azim) and small raiding party (sariyyah).
Large army: mubah; small sariyyah: makruh tanzih.
2
Locate the dalil and its interpretation
The primary dalil is the hadith: 'La tusafiru bil-Qur'an fi ardi al-'aduw' (Bukhari and Muslim). Understand how the Hanafi school restricts its application to scenarios of genuine fear.
The hadith is not absolute; it applies only when desecration is feared.
3
Analyze the conditions for women
Examine the rules for different categories of women: old women (aja'iz) may accompany a large army for essential services; young women should stay home; women should not fight except in necessity; taking women for conjugal service is disliked, and if necessary, use slave women instead of free women.
The principle is avoidance of fitna and preserving dignity.
4
Apply the rulings to new scenarios
Use the framework of safety (ghalabat al-salamah) to decide cases: e.g., entering with aman, or deciding on Quran copies in safe conditions.

Women and Quran copies: Do not take them out with the Islamic army. He said: There is no harm in taking out women and Quran copies with the Muslims if it is a large army that is safe from defeat, because the prevalent assumption is safety, and the prevalent is like certain. And it is disliked to take these out in a small raiding party that is not safe, because in that there is exposing them to loss and disgrace, and exposing the Quran copies to disrespect, for they (the enemy) will treat them lightly out of spite for the Muslims. This is the correct interpretation of his statement (peace be upon him): 'Do not travel with the Quran in enemy land.' And if a Muslim enters their land with a safe-conduct, there is no harm in his carrying the Quran with him if they are a people who fulfill treaties, because the apparent is no interference. Old women may go out with the great army to perform work suitable for them, like cooking, giving water, and treating wounds. As for young women (literally 'the drink'? mistaken), their staying in the houses is more protective against fitna. And they should not directly engage in fighting, because that would indicate the Muslims' weakness, except in necessity. And it is not recommended to take them out for sexual intercourse and service. If they must take them out, then with slave women rather than free women. Translation: If the mujahideen's army is so large that there is no fear of defeat, then they may take their women and the Holy Quran with them; there is no harm in that. Because such an army is overwhelmingly expected to return safely, and such overwhelming expectation is like certainty. And if it is a small army called a sariyyah, where generally victory is not certain but rather fear exists, then taking women and Quran with them is disliked, because there is fear of loss and disgrace. Because if the disbelievers gain control, they will treat them badly to anger the Muslims. On this basis, some hadiths report: 'Do not travel with the Quran in enemy land'—as Bukhari and Muslim narrated. The correct interpretation of such traditions is that there is fear of desecration. And if a Muslim enters their land with aman (safe conduct), there is no harm in his carrying the Quran with him, provided they are a people who keep their treaties and do not break promises, because ostensibly they will not interfere. Old women may and should go with the large army so that they can cook, feed, give water, treat the sick and wounded, and do other necessary work (as in the hadith of Anas (RA) narrated by Abu Dawud). But young women should stay in their homes so that they do not cause worry to Muslim men on the battlefield. Women should not fight in battle because that shows the Muslims' weakness—that their men have become weak—unless there is real necessity. If the mujahideen wish to take their wives for conjugal relations and service, they should not take them; it is not better. If they must take them, they should take slave women, not free women.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of taking women and copies of the Quran (masahif) on military expeditions. The ruling distinguishes between a large army ('askar 'azim) where safety is likely, and a small raiding party (sariyyah) where risk exists. In a large army, it is permissible to take them; in a small party, it is disliked (makruh) because of the risk of capture, disgrace, and desecration of the Quran. The hadith prohibiting travel with the Quran to enemy land is interpreted to apply when there is fear of desecration, not absolutely. If a Muslim enters with aman (safe conduct) and the people are trustworthy, he may carry the Quran. Regarding women: old women (aja'iz) may accompany the army to perform essential services like cooking, watering, and medical care, based on the practice of Anas ibn Malik. Young women should remain at home to avoid fitna. Women should not engage in combat except in necessity, as it indicates Muslim weakness. It is not recommended to bring women for conjugal relations and personal service; if unavoidable, slave women are preferred over free women.

Key Terms
سريّة (sariyyah): A small military detachment sent on a raid, often without the main army.
مصاحف (masahif): Copies of the Quran (plural of mus'haf).
عجائز (aja'iz): Old women, past the age of childbearing and sexual desire.
إماء (ima'): Slave women (female slaves); plural of amah.
حرائر (hara'ir): Free women (plural of hurrah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is it disliked (makruh) to take women and Quran copies on a military expedition?
A) When the army is large and safety is likely.
B) When the army is a small raiding party (sariyyah) where safety is not guaranteed.
C) When the women are old and intend to provide services.
D) When the enemy is trustworthy and keeps treaties.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on taking women and Quran copies depends on the level of safety: permissible in a large army, disliked in a small raiding party.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
beginner

Recommended Numbers for Jihad and Travel
Narrates hadith on recommended numbers and a Hanafi opinion on sariyah minimum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended numbers for travel, army, and detachment according to the hadith, and explain the Hanafi position on the minimum size of a sariyah.

Core Idea
Numbers in Jihad are recommended, not obligatory, and the Hanafi school sets a higher minimum for detachments.

This hadith from Ibn Abbas provides the Prophet's guidance on optimal group sizes for travel, military detachments, and armies. The numbers are recommendations (mustahabb), not binding obligations. The Hanafi school, drawing on practical military experience, reports that Imam Abu Hanifa considered a larger minimum for a sariyah (100 rather than 3). Understanding this distinction helps clarify when a ruling is based on textual recommendation versus juristic ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories and numbers
Find the four categories mentioned: travel companions (4), sariyah (3 as per hadith, 100 from Abu Hanifa), small army (400), large army (4000), and the number assured against defeat (12,000).
The hadith uses 'khayr' (best), indicating preference, not obligation.
2
Distinguish between recommended and obligatory
Recognise that the numbers are mustahabb (commended) because the phrase 'khayr' implies choice; the absence of imperative verbs supports this.
In Hanafi usul, a recommendation (sunnah) does not require repetition or compensation if omitted.
3
Analyse the sariyah minimum dispute
The hadith gives 3 as the minimum, but Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to have set it at 100. This reflects a difference between relying on the apparent meaning of the hadith and considering practical military effectiveness.
The Hanafi view is an example of istihsan (juridical preference) based on the objective of avoiding defeat.
4
Assess the thubut and dalala of the hadith
This hadith is narrated as ahad (single-chain), so its thubut is zanni. Its dalala (meaning) is also zanni because 'khayr' does not convey obligation. This opens the door for ijtihad.
Hadith from Abu Dawood: grade considered hasan by many scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حضرت ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہ نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے روایت کی ہے کہ سفر میں بہتر ساتھی چار عدد ہیں اور چھوٹے لشکروں میں بہتر لشکر چار سو ہیں بڑا لشکر چار ہزار بہتر ہے۔ اور جب بارہ ہزار ہوں تو تعداد کی کمی کی وجہ سے وہ مغلوب نہ ہوں گے۔ (رواہ ابو داؤد ) اور سریہ میں کم سے کم تین عدد ہیں۔ امام ابوحنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ ایک سو ہیں۔
Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, narrated from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that the best companions in travel are four, and the best small army is four hundred, the best large army is four thousand, and when there are twelve thousand, they will not be defeated due to lack of numbers. (Narrated by Abu Dawood) And the minimum for a sariyah (detachment) is three. It is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that it is one hundred.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage provides a hadith from Ibn Abbas regarding recommended numbers for military expeditions. The Prophet indicated optimal sizes: four travel companions, 400 for a small army, 4000 for a large army, and assured that 12,000 would not be defeated by numbers alone. The rest also mentions the minimum for a sariyah: the hadith says three, but a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa sets it at one hundred. This reflects a practical guideline for organizing forces.

Key Terms
سَفَر (safar): Travel
لَشْكَر (lashkar): Army
سَرِيَّة (sariyyah): Military detachment sent separately from the main army
بَهْتَر (behtar): Better (Urdu) – indicates recommendation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith in this lesson, what is the number that guarantees an army will not be defeated due to lack of numbers?
A) 400
B) 4,000
C) 12,000
D) 100

Key Takeaway
The numbers in the hadith are recommended (sunnah) not obligatory, and the Hanafi school, via Imam Abu Hanifa, sets the minimum for a sariyah at 100 based on practical ijtihad.

The Three Prohibitions: Ghadr, Ghulul, and Muthlah
Ruling with proof: three prohibitions and their definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibitions (ghadr, ghulul, muthlah), define each, and explain the dalil from the hadith.

Core Idea
The Prophet forbade treachery, theft from spoils, and mutilation — three distinct sins in jihad.

This lesson introduces three prohibited acts during warfare that are clearly forbidden by an explicit hadith. Understanding these definitions is essential for any student of fiqh al-jihad. The hadith quoted is a primary evidence used by the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibitions
Read the hadith: 'Do not embezzle, do not commit treachery, and do not mutilate.' List the three forbidden acts.
The Arabic uses the negation 'la' + verb, indicating a clear prohibition.
2
Define each term
From the text, define ghulul, ghadr, and muthlah precisely. Note the distinction between theft from spoils and general theft.
Ghulul is specific to khums before distribution.
3
Locate the dalil
The hadith is the primary proof. Note that it is an ahad hadith but its meaning is decisive (qat'i al-dalala).
The Hanafi school accepts ahad hadith in matters of prohibitions.
4
Explain wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the imperative prohibition indicates haram according to usul al-fiqh. The form 'la taf'alu' is used for prohibition.
The prohibition is definitive unless abrogated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غدر، غلول اور مثلہ کا حکم
وَيَنْبَغِي لِلمُسْلِمِينَ أَنْ لَا يَغْدِرُوا وَ لَا يَغُلُّوا وَ لَا يُمَثِّلُوا لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا تَغُلُّوا وَلَا تَغْدِرُوا وَلَا تُمَثِّلُوا وَالْغُلُولُ السَّرِقَةُ مِنَ الْمَغْنَمِ وَالْغَدْرُ الْحَيَانَةُ وَنَقْضُ الْعَهْدِ وَالْمُثْلَةُ الْمَرْوِيَّةُ فِي قِصَّةِ الْعِرْنِيِّينَ مَنْسُوخَةُ بِالنَّهَى الْمُتَأَخِّرِ هُوَ الْمَنْقُولُ
ترجمہ اور مسلمانوں کو چاہئے کہ غدر ، غلول اور مثلہ نہ کریں۔ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے اس فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ غلول نہ کرو۔ غدر نہ کرو اور مثلہ نہ کرو۔ جیسا کہ مسلم وغیرہ کی حدیث میں ہے۔ غلول ، مال غنیمت سے چوری کرنا، غدر، عہد توڑنا اور خیانت کرنا اور مثلہ مقتول کی ناک، کان وغیرہ کو کاٹ کر اس کی اصلی شکل بگاڑنا۔ اور عربینہ والوں کے متعلق جو یہ بات مروی ہے کہ انہیں مثلہ بھی کیا گیا تھا۔ حالانکہ ممنوع کام ہے تو حقیقت یہ ہے کہ اس کی ممانعت کا حکم اس واقعہ سے پہلے نہیں ہوا تھا بلکہ بعد میں ہوا تھا۔ اس لئے اب یہ ممنوع ہی ہوا۔ یہی قول منقول ہے۔
تشریح ولا يمثلوا الخ اگر دشمن قابو میں آ جائے تو اسے مثلہ نہیں کرنا چاہئے ۔ اگر چہ ایک بار رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے حکم سے مثلہ کا ثبوت ہے مگر اس کے بعد ہی آپ نے اس کی ممانعت فرمادی تھی لہذا مثلہ کا حکم منسوخ ہے۔ مثلہ کا واقعہ قبیلہ عربینہ کے لوگوں کے ساتھ پیش آیا تھا۔ اگر چہ یہ واقعہ پہلے بھی بیان کیا جاچکا ہے۔ پھر بھی یہاں اس کا مختصر ابیان یہ ہے کہ قبیلہ عربیہ کے کچھ لوگ مدینہ آ کر مسلمان ہوئے مگر بیمار پڑ گئے تب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کو حکم فرمایا کہ جس جگہ پر زکوۃ کے اونٹ رہتے اور چرتے ہیں وہاں جا کر رہو اور ان اونٹوں کا دودھ اور پیشاب پیو۔ انہوں نے اس پر عمل کیا اور اسی سے وہ تندرست ہو گئے تب چرواہوں کو قتل کر کے ان کے سارے جانور بھگا کر لے گئے۔
وہ گرفتار کر کے لائے گئے تب آپ نے ان کے ہاتھ پاؤں کاٹنے اور ان کی آنکھوں میں سلائی پھیر نے کا حکم دیا ۔ الخ۔ بخاری اور مسلم وغیرہ نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ اور حضرت انس رضی اللہ عنہ نے روایت کی ہے کہ اس واقعہ کے بعد رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جب کبھی کوئی خطبہ دیا ہر ایک میں مثلہ سے منع فرمایا ۔ رواہ البیہقی ۔ اور صحیح کی بعض روایتوں سے ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ عرینہ والوں نے چرواہوں کی آنکھیں بول کے کانوں سے پھوڑ دی تھیں اس لئے اس کے قصاص میں رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے پورا پورا بدلہ لینے کی غرض سے عربینہ والوں کی آنکھیں پھوڑ دیں۔ ابن سعد نے بھی یہی روایت کی ہے اور ابن ابی شیبہ نے عمران بن حصین سے روایت کی ہے کہ اس کے بعد رسول اللہ ہر ایک خطبہ میں ہمیں صدقہ دینے پر آمادہ کراتے اور مثلہ سے منع فرماتے تھے ۔ اور بیہقی نے معرفت میں کہا ہے کہ عربینہ والوں کا واقعہ یا تو منسوخ ہے جیسا کہ قتادہ اور ابن سیرین سے مروی ہے اور امام شافعی کا قول بھی یہی ہے۔ یا عرینہ والوں کو مثلہ کرنا چرواہوں کے بدلہ میں تھا۔ میں مترجم کہتا ہوں کہ یہی وجہ ہے کہ مثلہ ہمیشہ سے ممنوع ہے۔ اور عربینہ والوں سے قصاص لیا گیا تھا۔
Ruling on ghadr, ghulul, and muthlah. It is incumbent upon Muslims not to commit treachery, nor to embezzle from the spoils, nor to practice mutilation, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Do not embezzle, do not commit treachery, and do not mutilate.' And ghulul is theft from the spoils; ghadr is betrayal and breach of covenant; and muthlah is that which is narrated in the story of the 'Urayniyyeen, which is abrogated by the later prohibition. That is the transmitted view. Translation: And Muslims should not commit ghadr, ghulul, and muthlah, because of the command of the Messenger (peace be upon him): Do not commit ghulul, do not commit ghadr, and do not commit muthlah, as in the hadith of Muslim and others. Ghulul is theft from the spoils; ghadr is breaking a covenant and treachery; muthlah is disfiguring the slain by cutting nose, ear, etc. And regarding the 'Urayniyyeen, it is reported that they were mutilated, although it is prohibited. The reality is that the prohibition came after that incident; thus it is now prohibited. This is the transmitted saying. Commentary: 'Do not mutilate' etc. If the enemy is captured, they should not be mutilated. Although there is evidence of mutilation by command of the Messenger once, later he forbade it, so the ruling is abrogated. The story of the 'Urayniyyeen is as follows: Some people from the tribe of 'Uraynah came to Medina and became Muslim, but fell ill. The Prophet ordered them to go to the place where the zakat camels were and drink their milk and urine. They recovered, then killed the shepherds and drove away the camels. They were captured, and the Prophet ordered their hands and feet to be cut off and their eyes gouged out. Bukhari and Muslim narrated it. Anas narrated that after that, whenever the Prophet gave a sermon, he forbade muthlah. Bayhaqi narrated it. Some sound narrations indicate that the 'Urayniyyeen had gouged out the eyes of the shepherds, so the Prophet retaliated with the same. Ibn Sa'd narrated similarly. Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated from 'Imran ibn Husayn that after that, the Prophet urged us to give charity and forbade muthlah in every sermon. Bayhaqi said in Ma'rifah that the story of the 'Urayniyyeen is either abrogated, as narrated from Qatadah and Ibn Sirin, and this is also the view of Imam al-Shafi'i, or that the mutilation of the 'Urayniyyeen was in retaliation for the shepherds. The translator says that this is why muthlah is permanently prohibited, and the 'Urayniyyeen were given retaliation.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the ruling that Muslims must avoid three prohibited acts: ghadr (treachery/breach of covenant), ghulul (theft from the spoils of war), and muthlah (mutilation of the enemy). The evidence is a hadith in which the Prophet explicitly forbids these. The text then defines each term. A significant discussion follows regarding the story of the 'Urayniyyeen: although the Prophet himself ordered mutilation in that case, this was before the prohibition was revealed. Therefore the ruling is abrogated, and afterward mutilation is forbidden. The commentary elaborates that the incident was one of retaliation (qisas) because the 'Urayniyyeen had first mutilated the shepherds. Thus the prohibition of muthlah is clear and established.

Key Terms
غَدْر (ghadr): Treachery or breach of a covenant/agreement with the enemy
غُلُول (ghulul): Theft from the spoils of war before distribution
مُثْلَة (muthlah): Mutilation of a slain or captured enemy, disfiguring the body

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the meaning of 'ghulul'?
A) Breaking a treaty
B) Stealing from the spoils of war before distribution
C) Mutilating a dead body
D) Retreating from battle

Key Takeaway
The three prohibitions of ghadr, ghulul, and muthlah are firmly grounded in a clear prophetic hadith and are considered haram in the Hanafi school.

The Abrogation of Muthlah: The 'Urayniyyeen Incident
Abrogation discussion: the 'Urayniyyeen incident and the prohibition of muthlah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the concept of naskh (abrogation) as applied to the prohibition of muthlah and analyze the 'Urayniyyeen incident.

Core Idea
The 'Urayniyyeen incident seems to permit mutilation, but it was abrogated; the final ruling is that muthlah is haram.

The story of the 'Urayniyyeen presents an apparent conflict: the Prophet himself ordered mutilation, yet later forbade it. This lesson examines how the later prohibition abrogates the earlier practice. Understanding this incident clarifies the final ruling on muthlah.

Guided Path
1
Recount the incident
Read the story: the 'Urayniyyeen came to Medina, converted, fell ill, were sent to the camel pasture, recovered, then killed the shepherds and stole the camels. They were captured and punished by mutilation.
The incident is recorded in Bukhari and Muslim.
2
Identify the apparent conflict
The Prophet ordered mutilation in this case, but later prohibited it. This creates a question: was mutilation permissible at that time and later abrogated?
Some argue it was retaliation (qisas) for their mutilation of the shepherds.
3
Explain the abrogation
The text states that the later prohibition (the hadith 'la tumaththilu') abrogates the earlier practice. This is the Hanafi position.
The principle of naskh: a later ruling can override an earlier one if they are contradictory.
4
Note scholarly views
Imam al-Shafi'i also held that the incident is abrogated. The translator adds that it was permissible only as retaliation.
There is a view that the mutilation was qisas, not a general license.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
The mufta bihi is that muthlah is absolutely prohibited after the prohibition. The incident does not create an exception.
This is the relied-upon ruling in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غدر، غلول اور مثلہ کا حکم
وَيَنْبَغِي لِلمُسْلِمِينَ أَنْ لَا يَغْدِرُوا وَ لَا يَغُلُّوا وَ لَا يُمَثِّلُوا لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا تَغُلُّوا وَلَا تَغْدِرُوا وَلَا تُمَثِّلُوا وَالْغُلُولُ السَّرِقَةُ مِنَ الْمَغْنَمِ وَالْغَدْرُ الْحَيَانَةُ وَنَقْضُ الْعَهْدِ وَالْمُثْلَةُ الْمَرْوِيَّةُ فِي قِصَّةِ الْعِرْنِيِّينَ مَنْسُوخَةُ بِالنَّهَى الْمُتَأَخِّرِ هُوَ الْمَنْقُولُ
ترجمہ اور مسلمانوں کو چاہئے کہ غدر ، غلول اور مثلہ نہ کریں۔ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے اس فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ غلول نہ کرو۔ غدر نہ کرو اور مثلہ نہ کرو۔ جیسا کہ مسلم وغیرہ کی حدیث میں ہے۔ غلول ، مال غنیمت سے چوری کرنا، غدر، عہد توڑنا اور خیانت کرنا اور مثلہ مقتول کی ناک، کان وغیرہ کو کاٹ کر اس کی اصلی شکل بگاڑنا۔ اور عربینہ والوں کے متعلق جو یہ بات مروی ہے کہ انہیں مثلہ بھی کیا گیا تھا۔ حالانکہ ممنوع کام ہے تو حقیقت یہ ہے کہ اس کی ممانعت کا حکم اس واقعہ سے پہلے نہیں ہوا تھا بلکہ بعد میں ہوا تھا۔ اس لئے اب یہ ممنوع ہی ہوا۔ یہی قول منقول ہے۔
تشریح ولا يمثلوا الخ اگر دشمن قابو میں آ جائے تو اسے مثلہ نہیں کرنا چاہئے ۔ اگر چہ ایک بار رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے حکم سے مثلہ کا ثبوت ہے مگر اس کے بعد ہی آپ نے اس کی ممانعت فرمادی تھی لہذا مثلہ کا حکم منسوخ ہے۔ مثلہ کا واقعہ قبیلہ عربینہ کے لوگوں کے ساتھ پیش آیا تھا۔ اگر چہ یہ واقعہ پہلے بھی بیان کیا جاچکا ہے۔ پھر بھی یہاں اس کا مختصر ابیان یہ ہے کہ قبیلہ عربیہ کے کچھ لوگ مدینہ آ کر مسلمان ہوئے مگر بیمار پڑ گئے تب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کو حکم فرمایا کہ جس جگہ پر زکوۃ کے اونٹ رہتے اور چرتے ہیں وہاں جا کر رہو اور ان اونٹوں کا دودھ اور پیشاب پیو۔ انہوں نے اس پر عمل کیا اور اسی سے وہ تندرست ہو گئے تب چرواہوں کو قتل کر کے ان کے سارے جانور بھگا کر لے گئے۔
وہ گرفتار کر کے لائے گئے تب آپ نے ان کے ہاتھ پاؤں کاٹنے اور ان کی آنکھوں میں سلائی پھیر نے کا حکم دیا ۔ الخ۔ بخاری اور مسلم وغیرہ نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ اور حضرت انس رضی اللہ عنہ نے روایت کی ہے کہ اس واقعہ کے بعد رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جب کبھی کوئی خطبہ دیا ہر ایک میں مثلہ سے منع فرمایا ۔ رواہ البیہقی ۔ اور صحیح کی بعض روایتوں سے ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ عرینہ والوں نے چرواہوں کی آنکھیں بول کے کانوں سے پھوڑ دی تھیں اس لئے اس کے قصاص میں رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے پورا پورا بدلہ لینے کی غرض سے عربینہ والوں کی آنکھیں پھوڑ دیں۔ ابن سعد نے بھی یہی روایت کی ہے اور ابن ابی شیبہ نے عمران بن حصین سے روایت کی ہے کہ اس کے بعد رسول اللہ ہر ایک خطبہ میں ہمیں صدقہ دینے پر آمادہ کراتے اور مثلہ سے منع فرماتے تھے ۔ اور بیہقی نے معرفت میں کہا ہے کہ عربینہ والوں کا واقعہ یا تو منسوخ ہے جیسا کہ قتادہ اور ابن سیرین سے مروی ہے اور امام شافعی کا قول بھی یہی ہے۔ یا عرینہ والوں کو مثلہ کرنا چرواہوں کے بدلہ میں تھا۔ میں مترجم کہتا ہوں کہ یہی وجہ ہے کہ مثلہ ہمیشہ سے ممنوع ہے۔ اور عربینہ والوں سے قصاص لیا گیا تھا۔
Ruling on ghadr, ghulul, and muthlah. It is incumbent upon Muslims not to commit treachery, nor to embezzle from the spoils, nor to practice mutilation, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Do not embezzle, do not commit treachery, and do not mutilate.' And ghulul is theft from the spoils; ghadr is betrayal and breach of covenant; and muthlah is that which is narrated in the story of the 'Urayniyyeen, which is abrogated by the later prohibition. That is the transmitted view. Translation: And Muslims should not commit ghadr, ghulul, and muthlah, because of the command of the Messenger (peace be upon him): Do not commit ghulul, do not commit ghadr, and do not commit muthlah, as in the hadith of Muslim and others. Ghulul is theft from the spoils; ghadr is breaking a covenant and treachery; muthlah is disfiguring the slain by cutting nose, ear, etc. And regarding the 'Urayniyyeen, it is reported that they were mutilated, although it is prohibited. The reality is that the prohibition came after that incident; thus it is now prohibited. This is the transmitted saying. Commentary: 'Do not mutilate' etc. If the enemy is captured, they should not be mutilated. Although there is evidence of mutilation by command of the Messenger once, later he forbade it, so the ruling is abrogated. The story of the 'Urayniyyeen is as follows: Some people from the tribe of 'Uraynah came to Medina and became Muslim, but fell ill. The Prophet ordered them to go to the place where the zakat camels were and drink their milk and urine. They recovered, then killed the shepherds and drove away the camels. They were captured, and the Prophet ordered their hands and feet to be cut off and their eyes gouged out. Bukhari and Muslim narrated it. Anas narrated that after that, whenever the Prophet gave a sermon, he forbade muthlah. Bayhaqi narrated it. Some sound narrations indicate that the 'Urayniyyeen had gouged out the eyes of the shepherds, so the Prophet retaliated with the same. Ibn Sa'd narrated similarly. Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated from 'Imran ibn Husayn that after that, the Prophet urged us to give charity and forbade muthlah in every sermon. Bayhaqi said in Ma'rifah that the story of the 'Urayniyyeen is either abrogated, as narrated from Qatadah and Ibn Sirin, and this is also the view of Imam al-Shafi'i, or that the mutilation of the 'Urayniyyeen was in retaliation for the shepherds. The translator says that this is why muthlah is permanently prohibited, and the 'Urayniyyeen were given retaliation.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the ruling that Muslims must avoid three prohibited acts: ghadr (treachery/breach of covenant), ghulul (theft from the spoils of war), and muthlah (mutilation of the enemy). The evidence is a hadith in which the Prophet explicitly forbids these. The text then defines each term. A significant discussion follows regarding the story of the 'Urayniyyeen: although the Prophet himself ordered mutilation in that case, this was before the prohibition was revealed. Therefore the ruling is abrogated, and afterward mutilation is forbidden. The commentary elaborates that the incident was one of retaliation (qisas) because the 'Urayniyyeen had first mutilated the shepherds. Thus the prohibition of muthlah is clear and established.

Key Terms
مَنْسُوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; the earlier ruling is overridden by a later one
مُثْلَة (muthlah): Mutilation of a slain or captured enemy, disfiguring the body

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the mutilation of the 'Urayniyyeen considered abrogated?
A) Because the Prophet regretted it
B) Because the later prohibition from the Prophet overrides the earlier practice
C) Because it was only for that specific tribe
D) Because it was done by the Companions, not the Prophet

Key Takeaway
The 'Urayniyyeen incident does not create an exception; muthlah is abrogated and absolutely prohibited.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
