Prohibition of Killing Non-Combatants in Jihad
Ruling and dispute regarding killing non-combatants in jihad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing non-combatants in jihad and explain the legal cause (illa) that distinguishes it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
In jihad, killing is permitted only for those who fight — not for women, children, the elderly, or the disabled.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute: whether the permissibility to kill enemy combatants in jihad is based on their ability to fight (Hanafi) or on their disbelief (Shafi'i). The Hanafi school uses explicit prophetic prohibitions to argue that non-combatants such as women, children, the very old, and the disabled are not to be targeted. Understanding this dispute clarifies the moral and legal boundaries of warfare in Islam.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that women, children, the very old (shaykh fani), the paralyzed (muq'ad), and the blind are not to be intentionally killed in jihad. The Hanafi school holds that the legal cause (illa) permitting killing is actual combat (hirab), not disbelief.
The Arabic word used is 'al-hirab' which means actual fighting.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees regarding the very old, paralyzed, and blind. He argues that the cause for permissibility is disbelief (kufr) in adults, so all adult disbelievers are permissible targets regardless of fighting ability.
The opposing school is Imam al-Shafi'i, but the passage notes that Imam Malik and Ahmad agree with Hanafi on this issue.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof is based on the general permission to fight disbelievers (e.g., Quran 9:5). Since disbelief is present in all adult non-Muslims, killing them is permitted.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response cites specific hadith: the Prophet forbade killing women and children, and questioned the killing of a woman saying 'she was not fighting'. This shows that the cause is fighting, not disbelief. The analogy extends to all who cannot fight.
The hadith evidence is from Sahih Bukhari and Muslim.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi prohibits killing the elderly and disabled enemy combatants; Shafi'i permits it. This affects battlefield decisions, detention, and treatment of prisoners.
The mufta bihi in Hanafi school is the prohibition of killing non-combatants.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عورت، بچے ، بوڑھے، مقعد ، امی کو جہاد میں قتل نہ کیا جائے
وَلَا يَقْتُلُوا امْرَأَةً وَلَا صَبِيًّا وَلَا شَيْخًا فَانِيًا وَلَا مُقْعَدًا وَلَا أَعْمَى لِأَنَّ الْمُبِيحَ لِلْقَتْلِ عِنْدَنَا هُوَ الْحِرَابُ وَلَا يَتَحَقَّقُ وَلِهَذَا لَا يُقْتَلُ يَابِسُ الشَّقِّ وَالْمَقْطُوعُ الْيُمْنَى وَالْمَقْطُوعُ يَدُهُ وَرِجْلُهُ مِنْ خِلَافٍ وَالشَّافِعِيُّ يُخَالِفُنَا فِي الشَّيْخِ وَالْمُقْعَدِ وَالْأَعْمَى لِأَنَّ الْحَارِبَ عِنْدَهُ الْكُفْرُ وَالْحُجَّةُ عَلَيْهِ مَا بَيَّنَّا وَقَدْ صَحَّ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ نَهَى عَنْ قَتْلِ الصِّبْيَانِ وَالنِّسَاءِ وَحِينَ رَأَى رَسُولُ اللهِ امْرَأَةً مَقْتُولَةً قَالَ هَا مَا كَانَتْ هَذِهِ تُقَاتِلُ فَلِمَ قُتِلَتْ
ترجمہ اور مسلمانوں پر لازم ہے کہ وہ میدان جہاد میں کسی عورت یا بچہ یا شیخ فانی یا لنگڑے یا اندھے کو قتل نہ کریں ۔ کیونکہ ہمارے نزدیک لڑائی دشمن کے قتل کو اگر چہ جائز کرنے والی ہوتی ہے۔ مگر چونکہ ایسے لوگوں سے لڑائی نہیں ہو سکتی ہے اس لئے اسے اور ایسے شخص کو بھی جس کے بدن کا ایک پہلو خشک ہو چکا ہو یا دایاں ہاتھ کٹا ہوا ہو یا ایک طرف کا ہاتھ اور دوسری طرف کا پاؤں کٹا ہوا ہوا سے بھی قتل نہ کریں ۔ اور امام شافعی شیخ فانی لنگڑے اندھے کے قتل کو جائز سمجھتے ہیں اس وجہ سے کہ ان کے نزدیک قتل کو مباح کرنے والی چیز کفر کا ہونا ہے جو ان سب میں موجود ہے۔ ان کے خلاف ہماری دلیل وہی ہے جو ہم نے پہلے بیان کر دی ہے ( ۔ کہ لڑائی کا ہونا ہی قتل کے لئے مسیح ہے ) اور اس طرح سے بھی ثابت ہے کہ نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بچوں اور عورتوں کو قتل کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اور ایک دفعہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کسی عورت کو مقتول پایا تو فرمایا یہ عورت تو نہیں لڑ سکتی تھی پھر یہ کیوں قتل کی گئی۔
تشریح ولا يقتلوا امراة .. الخ بہت بوڑھے اندھے لنگڑے اور ہاتھ پاؤں کٹے لوگوں کے قتل میں دو اقوال ہیں یعنی قول اول میں سب قتل کئے جائیں گے اور دوسرے قول میں قتل نہیں کئے جائیں گے۔ امام مالک اور احمد رحمۃ اللہ علیہا کا یہی قول ہے۔ جیسا کہ الوجیز میں ہے۔ اور عورتوں اور بچوں کے قتل سے ممانعت کی حدیث صحیح بخاری و مسلم میں ہے۔ اور مقتولہ عورت کی حدیث عبدالرزاق وابوداؤ داور نسائی نے روایت کی ہے۔ اور صحیحین میں ہے کہ آپ نے کسی جہاد میں ایک عورت کو مقتول دیکھ کر عورتوں اور بچوں کو قتل کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے ۔ اور یہی مفہوم طبرانی و ابن حبان واحمد اور ابن ماجہ میں مذکور ہے۔ الحاصل عورتوں اور بچوں کے قتل کے ممنوع ہونے پر اجماع ہے۔ واضح ہو کہ اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ خاص ارادہ اور نشانہ کر کے عورت اور بچہ کوقتل نہیں کرنا چاہئے ۔ اور اگر ان کو علیحدہ کرنا اور ممتاز کرنا ممکن نہ
Women, children, elderly, paralyzed, and blind should not be killed in jihad. And they should not kill a woman, nor a child, nor a very old man, nor a paralyzed person, nor a blind person, because according to us the permitter of killing is fighting, and it is not realized (from them). Therefore, also the one with a dried side, and the one amputated of the right hand, and the one whose hand and foot on opposite sides are amputated, are not killed. And al-Shafi'i disagrees with us regarding the very old, the paralyzed, and the blind, because according to him the cause for warfare is disbelief, and the proof against him is what we have explained. And it is authentically reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade killing children and women, and when the Messenger of Allah saw a killed woman, he said: 'This one was not fighting; why was she killed?' Translation: And it is incumbent upon Muslims not to kill any woman, child, very old man, lame, or blind person in the battlefield. Because according to us, the thing that makes killing permissible is fighting; but since such people cannot fight, therefore they should not be killed, nor should one whose one side is paralyzed, or whose right hand is cut off, or whose hand on one side and foot on the other side are cut off. And Imam al-Shafi'i considers it permissible to kill the very old, the lame, and the blind, because according to him the permitter of killing is the existence of disbelief, which is present in all of them. Our proof against him is what we have already stated: it is fighting that permits killing. And it is also established that the Prophet forbade killing children and women. And once the Messenger of Allah found a woman killed and said: 'This woman could not fight; why was she killed?' Commentary: 'And do not kill a woman' etc. There are two opinions regarding killing the very old, blind, lame, and those with amputated limbs: in the first opinion, all are killed, and in the second, they are not killed. Imam Malik and Ahmad (may Allah have mercy on them) hold this view, as mentioned in al-Wajiz. And the hadith prohibiting killing women and children is in Sahih Bukhari and Muslim. And the hadith of the killed woman was narrated by Abdurrazzaq, Abu Dawud, and Nasa'i. And in the Two Sahihs, it is reported that the Prophet saw a woman killed in a battle and forbade killing women and children. And the same meaning is mentioned by al-Tabarani, Ibn Hibban, Ahmad, and Ibn Majah. In summary, there is consensus on the prohibition of killing women and children. It should be clear that the intended meaning is that one should not intentionally target and kill a woman or child; if it is not possible to separate and distinguish them [from combatants], then... (the text cuts off).
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage presents a clear inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi school prohibits killing women, children, the very old (shaykh fani), the paralyzed (muq'ad), and the blind in jihad, because the legal cause (illa) for permitting killing is actual combat (hirab). Since these individuals do not engage in fighting, they are not permissible targets. The Shafi'i school, however, argues that the cause is disbelief (kufr) itself, so it is permissible to kill any adult unbeliever regardless of fighting ability. The Hanafi response is based on prophetic hadith: the Prophet forbade killing women and children, and when he saw a dead woman, he questioned why she was killed. The commentary further notes that Imam Malik and Ahmad agree with the Hanafi position, and there is consensus (ijma) on the prohibition of killing women and children. However, the prohibition applies to deliberate targeting; if they are mixed with combatants and cannot be distinguished, some allowance may be made (though the text does not fully complete the discussion).

Key Terms
شَيْخ فَانِي (shaykh fani): A very old man who is decrepit and cannot fight
مُقْعَد (muq'ad): A person who is paralyzed or unable to walk
أَعْمَى (a'ma): A blind person
حِرَاب (hirab): Actual fighting/warfare

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Quran 2:190 (fight in the way of Allah those who fight you)
B) Hadith of the Prophet forbidding killing women and children
C) Consensus of the Companions on prohibition
D) Qiyas on the prohibition of killing monks

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits killing non-combatants in jihad because the legal cause is actual combat, not disbelief, and this is supported by explicit prophetic teachings.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
8 min
Rulings on Killing Non-Combatants in Jihad
Explains conditions under which non-combatants may be killed in jihad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general prohibition against killing non-combatants in jihad and identify the three exceptions recognized by the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Non-combatants are protected unless they fight, counsel war, or lead harmfully.

Jihad rules distinguish between combatants and non-combatants. While the default ruling is protection for women, children, the elderly, monks, and the insane, the Hanafi school permits killing them in specific circumstances where they contribute to harm. This lesson unpacks the conditions from the Quduri text and the supporting hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Start with the general principle: it is haram to kill non-combatants. The text lists women, children, the elderly (shaykh fani), monks, and the insane as protected.
Default ruling is based on the hadith prohibiting killing women and children.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud (Sa'b ibn Jaththamah) and the precedent of the Prophet killing Warid ibn Samah, an elderly but strategic advisor.
Also mentions general raids where collateral damage is permissible.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith establishes a general prohibition. The exceptions are derived from the principle of repelling harm (daf' al-sharr) and qiyas: if a non-combatant actively causes harm (by fighting, advising, or ruling), they lose protection.
The Prophet's killing of Warid shows that military expertise justifies targeting.
4
Note the three exceptions
From the Quduri matn: (1) anyone with strategic opinion in warfare (ra'y fi al-harb), (2) a woman who is a queen (malikah) whose harm extends to people, (3) anyone who physically fights.
Also includes monks who mix with people and incite; isolated monks remain protected.
5
Evaluate the evidence
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala). The Hanafi school relies on the stronger need to prevent harm, allowing exceptions through istihsan and qiyas.
Other schools may require explicit textual permission for exceptions; Hanafis use broader reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير
۳۴
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد هفتم
ہو جیسے قلعہ پر حملہ کرنے میں یا مشرکوں پر عام چھاپہ مارنے میں بچے یا عورتیں نشانہ بن جائیں تو اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ اور مواخذہ نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ ابوداؤ دو تر مندی کی حضرت صعب بن جثامہ کی حدیث میں مذکور ہے۔ اور شیخ فانی سے مراد وہ بوڑھا مرد ہے جو قتال نہیں کر سکتا ہے۔ اور جنب مقابلہ میں صفیں ایک دوسرے کے آمنے سامنے آجائیں اس وقت وہ چلا کر لوگوں کو مقابلہ پر آمادہ نہ کرتا ہو۔ اور نہ وہ حیلہ وتد بیر کر سکتا ہو۔ اور نہ وہ جنگ کی کاروائی میں صاحب رائے ہو ۔ اگر ایسا ہو تو اسے بھی قتل کر دیا جائے ۔ چنانچہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ورید ابن صمہ کو جو کہ ایک سو بیس برس کا تھا قتل کر دیا۔ کیونکہ وہ جنگی معاملات میں بہت ہوشیار اور صاحب رائے تھا۔ خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ ان لوگوں کا قتل اسی صورت میں جائز ہو گا جب کہ ان سے مسلمانوں کو نقصان ہو ورنہ جائز نہ ہوگا۔
مذکورہ بالا لوگوں کو کب قتل کرنے کی گنجائش ہے
قَالَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ اَحَدُهُؤُلَاءِ مِمَّنْ لَمْ رَأَى فِي الْحِرَابِ اَوْ تَكُونُ الْمَرْأَةُ مَلَكَةً لِتَعَدِّي ضَرَرِهَا إِلَى الْعِبَادِ وَ كَذَا يُقْتَلُ مَنْ قَاتَلَ مِنْ هُؤُلَاءِ دَفْعًا لِشَرِهِ وَلِأَنَّ الْقِتَالَ مُبِيعٌ حَقِيقَةٌ
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ البتہ اگران مجبور لوگوں میں سے کوئی شخص لڑائی کے سلسلہ میں رائے اور تد بیر رکھتا ہو یا عورت اپنے علاقہ کی ملکہ ( یا سر دار ) ہو تو اسے قتل کرنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا اثر اور ضرر بندوں اور عوام تک پہنچتا ہے
اسی طرح مذکورہ لوگوں میں سے جو کوئی قتال کرتا ہو تو اس کے شر سے بچنے کے لئے بھی اسے قتل کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور اس لئے بھی کہ قتال کا جاری رہنا ہی اس کے قتل کو مباح کرتا ہے ۔ اسی طرح جو راہب اپنی صومعہ ( عبادت گاہ) یا گر جا گھر میں ہوا عوام اور لوگوں سے میل جول نہ رکھتا ہو تو اس کو بھی قتل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے )۔
میدان جہاد میں مجنون کو بھی قتل نہ کیا جائے
وَلَا يَقْتُلُوا مَجنونا لأنه غَيْرَ مُخَاطَب إِلَّا أَنْ تُقَاتِلَ فَيُقْتُلُ دَفَعَالِرِهِ غَيْرَ أَنَّ الصَّبِيَّ وَ الْمَجْنُونَ يُقْتَلَان مَا دَامَا يُقَاتِلَانِ وَ غَيْرُهُمَا لَا بَأْسَ بِقَتلِهِ بَعْدَ الأَسرِ لِأَنَّهُ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْعِقَابِ لِتَوَجُهِ الْخِطَابِ نَحْوَهُ وَإِنْ كَانَ يَحِنُّ وَيُقِيقُ فَهُوَ فِي حَالِ إِفَاقَتِهِ كَالصَّحِيحِ
ترجمہ
اسی طرح مسلمانوں کو چاہئے کہ کسی دیوانہ کو بھی قتل نہ کریں کیونکہ اسے شریعت کی طرف سے کوئی خطاب نہیں ہے۔ البتہ اگر وہ لڑائی میں عملی حصہ دار ہو تو اسے بھی قتل کر دیا جائے گا تا کہ لوگ اس کے نقصان سے محفوظ رہیں۔ لیکن آئمہ اربعہ کے نزدیک بچہ اور دیوانہ کوقتل کرنا اس وقت تک جائز ہے جب تک وہ قتال میں شریک ہوں یعنی اگر وہ گرفتار کر لئے جائیں تو انہیں قتل نہیں کیا جائے اور ان کے علاوہ دوسرے لوگوں کو قید کے بعد بھی قتل کر لینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ لوگ بھی عذاب دیئے جانے کے مستحق ہو چکے ہیں اس لئے کہ ان کے عاقل اور بالغ ہو جانے کے بعد سے حکم الہی کے وہ بھی مخاطب بن چکے ہیں اور اگر کوئی مجنون ایسا ہو کہ کسی وقت اسے جنون رہتا ہو اور کسی وقت وہ اچھا ہو جاتا ہو تو اس کی تندرستی کی حالت میں اس پر تندرستی کا حکم نافذ ہوگا اور وہ بھی تندرست کے مثل ہو گا۔
Book of Siyar. 34. Ashraf al-Hidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 7. Such as when attacking a fortress or making a general raid against polytheists, if children or women become targets, there is no harm in that, and no accountability. As mentioned in the hadith of Sa'b ibn Jaththamah in Abu Dawud. And 'shaykh fani' refers to an old man who cannot fight. And when the lines face each other in battle, at that time he does not shout to incite people to fight, nor does he use tricks and tactics, nor is he a person of opinion in warfare. If he is such, he may also be killed. Thus, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) killed Warid ibn Samah who was 120 years old, because he was very clever and a person of opinion in military matters. The conclusion is that killing these people is only permissible when Muslims suffer harm from them, otherwise not. When is there leeway to kill the above-mentioned people? He (al-Quduri) said: 'Except if one of these is among those who have an opinion in warfare, or the woman is a queen due to her harm extending to the people, and likewise whoever fights among these is killed in repelling his evil, and because fighting is truly permissible.' Translation: Al-Quduri said: 'However, if any of these helpless people has opinion and tactics in warfare, or a woman is the queen (or leader) of her region, then killing her is permissible because her effect and harm reach the people and the general public.' Similarly, whoever among the mentioned people fights, he too will be killed to repel his evil, and also because the continuation of fighting itself makes his killing permissible. Likewise, a monk who is in his monastery (place of worship) or church, not mixing with the public, should not be killed. The insane should also not be killed in the battlefield. And do not kill an insane person because he is not legally addressed, unless he fights then he is killed to repel his evil. However, the boy and the insane are killed as long as they fight, but others (i.e., adult sane combatants) may be killed after capture because they are deserving of punishment due to the address of the law being directed towards them. And if he (the insane person) sometimes becomes sane and sometimes insane, then in his state of sanity he is like a sane person. Translation: Similarly, Muslims should not kill any insane person because he has no address from the Shari'ah. However, if he actively participates in fighting, then he will be killed so that people are safe from his harm. But according to the four imams, it is permissible to kill a boy and an insane person as long as they are participating in fighting; i.e., if they are captured, they are not killed. As for others, there is no harm in killing them after capture because they have become deserving of punishment since after becoming sane and adult, they have been addressed by divine command. And if an insane person is such that sometimes he is insane and sometimes he becomes well, then in his state of health the ruling of health applies to him and he is like a healthy person.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on the permissibility of killing non-combatants during jihad. The author begins by stating the general principle: it is not permissible to kill women, children, old men, monks, or the insane unless they pose a direct threat. The evidence includes a hadith from Abu Dawud (Sa'b ibn Jaththamah) and the precedent of the Prophet killing the elderly Warid ibn Samah because of his military expertise. The Arabic matn from al-Quduri specifies three exceptions: (1) a person who gives strategic counsel in warfare, (2) a woman who is a queen or leader whose harmful influence extends to people, and (3) anyone who actually fights. In such cases, killing is permitted to repel their evil. The commentary then addresses the insane: they are not legally responsible (mukhatab), so they should not be killed unless they physically fight. Once captured, however, sane adult combatants may be killed even after capture because they are liable for punishment. For an insane person who has lucid intervals, during his lucid state he is treated as sane. The passage concludes by emphasizing that the underlying rationale is protection from harm: killing is only justified when the non-combatant's actions or position cause harm to Muslims.

Key Terms
مخاطب (mukhatab): One who is addressed by the legal commands of the Shari'ah, i.e., accountable. The insane are not mukhatab, so they are not liable for punishment.
ملكة (malikah): A queen or female ruler whose decisions and influence cause harm to the people; such a woman may be killed in jihad.
رأي في الحرب (ra'y fi al-harb): Strategic opinion or counsel in warfare; a person who gives such advice may be killed even if not physically fighting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, under what condition is it permissible to kill a female non-combatant in jihad?
A) Always permissible
B) If she is old
C) If she is a queen or leader whose harm extends to people
D) Never permissible

Key Takeaway
Non-combatants are protected in Hanafi jihad law unless they actively fight, give strategic counsel, or rule harmfully.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules

Ruling on Killing One's Disbelieving Father in Battle
States the ruling on patricide in jihad with proof and exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a Muslim soldier initiating the killing of his own father in jihad and apply the exception for self-defense.

Core Idea
Initiating patricide in battle is makruh tahrimi, but self-defense makes it permissible.

This lesson examines a delicate fiqh scenario: the Muslim soldier facing his own disbelieving father in combat. The text balances filial duty with the exigencies of war, showing that while proactive killing is disliked, self-defense overrides it. We will unpack the ruling, its proof, and the critical exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is the mujahid initiating the killing of his own father who is among the polytheists. The default ruling is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
Makruh tahrimi is close to haram in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites two proofs: (1) Quranic verse Luqman 31:15 'accompany them with kindness' and (2) the son's obligation to provide nafaqah (maintenance) for his father, implying preservation of life.
The verse is qati' al-thubut but zanni al-dalalah in this context.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative of 'accompany with kindness' prohibits causing harm, especially killing, which is the utmost displeasure. Similarly, the duty of nafaqah contradicts proactive destruction.
4
Note the exception and its basis
If the father attacks the son and there is no way to repel him except by killing, then it is permissible (la ba'sa) because the son's intention is repulsion (daf') not aggression (ibtida). The text uses an analogy: if a Muslim father attacks his Muslim son, the son may kill in self-defense; here it is even more applicable.
The exception is based on necessity and the change of intention.
5
Apply the ruling
Practice with the given scenario: determine whether the son must avoid killing or may defend himself based on the father's actions and available options.
The applied task will reinforce the distinction.

Source Text

مجاہد اپنے باپ کو پیش قدمی کر کے قتل نہ کرے
کتاب
وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَبْتَدِئَ الرَّجُلُ أَبَاهُ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِيْنَ فَيَقْتُلَهُ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَصَاحِبُهُمَا فِي الدُّنْيَا مَعْرُوفًا وَ لأَنَّهُ يَحِبُّ عَلَيْهِ إِحَيَاؤُهُ بِالْإِنْفَاقِ فَيْنَا قِضَةُ الْإِطْلَاقُ فِي افْنَائِهِ
ترجمہ اور یہ بات مکروہ ہے کہ مجاہد پہل اور پیش قدمی کر کے اپنے باپ کو خود قتل کرے۔ اس فرمان باری تعالیٰ کی وجہ سے کہ وَصَاحِبُهُمَا فِي الدُّنْيَا مَعْرُوفًا یعنی دنیا میں اپنے والدین کے ساتھ اچھی طرح پر زندگی بسر کرو ( ۔ اس لئے اگر باپ مشرکوں کے ساتھ ہو کر مسلمانوں سے قتال کرنے کو آئے اور مجاہدین کی صف میں اس باپ کا بیٹا بھی موجود ہو تو اسی بات میں بھلائی ہے کہ اپنی طرف سے پیش قدمی کر کے اسے قتل نہ کرے ) اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ بیٹے پر یہ واجب ہے کہ نفقہ دے کر اپنے باپ کو زندہ رکھے اور بھوکا رکھ کر اسے نہ مرنے دے) ایسی صورت میں قصدا اور پیش قدمی کر کے اسے مار ڈالنے کی مطلق اجازت ہونا اس تقاضا کے خلاف ہوگا۔
باپ نے بیٹے کو اور بیٹے نے باپ کو پالیا اور آمنا سامنا ہو تو کیا کریں
فَإِنْ أَدْرَكَهُ امْتَنَعَ عَلَيْهِ حَتَّى يَقْتُلَهُ غَيْرُهُ لِأَنَّ الْمَقْصُرُدَ يَحْصُلُ بِغَيْرِهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ اقْتِحَامِهِ الْمَاثَمَ وَإِنْ قَصَدَ الْأَبُ قَبْلَهُ بِحَيْثُ لَا يُمْكِتُهُ دَفَعُهُ إِلَّا بِقَتِلِهِ لَا بَأْسَ بِهِ لِأَنَّ مَقْصُودَهُ الدَّفَعُ الأَتَرى انه لوشَهرَ الْابُ الْمُسْلِمُ سَيفَهُ عَلَى ابْنِهِ وَ لا يُمْكِنُهُ دَفَعُهُ إِلَّا بِقَتْلِهِ يَقْتُلُهُ لِمَائِينَا فَهُذَا أَوْلى
ترجمہ پھر اگر باپ نے بیٹے کو یا بیٹے نے اپنے باپ کو میدان جہاد میں پایا اور دونوں کا آمنا سامنا ہو گیا ۔ تو باپ کو وہیں پر روک رکھے خود اس پر حملہ نہ کرے یہاں تک کہ کوئی دوسرا شخص اسے قتل کر دے ( یعنی باپ یہ چاہتا ہو کہ اسے قتل کر دے لیکن بیٹے کے لئے اگر یہ ممکن ہو کہ خود کو اس سے بچا کر اسے قتل کر دے تو بیٹے کو چاہئے کہ کسی بھی طرح سے اسے لڑائی میں مشغول رکھے مثلاً اس کے گھوڑے کی ٹانگ کاٹ دے یا اسے گھوڑے پر سے گرا دے۔ یا کسی جگہ اسے مجبور کر کے روک کر رکھے یہاں تک کہ کوئی دوسرا مسلمان وہاں پر آ کر اسے قتل کر دے یہی حکم دوسرے محارم ماں ، دادا، دادی وغیرہ کا ہے۔ کیونکہ جو مقصود ہے اسے وہ خود نہ کر کے دوسرے کے ذریعے حاصل کر سکتا ہے اور اگر کافر باپ نے اسے قتل کرنا چاہا اور اس کو قتل کرنے کے سوا خود کو بچانے کی کوئی صورت اس بیٹے کے پاس نہ ہو تو ایسی صورت میں باپ کو قتل کر دینے میں بھی کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ایسی صورت میں اس مسلمان بیٹے کو اپنی ذات سے اس مصیبت کو دور کرنے اور خود کو بچانے کے سوا دوسری کوئی نیت نہیں ہے۔ کیا یہ بات سمجھ میں نہیں آتی ہے ( بلکہ ضرور آتی ہے ) کہ اگر کسی موقع میں مسلمان باپ بھی اپنے بیٹے پر اس کے قتل کرنے کی نیت سے تلوار کھینچ لے۔ اور بیٹا کسی صورت سے بھی خود کو اس سے نہیں بچا سکتا ہو سوائے اس کے خود سبقت کر کے باپ کو قتل کر دے تو اسے قتل کرنا جائز ہوتا ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے کہ اس لاچاری میں وہ خود کو اس خطرناک نقصان سے بچالے۔ پس یہاں کا فرباپ سے مقابلہ ہونے کی صورت میں تو بدرجہ اولی جائز ہوگا۔
تشریح فَإِنْ أَدْرَكَهُ الخ اگر میدان میں بیٹے کے لئے یہ ممکن نہ ہو کہ باپ کے حملہ میں خود کو اس سے بچا سکے ۔ تو از خود اس پر حملہ نہ کرلے بلکہ اسے کسی طرح اتنی دیر تک روک رکھے کہ کوئی دوسرا آ کر اسے قتل کر دے اور اگر یہ بھی ممکن نہ ہو اور اس کے حملہ سے بچنے کے لئے
A mujahid should not initiate killing his father. Book: It is makruh (disliked) for a man to initiate killing his father from among the polytheists, due to the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'And accompany them in this world with kindness' (Luqman 31:15), and because it is obligatory upon him to keep him alive through spending, so this would contradict the absolute permission in destroying him. Translation: It is makruh for a mujahid to take the initiative and himself kill his father, due to the command of Allah: 'and accompany them in this world with kindness', meaning live with your parents well in this world. So if the father comes among the polytheists to fight the Muslims, and the son is present in the ranks of the mujahideen, it is better that he does not take the initiative to kill him. And also because the son is obliged to keep his father alive by providing maintenance, and not to let him die by starving him. In such a case, giving absolute permission to intentionally and proactively kill him would contradict this requirement. What to do if father and son encounter each other? Then if he (the son) meets him (the father), he should restrain himself until someone else kills him, because the objective can be achieved by someone else without him committing sin. But if the father intends him first such that he cannot repel him except by killing him, then it is no problem, because his objective is repulsion. Do you not see that if a Muslim father draws his sword against his son and he cannot repel him except by killing him, he kills him due to what we have explained; so this (the case of the disbelieving father) is even more applicable. Translation: Then if the father meets the son or the son meets his father in the battlefield and they come face to face, then he should restrain the father there and not attack him until someone else kills him. (That is, the father wants to kill him, but if it is possible for the son to save himself and let someone else kill him, the son should engage him in fighting in some way, e.g., cut his horse's leg or throw him off the horse, or force him to stop somewhere, until another Muslim comes and kills him. The same ruling applies to other close relatives: mother, grandfather, grandmother, etc., because the objective can be achieved through someone else without him doing it himself.) But if the disbelieving father intends to kill him and there is no way for the son to save himself except by killing him, then in that case there is no harm in killing the father, because in such a situation the Muslim son has no intention other than repelling this calamity from himself and saving himself. Do you not understand (rather you do understand) that if on some occasion a Muslim father also draws his sword against his son with the intention of killing him, and the son cannot save himself except by taking the initiative and killing the father, then it is permissible for him to kill him, because in this helplessness he saves himself from this dangerous harm. So here, in the case of facing the father, it is all the more permissible. Explanation: 'then if he meets him...' etc. If in the battlefield it is not possible for the son to save himself from the father's attack, then he should not attack him himself, but rather delay him in some way until someone else comes and kills him. If that is also not possible and to save himself from his attack...
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage addresses the specific situation of a Muslim soldier encountering his own disbelieving father in battle. It begins by stating the ruling: it is makruh (disliked) for the son to initiate the killing of his father. The proof is the Quranic verse commanding kindness to parents in this world (Luqman 31:15) and the fact that the son is obligated to provide maintenance for his father, which implies preserving his life. Therefore, proactively killing him contradicts this duty. The text then provides guidance on what to do if they meet: the son should avoid killing his father himself if possible, for instance by disabling his horse or delaying him until another Muslim can kill him. This applies also to other close relatives. However, if the father actively attacks the son and the son cannot save himself except by killing his father, then it is permissible (la ba'sa bihi) for the son to kill him in self-defense. The rationale is that the son's intention is repulsion of harm, not patricide. The text reinforces this with an analogy: if a Muslim father were to attack his Muslim son, the son would be allowed to kill in self-defense; so here, with a disbelieving father, it is even more justified. The commentary explains that the same ruling applies to other mahram relatives.

Key Terms
ابتدا (ibtida): Initiating an action; here it means the son taking the first step to kill his father without being provoked.
دفع (daf'): Repelling harm; the son's intention in killing his father in self-defense is daf', not aggression.
مأثم (matham): Sin; the text says the son should avoid committing sin (ithm) by not killing his father unless necessary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Muslim soldier encounters his disbelieving father in battle and the father attacks him, what is the ruling?
A) He must let his father kill him
B) He may kill his father in self-defense
C) He should retreat
D) It is wajib to kill his father

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits initiating patricide but allows it in self-defense when necessary.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules

Imam's Authority to Make Truce with Enemy Combatants
Ruling on permissibility of truce based on benefit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on truce with enemy combatants and explain the Quranic and Sunnah proofs, including the role of maslahah.

Core Idea
A truce with the enemy is permissible only when it benefits the Muslims; otherwise it is forbidden.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of truce (muwada'ah) with enemy combatants. The text from Al-Hidayah establishes that the Imam may make peace when it serves Muslim interest, citing the Quran and the Prophet's treaty at Hudaybiyyah. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the conditional nature of permissibility based on maslahah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act is the Imam making a truce (muwada'ah) with enemy combatants. The condition is that it must be beneficial (maslahah) for the Muslims.
The ruling is conditional on benefit, not absolute.
2
Locate the primary proof (Quran)
The text cites Quran 8:61: 'And if they incline to peace, then incline to it and rely upon Allah.' The command indicates permissibility.
The Hanafi school interprets this as an option, not an obligation, because the context is fighting.
3
Examine the secondary proof (Sunnah)
The Prophet's treaty at Hudaybiyyah for ten years demonstrates the permissibility in practice.
The Prophet's action confirms the Quranic permission.
4
Understand the extension of the ruling (ta'diya al-ma'na)
The duration of the truce is not restricted to ten years; the underlying rationale (repelling evil) extends to longer periods if benefit exists.
The ruling is based on meaning, not just the specific historical term.
5
Identify the boundary (when truce becomes impermissible)
If there is no benefit, the truce is forbidden because it constitutes abandoning jihad in form and meaning.
The condition of benefit is decisive.

وَإِذَا رَأَى الْإِمَامُ أَنْ تُصَالِحَ أَهْلَ الْحَرْبِ أَوْ فَرِيقًا مِّنْهُمْ وَ كَانَ فِي ذَالِكَ مَصْلَحَةً لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ فَلَا بَأْسَ بِهِ لِقَوله تَعَالَى وَإِن جَنَحُوا اللسَّلْمِ فَاجْنَحْ لَهَا وَتَوَكَّلْ عَلَى اللهِ وَ وَادَعَ رَسُولُ اللهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَهْلَ مَكَةَ عَامَ الْحُدَيْبِيَّةِ عَلى أَنْ يَضَعَ الْحَرْبُ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَهُمْ عَشَرَ سِنِينَ وَلِأَنَّ الْمُوَادَعَةَ جِهَادُ مَعْنَى إِذَا كَانَ خَيْراً لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ لاَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ وَهُوَ دَفَعُ الشَّرِ حَاصِل بِهِ وَلَا يَقْتَصِرُ الْحُكمُ عَلَى الْمُدَّةِ الْمَرْوِيَّةِ لِتَعَدَّى الْمَعْنَى إِلَى مَازَادَ عَلَيْهَا بِخِلَافِ مَإِذَا لَمْ تَكُنْ خَيْرُ الأَنَّهُ تَرْك الْجِهَادِ صُورَةً وَمَعْنَى
ترجمہ اگر امام نے مسلمانوں کے حق میں دشمنوں سے یا ان کے کسی فریق سے صلح کر لینے ہی میں مصلحت سمجھی اور واقعتا ایسا کرنے میں مسلمانوں کے حق میں بہتری ہو تو ایسا کر لینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے وَإِنْ جَنَحُوا لِلسّلْمِ فَاجْنَحْ لَهَا وَ توَكَّلْ عَلَی اللہ یعنی اگر کافروں کی جماعت مسلمانوں سے صلح کر لینے کے لئے جھک جائے تو اے نبی آپ ان سے مصالحت کے لئے جھک جائیں اور اللہ تعالیٰ پر توکل کرلیں اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حدیبیہ کے سال میں مکہ والوں کے ساتھ دس برس تک کے لئے اس شرط پر مصالحت کی تھی کہ آپ کے اور کافروں کے درمیان لڑائی بند رہے گی ۔ رواہ ابو داؤد واحمد وغیرہ ۔ اور اس دلیل سے بھی جائز ہے کہ مصالحت کرنی بھی جہاد ہی کے حکم میں ہے مگر باطنی طور پر بشر طیکہ وہ مسلمانوں کے واسطے بہتر ہو۔ کیونکہ جہاد کا مقصد شر کو دور کرنا ہوتا ہے اور وہ اس سے حاصل ہوتا ہے۔ واضح ہو کہ ایک روایت میں مصالحت کی مدت جو دس برس لکھی گئی ہے وہ صلح کے جائز ہونے کی ہے لیکن اتنی ہی کا ہونا ضروری بھی نہیں ہے جس معنی کی بناء پر جائز کہا گیا ہے وہ معنی اس سے زیادہ مدت میں بھی پائے جاتے ہیں۔ یعنی اگر دس برس سے زیادہ مصالحت کرنے میں بھی مسلمانوں کا فائدہ ہو تو وہ بھی جائز ہوگی لیکن اگر مسلمانوں کے حق میں مصالحت میں فائدہ اور مصلحت نہ ہو تو وہ جائز نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس دوسری صورت میں جبکہ وہ مسلمانوں کے لئے مفید نہ ہو جہاد کا ظاہری اور باطنی دونوں طور پر چھوڑ نا لازم آتا ہے۔
تشریح دشمنوں سے مصالحت کرنے میں اگر مسلمانوں کے لئے فائدہ ہو تو بالاتفاق تمام فقہاء کے نزدیک جائز ہے اسی طرح اگر مصلحت نہ ہو تو بالا تفاق جائز نہیں ہے۔ بیٹی نے کہا ہے کہ صلح حدیبیہ میں کفار قریش سے جو مصالحت ہوئی تھی اس سلسلہ میں کئی اور روایتوں میں دو برس کی مدت بیان کی گئی ہے۔ اس سے مراد ہی مدت ہے جس میں وہ مصالحت باقی رہی اور اس پر عمل ہو اور نہ اصل میں مصالحت تو دس برسوں کے لئے ہوئی تھی۔ اور بیٹی کا یہ کلام بہت بہتر ہے۔ جس کی وجہ یہ ہوئی کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے حمایت میں بنوخزاعہ تھے۔ اس لئے قریش نے اپنے حلیف بنو بکر کی مدد کر کے خزاعہ پر حملہ کر دیا۔ اس طرح جب قریش نے اس عہد کو توڑ دیا تو رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے چڑھائی کر کے مکہ فتح کر لیا۔ اور یہ واقعہ دو برس کے بعد ہوا
Translation: If the Imam sees that making peace with the warring party or a faction of them is beneficial for the Muslims, there is no harm in it, because Allah says: 'And if they incline to peace, then incline to it and rely upon Allah' (Quran 8:61). The Messenger of Allah (saw) made a truce with the people of Mecca in the year of Hudaybiyyah on the condition that war be suspended between them for ten years. And because muwada'ah (truce) is jihad in meaning when it is good for the Muslims, since the objective—repelling evil—is achieved by it. The ruling is not restricted to the reported period (ten years) because the underlying meaning extends beyond it. Contrary to when it is not good, because then it would be abandoning jihad both in form and meaning. 
 Commentary: If the Imam considers it in the interest of Muslims to make peace with the enemies or a group of them, and indeed there is benefit in it for the Muslims, then doing so is permissible. Because Allah says: 'And if they incline to peace...' meaning if the group of disbelievers inclines to make peace with the Muslims, O Prophet, you also incline to peace with them and trust in Allah. The Prophet (saw) made a truce with the people of Mecca in the year of Hudaybiyyah for ten years on the condition that war would cease between him and them. It is narrated by Abu Dawud and Ahmad, among others. It is also permissible because making peace is in the category of jihad, but inwardly, provided it is better for the Muslims. The purpose of jihad is to repel evil, and that is achieved by peace. Note: The reported period of ten years is for the permissibility of peace; it is not necessary that it be only that duration. The underlying meaning for permissibility is found in longer periods as well. If making peace for more than ten years benefits the Muslims, it is permissible. But if there is no benefit or interest in peace for the Muslims, it is not permissible, because in that case it would amount to abandoning jihad both outwardly and inwardly. 
 Explanation: Making peace with enemies is unanimously permissible among all jurists if there is benefit for the Muslims. Similarly, if there is no benefit, it is unanimously impermissible. Al-Bayhaqi stated that in some narrations, the duration of the Hudaybiyyah treaty is mentioned as two years. This refers to the period during which the treaty remained effective, not the original term, which was ten years. Al-Bayhaqi's statement is sound. The reason is that Banu Khuza'ah were allies of the Prophet (saw), so Quraysh attacked them with the help of their allies Banu Bakr, thereby breaking the treaty. Then the Prophet (saw) marched and conquered Mecca. This happened after two years.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling from the Hidayah on the permissibility of truce (muwada'ah) with enemy combatants. The matn states that if the Imam deems it beneficial, there is no objection. The proof is from the Quran (Al-Anfal 8:61) which commands accepting peace if the enemy inclines to it, and from the Sunnah of the Prophet's treaty of Hudaybiyyah. The commentary explains that truce is considered 'jihad in meaning' because it achieves the same objective of repelling evil. The duration of the truce is not restricted to the ten years of the Prophet's treaty; the underlying rationale (ta'diya al-ma'na) allows for longer terms if benefit exists. If there is no benefit, peace is forbidden because it would be abandoning jihad entirely. The commentary also resolves a discrepancy in narrations about the duration of Hudaybiyyah: some mention two years, but that refers to the time it was actually observed before being broken by Quraysh. The passage emphasizes the importance of maslahah (public interest) in such decisions.

Key Terms
موادعة (muwada'ah): A truce or peace treaty with enemy combatants, synonymous with musalahah.
مصلحت (maslahah): Public interest or benefit that justifies the truce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary textual evidence for the permissibility of truce with enemy combatants?
A) The hadith of Hudaybiyyah only
B) The Quranic verse 8:61 and the Prophet's treaty with Quraysh
C) Ijma' of the Companions
D) Qiyas on other contracts

Key Takeaway
A truce with enemy combatants is permissible only when it serves the benefit of the Muslims; otherwise it is forbidden.

Breaking a Truce: The Obligation of Prior Notification
Ruling on when and how an Imam may break a truce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on breaking a truce and explain why prior notification (nabdh) is wajib.

Core Idea
An Imam must notify the enemy before breaking a truce; sudden treachery is prohibited.

This lesson examines a critical aspect of Islamic international law: the rules of breaking a truce. The Hanafi school emphasizes that even when breaking a treaty is beneficial, the Imam cannot act unilaterally without warning. The passage grounds this in the Prophet's sunnah and the principle of avoiding treachery (ghadr). By the end, you will understand the legal procedure and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon (breaking a truce) and its legal classification (wajib with conditions).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary proof cited: the Prophet's nullification of the Hudaybiyyah treaty and his hadith about no treachery.
Both the action and the explicit hadith are used.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the dalil proves the need for notification. The Prophet's throwing back (nabdh) shows it is a required step; the hadith prohibits treachery, which notification avoids.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may not emphasize the grace period, but Hanafi insists on a period enabling news to reach the enemy's population.
The ikhtilaf is over the necessity of allowing time, not notification itself.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The requirement of prior notification is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position, supported by the Prophet's practice and the need to avoid treachery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ إِنْ صَالحَهُمُ مُدَّةً ثُمَّ رَأى نَقْضَ الصُّلح أَنْفَعَ نَبَذَالَيْهِمُ الاِمَامُ وَقَاتَلَهُمْ لأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ نَبَذَالْمُوَادَعَةَ الَّتِي كَانَتْ بَيْنَهُ وَ بَيْنَ اَهْلِ مَكَّةَ وَلانَّ الْمَصْلَحَةَ لَمَّا تَبَدَّلَتْ كَان النَّبذُ جِهَادًا وَايْفَاءُ الْعَهْدِ تَرُكُ الْجِهَادِ صُورَةً وَمَعَنِّى فَلَابُدَّ مِنَ النَّبدِ تَحَرُّزًا عَنِ الْعَدْرِ وَ قَدْ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِي الْعُهُودِ وَفَاء لَا غَدْرٌ وَ لَا بُدَّمِنِ اعْتِبَارِ مُدَّةٍ يُبْلُغُ فِيهَا خَبَرُ النَّبذِإِلَى جَمْعِهِمْ وَيُكَتَفى فِى ذَالِكَ بِمُضِيّ مُدَّةٍ يَتَمَكَّنُ مَلِكُهُمْ بَعْدَ عِلْمِهِ بِالنَّبِذِمِنُ إِنْفَاذِ الْخَبَرِ إِلَى أَطْرَافِ مَمْلَكَتِهِ لأنَّ بِذَالِكَ يَنتَفِي الْغَدْرُ
ترجمہ اور اگر امام مسلمین نے کافروں سے کسی خاص معین مدت کے لئے صلح کی مگر بعد میں اس نے اس معاہدہ کے توڑ ڈالنے میں مصلحت مجبھی تو امام کو چاہئے کہ عہد توڑ ڈالنے کی خبر کافروں کو پہلے کر دے پھر ان سے قتال کرے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس عہد کو جو آپ کے اور کفار قریش کے درمیان ہوا تھا ان کفار پر پھینک دیا ( توڑ دیا) اور قریش کو اس سے مطلع کر دیا ( یعنی معاہدہ کے ڈیڑھ برس کے بعد قریش مکہ نے بنو بکر کے ساتھ ہو کر بد عہدی کرتے ہوئے اس قبیلہ خزاعہ پر حملہ کر دیا تھا جو رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے جانبدار اور حلیف تھے تب آپ نے بھی ان کا عبدان پر پھینک مارا۔ اور لڑائی کا سامان کر کے مکہ پر چڑھائی کر دی ۔ جیسا کہ بیہقی وغیرہ نے اس کی روایت کی ہے) اور اس دلیل سے کہ جب مسلمانوں کی مصلحت بدل گئی تو عہد کو پھینک دینا جہاد ہے۔ اور عہد کو پورا کرنا ظاہر و باطن ترک جہاد ہے۔
And if he (the Imam) made a truce with them for a specified period, and then he sees that breaking the truce is more beneficial, the Imam should throw (the treaty) back to them and fight them, because the Prophet (saw) threw back the truce that was between him and the people of Mecca. And because when the benefit changed, throwing back becomes jihad, while fulfilling the treaty would be abandoning jihad in form and meaning. So he must throw it back to avoid treachery. The Prophet (saw) said regarding treaties: 'Fulfillment, no treachery.' It is necessary to consider a period in which the news of the throwing back reaches their assembly, and it is sufficient to allow a period that enables their king, after knowing of the throwing back, to send the news to the extremities of his kingdom, because by that treachery is avoided. Translation: If the Imam of the Muslims made a truce with the disbelievers for a specific period, but later he sees benefit in breaking the treaty, the Imam should first inform the disbelievers of the nullification and then fight them. Because the Prophet (saw) threw back the treaty that was between him and the Quraysh (i.e., broke it) and informed them (meaning: one and a half years into the treaty, the Quraysh, with Banu Bakr, treacherously attacked Banu Khuza'ah, who were allies of the Prophet, so the Prophet threw back the treaty and prepared to march on Mecca, as narrated by al-Bayhaqi and others). And with this evidence: when the benefit changed, throwing back becomes jihad, and fulfilling the treaty would be abandoning jihad both outwardly and inwardly.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where a truce is already in place but the Imam later finds it more beneficial to break it. The Hanafi ruling is that the Imam must first formally nullify the treaty by notifying the enemy (nabdh) before attacking. This is based on the Prophet's action when Quraysh violated the Hudaybiyyah treaty: he announced its nullification before marching on Mecca. The reasoning is that fulfilling a treaty when it is no longer beneficial would be abandoning jihad (which is obligatory), so breaking it becomes an act of jihad. However, to avoid treachery (ghadr), a sufficient period must be allowed for the enemy's leadership to be informed. The Prophet's hadith emphasizes fulfilling treaties without treachery, so notification is essential. The duration of this grace period is determined by practical feasibility: enough time for the enemy king to send word to all corners of his kingdom. This ensures that the Muslims are not guilty of treachery.

Key Terms
نبذ (nabdh): The act of formally nullifying a treaty by throwing it back to the enemy, i.e., announcing its termination.
غدر (ghadr): Treachery or breach of trust; the Prophet prohibited ghadr in treaties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must the Imam do before breaking a truce to avoid treachery?
A) He must gather the Muslims for consultation.
B) He must launch a surprise attack.
C) He must notify the enemy of the nullification and allow time for the news to spread.
D) He must wait until the treaty period expires.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires prior notification (nabdh) and sufficient time for the enemy to be informed before breaking a truce, to avoid treachery.

Revoking a Peace Treaty: Conditions and Procedure in Hanafi Fiqh
Explaining when and how an imam may revoke a peace treaty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for revoking a peace treaty and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) requiring notification and sufficient time.

Core Idea
A treaty may be revoked for greater benefit, but only with formal notice and time for the news to spread.

Peace treaties with disbelievers are a form of jihad in the Hanafi school, aimed at repelling harm. This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses when and how such a treaty may be revoked. Understanding the balance between fulfilling covenants (wafa') and pursuing maslahah (benefit) is key, as is the ethical imperative to avoid treachery (ghadr). This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof from the Sunnah, and the practical steps required of the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the revocation (naqd) of a peace treaty (sulh) with disbelievers. The ruling is ja'iz (permissible) but conditional on benefit and proper notification.
The text states: 'وَ إِنْ صَالحَهُمُ مُدَّةً ثُمَّ رَأى نَقْضَ الصُّلح أَنْفَعَ نَبَذَالَيْهِمُ الاِمَامُ وَقَاتَلَهُمْ'.
2
Locate the dalil
What proofs are cited? The action of the Prophet ﷺ in abrogating the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah and the hadith: 'الْعُهُودِ وَفَاء لَا غَدْرٌ' (fulfillment, not treachery).
The Prophet’s precedent and the hadith together establish the permissibility and the requirement of notice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How do these proofs yield the ruling? The Prophet's action shows that treaties can be terminated when benefit changes. The hadith prohibits treachery, so notification is required to avoid it.
The imam must give nabdh (notice) and allow a time period for the news to spread.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement? Yes, some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require that the enemy breach the treaty first. The Hanafi position allows revocation based on change of benefit (maslahah).
The Hanafi position is broader, focusing on the imam's judgment of benefit.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
Which position is relied upon? The text’s position—notification and sufficient period—is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, supported by the Sunnah and the story of Mu‘awiyah.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and affirmed by later authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہفتم جھک جائیں اور اللہ تعالیٰ پر توکل کرلیں اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حدیبیہ کے سال میں مکہ والوں کے ساتھ دس برس تک کے لئے اس شرط پر مصالحت کی تھی کہ آپ کے اور کافروں کے درمیان لڑائی بند رہے گی ۔ رواہ ابو داؤد واحمد وغیرہ ۔ اور اس دلیل سے بھی جائز ہے کہ مصالحت کرنی بھی جہاد ہی کے حکم میں ہے مگر باطنی طور پر بشرطیکہ وہ مسلمانوں کے واسطے بہتر ہو۔ کیونکہ جہاد کا مقصد شر کو دور کرنا ہوتا ہے اور وہ اس سے حاصل ہوتا ہے۔ واضح ہو کہ ایک روایت میں مصالحت کی مدت جو دس برس لکھی گئی ہے وہ صلح کے جائز ہونے کی ہے لیکن اتنی ہی کا ہونا ضروری بھی نہیں ہے جس معنی کی بناء پر جائز کہا گیا ہے وہ معنی اس سے زیادہ مدت میں بھی پائے جاتے ہیں۔ یعنی اگر دس برس سے زیادہ مصالحت کرنے میں بھی مسلمانوں کا فائدہ ہو تو وہ بھی جائز ہوگی لیکن اگر مسلمانوں کے حق میں مصالحت میں فائدہ اور مصلحت نہ ہو تو وہ جائز نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس دوسری صورت میں جبکہ وہ مسلمانوں کے لئے مفید نہ ہو جہاد کا ظاہری اور باطنی دونوں طور پر چھوڑ نا لازم آتا ہے۔ تشریح دشمنوں سے مصالحت کرنے میں اگر مسلمانوں کے لئے فائدہ ہو تو بالاتفاق تمام فقہاء کے نزدیک جائز ہے اسی طرح اگر مصلحت نہ ہو تو بالا تفاق جائز نہیں ہے۔ بیٹی نے کہا ہے کہ صلح حدیبیہ میں کفار قریش سے جو مصالحت ہوئی تھی اس سلسلہ میں کئی اور روایتوں میں دو برس کی مدت بیان کی گئی ہے۔ اس سے مراد ہی مدت ہے جس میں وہ مصالحت باقی رہی اور اس پر عمل ہو اور نہ اصل میں مصالحت تو دس برسوں کے لئے ہوئی تھی۔ اور بیٹی کا یہ کلام بہت بہتر ہے۔ جس کی وجہ یہ ہوئی کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے حمایت میں بنوخزاعہ تھے۔ اس لئے قریش نے اپنے حلیف بنو بکر کی مدد کر کے خزاعہ پر حملہ کر دیا۔ اس طرح جب قریش نے اس عہد کو توڑ دیا تو رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے چڑھائی کر کے مکہ فتح کر لیا۔ اور یہ واقعہ دو برس کے بعد ہوا نہ صلح کر کے مدت معینہ کے بعد صلح کو توڑنے کا حکم وَ إِنْ صَالحَهُمُ مُدَّةً ثُمَّ رَأى نَقْضَ الصُّلح أَنْفَعَ نَبَذَالَيْهِمُ الاِمَامُ وَقَاتَلَهُمْ لأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ نَبَذَالْمُوَادَعَةَ الَّتِي كَانَتْ بَيْنَهُ وَ بَيْنَ اَهْلِ مَكَّةَ وَلانَّ الْمَصْلَحَةَ لَمَّا تَبَدَّلَتْ كَان النَّبذُ جِهَادًا وَايْفَاءُ الْعَهْدِ تَرُكُ الْجِهَادِ صُورَةً وَمَعَنِّى فَلَابُدَّ مِنَ النَّبدِ تَحَرُّزًا عَنِ الْعَدْرِ وَ قَدْ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِي الْعُهُودِ وَفَاء لَا غَدْرٌ وَ لَا بُدَّمِنِ اعْتِبَارِ مُدَّةٍ يُبْلُغُ فِيهَا خَبَرُ النَّبذِإِلَى جَمْعِهِمْ وَيُكَتَفى فِى ذَالِكَ بِمُضِيّ مُدَّةٍ يَتَمَكَّنُ مَلِكُهُمْ بَعْدَ عِلْمِهِ بِالنَّبِذِمِنُ إِنْفَاذِ الْخَبَرِ إِلَى أَطْرَافِ مَمْلَكَتِهِ لأنَّ بِذَالِكَ يَنتَفِي الْغَدْرُ ترجمہ اور اگر امام مسلمین نے کافروں سے کسی خاص معین مدت کے لئے صلح کی مگر بعد میں اس نے اس معاہدہ کے توڑ ڈالنے میں مصلحت مجبھی تو امام کو چاہئے کہ عہد توڑ ڈالنے کی خبر کافروں کو پہلے کر دے پھر ان سے قتال کرے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس عہد کو جو آپ کے اور کفار قریش کے درمیان ہوا تھا ان کفار پر پھینک دیا ( توڑ دیا) اور قریش کو اس سے مطلع کر دیا ( یعنی معاہدہ کے ڈیڑھ برس کے بعد قریش مکہ نے بنو بکر کے ساتھ ہو کر بد عہدی کرتے ہوئے اس قبیلہ خزاعہ پر حملہ کر دیا تھا جو رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے جانبدار اور حلیف تھے تب آپ نے بھی ان کا عبدان پر پھینک مارا۔ اور لڑائی کا سامان کر کے مکہ پر چڑھائی کر دی ۔ جیسا کہ بیہقی وغیرہ نے اس کی روایت کی ہے) اور اس دلیل سے کہ جب مسلمانوں کی مصلحت بدل گئی تو عہد کو پھینک دینا جہاد ہے۔ اور عہد کو پورا کرنا ظاہر و باطن ترک جہاد ہے۔ حالانکہ ظاہر و باطن دونوں طرح ترک جہاد جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے عہد کوختم کر دینا ہی ضروری ہوا۔ ختم کر دینے کے معنی یہ ہوتے ہیں کہ کافروں کو پہلے سے مطلع کر دیا جائے ہم نے تم سے کئے ہوئے عہد کو اب ختم کر دیا ہے تا کہ غداری اور بدعہدی نہ ہو ۔ حالانکہ رسول اللہ نے عہود کے بارے میں فرمایا ہے کہ عہد وفا ہے اور غدر نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ ابن ماجہ نے اس کی روایت کی ہے اور عہد ختم کرنے کے موقع پر اتنی مدت درمیان میں ہونی ضروری ہے جس میں تمام کافروں کو معاہدہ کے ختم ہونے کی خبر پہنچ سکے اور وہ دھو کہ میں یا بے خبر نہ ر ہیں۔ مگر اس کے لئے حقیقت سب کو مطلع ہو جانا بھی ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ صرف اتنی مدت کا گذر جانا کافی ہے کہ کافروں کا بادشاہ یا راجہ اس معاہدہ کے ختم ہو جانے سے خود واقف ہو کر اپنے تمام علاقوں میں خبر پہنچا سکے ایسا کر دینے سے بد عہدی کا الزام نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح وَلَا بُدَّمِنِ اعْتِبَارِ مُدَّةٍ الخ اگر امام المسلمین مسلمانوں کے فائدہ کے پیش نظر کافروں سے مصالحت کرنا چاہے تو کرسکتا ہے۔ اس طرح اگر مصالحت کے بعد کسی وجہ سے اس معاہدہ کو ختم کر دینا چاہے تو اس کی بھی اسے اجازت ہے ۔ البتہ یہ ضروری ہے کہ کافروں کے سرداروں کو اس کی اطلاع بھی کر دے تا کہ بد عہدی اور غداری کا ہم پر الزام نہ ہو اور وہ غفلت میں پڑے نہ رہیں۔ ساتھ ہی اتنا وقت بھی ان کو دیا جائے جس میں خبر ان کے ہاں پھیل سکے پھر خبر خواہ پھیلے یا نہ پھیلے اس کی ذمہ داری نہ ہوگی ۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ جب کافروں کے بادشاہ کو یہ خبر دیدی گئی کہ ہم نے عہد توڑ دیا ہے تو اس کے بعد فورا ہی حملہ نہ کر دے کیونکہ وہ لوگ اس معاہدہ کی بنا پر دھو کہ میں لڑائی سے غافل رہیں گے ایسی صورت میں حملہ کرنا بد عہدی ہوگی بلکہ اتنی مدت بھی متعین کر دی جائے کہ وہ کفار اس سے باخبر ہو سکیں۔ لیکن ان سب کو خبر ہوئی یا نہیں اس کی خبر نہیں ہو سکتی ہے اس لئے اتنی مدت کا گذر جانا ہی کافی ہوگا۔ کہ جس میں کافروں کا بادشاہ اپنے ملک کے تمام علاقوں میں اس خبر سے سب کو مطلع کر سکتا ہو۔ چنانچہ امیر معاویہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ نے کفار روم کے ساتھ معاہدہ کیا پھر لشکر کو لے کر ان کا فروں کی طرف روانہ ہو گئے ۔ پھر عہد کے توڑنے کی خبر دینے کے ساتھ ہی ان پر حملہ بھی کر دینا چاہا۔ اتنے میں ایک شخص پیچھے سے گھوڑا دوڑاتے ہوئے یہ کہتا ہوا آیا کہ الله اكبر، الله أكبرُ، وَفَاء لَا غَدْرُ ۔ اس پر مڑ کر ان کو دیکھا تو وہ عمر وابن عنبہ تھے۔ معاویہ رضی اللہ عنہ نے ان سے پوچھا کہ کیا بات ہے تو فرمایا کہ میں نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے سنا ہے کہ جس شخص سے کسی قوم کے درمیان معاہدہ ہو تو وہ اس مدت کے اندر کوئی گرہ مضبوط نہ کرے اور نہ کھولے (معاہدہ میں ذرہ برابر کمی و بیشی نہ کرے ) یہاں تک کہ وہ مدت گذر جائے ۔ یا عہد توڑنے کی اطلاع برابری کے ساتھ ان کو بھی دے۔ پس یہ سن کر معاویہ رضی اللہ عنہ اپنا لشکر لے کر لوٹ آئے۔ ( رواه احمد ، ابو داود والترندی والنسائی وابن ماجه وابن حبان ) اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ مدت کے درمیان حملہ کا سامان نہ کرے مگر اس طرح سے کہ ان کو بھی اطلاع دیدے تا کہ وہ لوگ بھی سامان کر سکیں۔
And if the imam made a peace treaty with them for a specified period, then he saw that breaking the treaty is more beneficial, the imam should throw (the treaty) back to them and fight them, because the Prophet ﷺ threw back the peace treaty that was between him and the people of Makkah, and because when the benefit changed, the throwing back became jihad, and fulfilling the covenant is abandoning jihad in form and meaning. So it is necessary to throw it back to avoid treachery. And the Prophet ﷺ said regarding covenants: 'Fulfillment, not treachery.' And it is necessary to observe a period in which the news of the throwing back reaches their gathering, and it is sufficient in that for a period to pass in which their king, after knowing of the throwing back, is able to send the news to the farthest parts of his kingdom, because by that treachery is removed.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm wa dalil) from the Hanafi school regarding the revocation of a peace treaty with disbelieving enemies. The author begins by stating the condition: if the imam has made a peace treaty for a specific period, but later finds that breaking the treaty brings more benefit to the Muslims, he is permitted to abrogate it. However, he must first give notice (al-nabdh) to the enemy—that is, publicly annul the treaty and inform them—before engaging in combat. The proof is the precedent of the Prophet ﷺ in the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah: when the Quraysh breached the treaty by attacking the Banu Khuza‘ah (allies of the Muslims), the Prophet ﷺ declared the treaty null and then conquered Makkah. The legal reasoning (ta‘lil) is that when the benefit changes, upholding the treaty amounts to abandoning jihad in both form and essence, which is not permissible. Therefore, abrogation becomes necessary. To avoid treachery (ghadr), the imam must ensure that the enemy is notified and given sufficient time for the news to spread. The measure is the minimum time needed for the enemy king to inform all parts of his kingdom. This is illustrated by the story of Mu‘awiyah (radiyallahu ‘anhu), who learned from ‘Amr ibn ‘Anbasah that the Prophet forbade attacking during a treaty without notice. Hence, the lesson emphasizes that while treaties are binding (wafa’ la ghadr), they can be revoked for overriding benefit, provided proper notification is given to avoid deception.

Key Terms
النَّبْذ (al-nabdh): The act of throwing back or abrogating a treaty by formal notice to the other party.
الغَدْر (al-ghadr): Treachery or breach of covenant without justification.
مُدَّة (muddah): A specified period of time for a treaty; also the period needed for notification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must the imam do before fighting after revoking a peace treaty?
A) Attack immediately to gain surprise.
B) Give notice to the enemy and allow time for the news to spread.
C) Wait for the treaty period to expire naturally.
D) Seek permission from the enemy king.

Key Takeaway
A peace treaty with disbelievers may be revoked for overriding benefit, but only after formal notice and a sufficient grace period to avoid treachery.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
6 min
Fighting Disbelievers Without Notice: Collective Betrayal
Clarifying the imam's right to fight without notice when betrayal is collective.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi conditions for fighting disbelievers without prior notice when a treaty is breached, distinguishing collective betrayal from individual unauthorized acts.

Core Idea
Only unanimous collective betrayal permits immediate retaliation; rogue acts require investigation.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a critical nuance in the law of jihad: when can the imam strike without formally dissolving the treaty? The answer hinges on whether the breach is truly collective or merely the action of a few. Understanding this distinction prevents unjust warfare and preserves the integrity of treaties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The imam may fight without prior notice (nabdh) if the disbelievers initiate betrayal (خيانة) by unanimous agreement (بِاتِّفَاقِهِمْ).
The ruling is ja'iz (permissible) under this condition.
2
Analyze the Condition: Unanimous Agreement
The text uses 'bi-ittifaqihim' – meaning the entire group collectively decides and acts. Mere individual or group action without consensus does not suffice.
Hanafis require widespread complicity, not isolated incidents.
3
Contrast with Individual Acts
If a band of highway robbers (with no military strength) attacks, it is not a breach of the treaty for the whole group. If they have military strength and fight openly, it is a breach only for themselves, unless the king authorized them.
Authorization by the king makes the act collective by implication.
4
Understand the Role of Authorization
Without the king's permission, even an armed group's open warfare does not bind the entire community. With permission, the entire group becomes liable because it is 'by their unanimous agreement in meaning'.
This prevents attributing rogue actions to the whole state.
5
Identify the Proof
The ruling is based on qiyas jaliy (clear analogy): when they unanimously betray, they have already nullified the covenant, so there is no need to nullify it again. This is derived from the principle of reciprocity and avoiding treachery.
The proof is rational (dalil aqli) within the framework of treaty law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كفار نقض عہد میں پہل کریں تو امام بھی ان سے مقابلہ کرے قَالَ وَ إِنْ بَدَوْا بِخِيَانَةٍ قَاتَلَهُمْ وَلَمْ يَنْبُذْ إِلَيْهِمْ إِذَا كَانَ ذَلِكَ بِاتِّفَاقِهِمْ لِأَنَّهُمْ صَارُوا نَاقِضِينَ لِلْعَهْدِ فَلَا حَاجَةَ إِلَى نَقْضِهِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا دَخَلَتْ جَمَاعَةٌ مِنْهُمْ فَقَطَعُوا الطَّرِيقَ وَلَا مَنْعَةَ لَهُمْ حَيْثُ لَا يَكُونُ هَذَا نَقْضًا لِلْعَهْدِ وَلَوْ كَانَتْ لَهُمْ مَنْعَةٌ وَقَاتَلُوا الْمُسْلِمِينَ عَلَانِيَةً يَكُونُ نَقْضًا لِلْعَهْدِ فِي حَقِّهِمْ دُونَ غَيْرِهِمْ لِأَنَّهُ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِ مَلِكِهِمْ فَفِعْلُهُمْ لَا يَلْزَمُ غَيْرَهُمْ حَتَّى لَوْ كَانَ بِإِذْنِ مَلِكِهْمْ صَارُوا نَافِضِينَ لِلْعَهْدِ لِأَنَّهُ بِاتِّفَاقِهِمْ مَعْنَى
He said: And if they begin with treachery, he fights them and does not throw (the treaty) back to them if that (treachery) is by their unanimous agreement, because they have become breakers of the covenant, so there is no need to break it. Contrary to the case when a group of them enters and cuts the road, and they have no military strength; then this is not a breach of the covenant. And if they have military strength and fight the Muslims openly, it is a breach of the covenant in their right alone, not others, because it is without the permission of their king; so their action does not bind others. Even if it is with the permission of their king, they become breakers of the covenant, because it is by their unanimous agreement in meaning.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi ruling (from the matn) that explains the imam's response when disbelievers initiate breach of the treaty. The key distinction is based on collective versus individual action. If the entire group (bi-ittifaqihim) jointly commits an act of betrayal, such as attacking Muslims, then the treaty is considered broken by them, and the imam may fight them immediately without prior notice (nabdh). This is because they have already nullified the treaty by their actions. However, if only a band of individuals from among them commit an act of highway robbery (qata' al-tariq) and they have no power (man'ah), this is not considered a breach of the treaty by the entire group. If those individuals have power and openly fight Muslims, the breach applies only to them individually, not to the whole community, because they acted without the king's authorization. Thus, the imam cannot attack the entire group based on the actions of a few. But if the king authorizes them, then the entire group becomes liable because it is as if the king collectively agreed to the breach. The commentary on this passage (from Ashraf al-Hidayah) further explains these nuances.

Key Terms
اتِّفَاق (ittifāq): Unanimous agreement or collective action of the disbelievers in betraying the treaty.
مَنْعَة (man‘ah): Military strength or power to resist; if the group has no man‘ah, their act is not a breach.
إِذْن مَلِك (idhn malik): Permission of the ruler/king of the disbelievers; without it, rogue actions do not breach the treaty for all.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can the imam fight the disbelievers without prior notice after a treaty?
A) When a small group from them commits highway robbery with no military strength.
B) When they collectively and unanimously initiate betrayal.
C) When any individual from them breaks the treaty.
D) When their king is unaware of the betrayal.

Key Takeaway
The imam may fight without notice only when the entire group is complicit; individual unauthorized acts do not void the treaty for all.

The Obligation of Giving Notice (Nabdh) Before Treaty Abrogation
Explaining the requirement of a period for informing the enemy before treaty abrogation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that giving notice before breaking a treaty is wajib and apply the condition that a sufficient period must be allowed for the enemy to be informed.

Core Idea
Breaking a treaty without notice is treachery; the imam must give equal notice and time for it to spread.

This lesson examines the proper procedure for terminating a peace treaty with non-Muslims according to Hanafi fiqh. The central concern is avoiding treachery (ghadr), which is strictly prohibited. The author explains that the imam must formally announce the abrogation and allow enough time for the news to reach the enemy's leadership, drawing on a hadith and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling
Determine what action is being discussed and its legal classification. Here, the act is 'nabdh' (formal notice of treaty abrogation). The ruling is wajib (obligatory) to avoid treachery.
The passage emphasizes that jihad is not permissible in both outward and inward ways without proper notice.
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the primary evidence cited. The author quotes a hadith reported by multiple narrators: 'Whoever has a covenant with a people, he should not tighten a knot nor loosen it until its term expires, or he gives notice of termination equally to them.'
The hadith is ahad (solitary) but its meaning is clear and decisive (dalala qati).
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the dalil proves the ruling. The imperative tone (giving notice) indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. The hadith presents two options: fulfill the treaty or give equal notice.
4
Identify the Condition (Sufficient Period)
The passage clarifies that actual notice to every individual is not required; rather, a period must be allowed sufficient for the enemy king to spread the news throughout his territory. This is the minimum requirement.
The author uses the incident of Amir Muawiyah and Amr ibn Anbasah to illustrate this condition.
5
Apply the Ruling to a Scenario
Consider a modern parallel: if a Muslim state has a ceasefire with a non-Muslim group, the government must publicly announce its decision to terminate and allow reasonable time for the other side's leadership to inform their constituents before any military action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حالانکہ ظاہر و باطن دونوں طرح ترک جہاد جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے عبد کوختم کر دینا ہی ضروری ہوا۔ ختم کر دینے کے معنی یہ ہوتے ہیں کہ کافروں کو پہلے سے مطلع کر دیا جائے ہم نے تم سے کئے ہوئے عہد کو اب ختم کر کافی ہے کہ کافروں کا بادشاہ یا راجہ اس معاہدہ کے ختم ہو جانے سے خود واقف ہو کر اپنے تمام علاقوں میں خبر پہنچا سکے ایسا کر دینے سے بد عہدی کا الزام نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح وَلَا بُدَّمِنِ اعْتِبَارِ مُدَّةٍ الخ اگر امام المسلمین مسلمانوں کے فائدہ کے پیش نظر کافروں سے مصالحت کرنا چاہے تو کرسکتا ہے۔ اس طرح اگر مصالحت کے بعد کسی وجہ سے اس معاہدہ کو ختم کر دینا چاہے تو اس کی بھی اسے اجازت ہے ۔ البتہ یہ ضروری ہے کہ کافروں کے سرداروں کو اس کی اطلاع بھی کر دے تا کہ بد عہدی اور غداری کا ہم پر الزام نہ ہو اور وہ غفلت میں پڑے نہ رہیں۔ ساتھ ہی اتنا وقت بھی ان کو دیا جائے جس میں خبر ان کے ہاں پھیل سکے پھر خبر خواہ پھیلے یا نہ پھیلے اس کی ذمہ داری نہ ہوگی ۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ جب کافروں کے بادشاہ کو یہ خبر دیدی گئی کہ ہم نے عہد توڑ دیا ہے تو اس کے بعد فورا ہی حملہ نہ کر دے کیونکہ وہ لوگ اس معاہدہ کی بنا پر دھو کہ میں کا گذر جانا ہی کافی ہوگا۔ کہ جس میں کافروں کا بادشاہ اپنے ملک کے تمام علاقوں میں اس خبر سے سب کو مطلع کر سکتا ہو۔ چنانچہ امیر معاویہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ نے کفار روم کے ساتھ معاہدہ کیا پھر لشکر کو لے کر ان کا فروں کی طرف روانہ ہو گئے ۔ پھر عہد کے توڑنے کی خبر دینے کے ساتھ ہی ان پر حملہ بھی کر دینا چاہا۔ اتنے میں ایک شخص پیچھے سے گھوڑا دوڑاتے ہوئے یہ کہتا ہوا آیا کہ الله اكبر، الله أكبرُ، وَفَاء لَا غَدْرُ ۔ اس پر مڑ کر ان کو دیکھا تو وہ عمر وابن عنبہ تھے۔ معاویہ رضی اللہ عنہ نے ان سے پوچھا کہ کیا بات ہے تو فرمایا کہ میں نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے سنا ہے کہ جس شخص سے کسی قوم کے درمیان معاہدہ ہو تو وہ اس مدت کے اندر کوئی گرہ مضبوط نہ کرے اور نہ کھولے (معاہدہ میں ذرہ برابر کمی و بیشی نہ کرے ) یہاں تک کہ وہ مدت گذر جائے ۔ یا عہد توڑنے کی اطلاع برابری کے ساتھ ان کو بھی دے۔ پس یہ سن کر معاویہ رضی اللہ عنہ اپنا لشکر لے کر لوٹ آئے۔ ( رواه احمد ، ابو داود والترندی والنسائی وابن ماجه وابن حبان ) اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ مدت کے درمیان حملہ کا سامان نہ کرے مگر اس طرح سے کہ ان کو بھی اطلاع دیدے تا کہ وہ لوگ بھی سامان کر سکیں۔
Although leaving jihad is not permissible in both outward and inward ways. Therefore, it is necessary to annul the covenant. The meaning of annulment is to inform the disbelievers beforehand that we have now terminated the covenant we had with you, so that there is no treachery and breach of faith. Indeed, the Messenger of Allah said about covenants: 'The covenant is fulfilled and there is no treachery.' As reported by Ibn Majah. And at the time of covenant termination, a period must be set such that the news of the termination of the treaty can reach all the disbelievers, and they do not remain in heedlessness or unaware. However, it is not necessary that everyone be actually informed; rather, it is sufficient that a period passes in which the king or ruler of the disbelievers, upon learning of the termination, can spread the news throughout his territories. By doing so, the accusation of breach of faith will not arise. Explanation: 'And there must be consideration of a period' etc. If the imam of the Muslims, considering the benefit of the Muslims, wishes to make peace with the disbelievers, he may do so. Similarly, if after peace he wishes to terminate the treaty for some reason, he is also permitted to do so. However, it is necessary that he informs their leaders so that the accusation of breach of faith and treachery does not fall upon us, and they do not remain heedless. Along with that, they should be given enough time for the news to spread among them. Then, whether the news spreads or not, there will be no responsibility upon us. In summary, when the king of the disbelievers is given the news that we have broken the treaty, he should not attack immediately because due to the treaty they will be heedless of war. In such a case, attacking would be treachery. Rather, a period should be set so that the disbelievers can become aware of it. But it is not possible to know whether all of them have been informed, so the passage of such a period is sufficient, in which the king of the disbelievers can inform everyone in all areas of his country about the news. For example, Amir Muawiyah (may Allah be pleased with him) had a treaty with the disbelievers of Rome. Then he set out with his army towards them. He then wanted to attack them along with giving the news of treaty breaking. Meanwhile, a person came from behind riding a horse, saying: 'Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, fulfillment not treachery.' He turned back and saw that it was Amr ibn Anbasah. Muawiyah asked him what the matter was. He said: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah say: Whoever has a covenant with a people, he should not tighten a knot nor loosen it (i.e., make no change in the covenant) until its term expires, or he gives notice of termination equally to them.' Hearing this, Muawiyah returned with his army. (Narrated by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, and Ibn Hibban). Its meaning is that during the period, he should not prepare for attack except in such a way that he also informs them so that they too can prepare.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the requirement of giving notice (inbaadh) before terminating a treaty with non-Muslims. The author explains that simply breaking a treaty without prior notice constitutes treachery (ghadr), which is forbidden by the hadith 'al-ahdu wafaa' (the covenant is fulfillment). Therefore, when the imam decides to abrogate a treaty, he must announce the termination and allow enough time for the enemy king to disseminate the news throughout his territory. The actual arrival of the news to every individual is not necessary; the mere passage of a period sufficient for the king to inform his subjects is enough. The author illustrates this with the well-known incident of Amir Muawiyah and Amr ibn Anbasah, where the Companion prevented an immediate attack after giving notice, citing the Prophet's command to either wait for the treaty's expiry or give equal notice. The ruling applies to all cases where the imam sees benefit in terminating a peace treaty.

Key Terms
نبذ (nabdh): The formal act of abrogating a treaty by giving notice to the other party.
عہد (ahd): A covenant or treaty between Muslims and non-Muslims, typically a peace agreement or truce.
غدر (ghadr): Treachery or breach of faith, which is strictly prohibited in Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum requirement for breaking a treaty with non-Muslims according to the Hanafi school?
A) Attack immediately if the imam deems it beneficial.
B) Give notice to the enemy leaders and allow enough time for the news to spread through their territory.
C) Wait for the treaty term to expire without any action.
D) Inform all individual enemy soldiers before attacking.

Key Takeaway
Notice before treaty abrogation is wajib to avoid treachery; the imam must allow enough time for the enemy to be informed.

Responding to Enemy Treachery Without Notice
Ruling on responding to enemy treachery without notice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fighting the enemy without prior notice, identify the condition of collective treachery, and apply the ruling to scenarios involving partial or unauthorized breaches.

Core Idea
Collective enemy treachery dissolves treaty; no notice needed before fighting.

In the law of armed conflict (siyar), the Hanafi school distinguishes between individual acts of hostility and collective violations of a treaty. This lesson examines a key passage from al-Hidayah that clarifies when a Muslim imam may respond militarily without the usual requirement of prior notification. Understanding this ruling requires careful parsing of the condition of 'collective agreement' (ittifaq) and the role of military strength (man'ah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
The text states that if the enemy initiates treachery (khiyanah), the imam should fight them without giving notice (nabdh). This is the general rule.
The ruling is conditional upon the treachery being by their agreement (bi-ittifaqihim).
2
Identify the proof (dalil)
The reasoning: 'because they have become violators of the treaty, so there is no need to abrogate it.' The enemy's own action nullifies the treaty, so additional notice is unnecessary.
This is a rational proof (talil) based on the enemy's breach.
3
Identify the exception for a small group without power
If a small group of the enemy commits highway robbery but has no military strength (man'ah), this is not considered a treaty breach. Therefore, notice would still be required before fighting the whole community.
The presence or absence of man'ah determines whether the act signifies collective treachery.
4
Identify the nuance for a group with power but without king's permission
If a powerful group openly fights Muslims but without the permission of their king, the breach applies only to them personally, not to the entire community. Their action does not bind others.
This preserves the treaty for the rest of the enemy population.
5
Identify the ruling when the king permits
If the powerful group acted with the king's permission, then the entire community is considered treacherous, and no notice is needed before fighting all.
King's permission equates to collective agreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَ إِنْ بَدَو ابخِيَانَةٍ قَاتَلَهُمْ وَلَمْ يَنْبُذُ إِلَيْهِمْ إِذَا كَانَ ذَالِكَ بِاتِّفَاقِهِمْ لأَنَّهُمْ صَارُوا نَا قِضِيْنَ لِلْعَهْدِ فَلَا حَاجَةَ إِلى نَقْضِهِ بِخِلافِ مَا إِذَا دَخَلَ جَمَاعَةٌ مِّنْهُمُ فَقَطَعُوا الطَّريقَ وَلَا مَنْعَة لَهُمُ حَيْثُ لا يَكُونَ هَذَا نَقْضًا لِلْعَهْدِ وَلَوْ كَانَتْ لَهُمْ مَنْعَةٌ وَقَاتَلُوا الْمُسْلِمِينَ عَلَانِيَةً يَكُونُ نَقُضًا لِلْعَهْدِ فِى حَقَّهِمْ دُونَ غَيْرِهِمُ لانه بغير إذن مَلِكِهمْ فَفِعْلُهُمْ لَا يلزمُ غَيْرَهُمْ حَتَّى لَوْ كَانَ بإذن مَلِكِهُمْ صَارُوا نَافِضِينَ لِلْعَهْدِ لأنَّهُ بِاتِّفَاقِهِمْ مَعْنَى
He said: And if they initiate treachery, he should fight them and not give notice to them [of abrogation] if that [treachery] is by their agreement, because they have become violators of the treaty, so there is no need to abrogate it. Contrary to the case when a group of them enter [Muslim land] and commit highway robbery, and they have no [military] strength, for this is not a breach of the treaty. But if they have strength and they openly fight the Muslims, it is a breach of the treaty with respect to them, not others, because it is without the permission of their king; thus their action does not bind others. However, if it was with the permission of their king, they become violators of the treaty because that is by their agreement in meaning.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This is a matn from the original text (likely al-Hidayah) followed by commentary. The ruling: If the disbelievers collectively (by common agreement or with the king's permission) commit an act of treachery (such as attacking Muslims), the imam may fight them without first giving notice of abrogation of the treaty. The reason is that they have already invalidated the treaty by their own actions. The exception is if a small group without power commits robbery or a limited attack; that does not nullify the treaty for the whole community. However, if that group has power and fights openly, it breaks the treaty only for them, not for the rest, unless they acted with the king's permission. In that case, the entire community is considered treacherous.

Key Terms
خیانة (khiyānah): Treachery, betrayal of trust, specifically a breach of the treaty by the enemy.
نبذ (nabdh): The formal abrogation of a treaty by giving notice to the enemy.
منعة (man'ah): Military strength or power; having the ability to fight effectively.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when can the imam fight the enemy without giving prior notice?
A) Whenever a single enemy soldier attacks a Muslim.
B) Only when the enemy initiates treachery by mutual agreement (e.g., the whole community or with the king's permission).
C) Never; notice must always be given.
D) Only when the enemy has no military strength.

Key Takeaway
When the enemy collectively violates a treaty, the treaty is dissolved and the imam can fight without further notice.
