Peace with Disbelievers in Exchange for Wealth: Permissibility and Classification of Wealth
Ruling on accepting money for peace with conditions and classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting money from the enemy in exchange for peace, identify the condition of need, and distinguish the treatment of wealth as jizyah or ghanimah based on the circumstances.

Core Idea
Peace with payment is permissible when Muslims have a need; the wealth is spent like jizyah unless taken under siege, then it's ghanimah.

This passage extends the general permissibility of peace treaties to those involving monetary compensation. It establishes a key distinction: whether the enemy was besieged or not determines how the money is classified. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the condition of need, and the analogical reasoning behind the classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is the imam making peace (muwāda‘ah) with the people of war in exchange for wealth. The ruling is 'lā ba’sa bihi' (no harm), i.e., permissible.
The ruling is conditional, as seen in the next step.
2
Locate the Condition
The permissibility is conditional on the Muslims having a genuine need (hājah). If there is no need, it is not permissible because the purpose of jihad is to elevate Allah's word, not to seek wealth.
This condition prevents the ruling from being absolute.
3
Identify the Proof (Dalīl)
The author uses qiyas jaliy (clear analogy): since peace without wealth is permissible, peace with wealth is also permissible by analogy. This is a straightforward qiyas from the original permissibility.
No specific text is quoted; the reasoning is analogical.
4
Distinguish the Two Scenarios and Their Treatment
If the enemy sends a messenger (no siege), the wealth is treated like jizyah and spent in the same categories. If the Muslim army surrounds them (siege), the wealth is ghanimah: one-fifth (khums) is taken, and the rest is distributed among the soldiers.
The decisive factor is the presence or absence of military force (qahr).
5
Note the Underlying Rationale
When the enemy voluntarily pays to avoid war (no siege), it resembles the jizyah paid by dhimmis for protection. When the payment is made under duress of siege, it is spoils taken by force, hence ghanimah.
The analogy (ma‘nā) drives the classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَارَأَى الْإِمَامُ مُوَادَعَةَ أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ وَ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ عَلَى ذَالِكَ مَا لا فَلَا بَأْسَ بِهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمَّا جَازَتِ الْمُوَادَعَهُ بِغَيْرِ الْمَالِ فَكَذَا بِالْمَالِ لكن هذا إذا كَانَ بِالْمُسْلِمِينَ حَاجَةً أَمَّا إِذَا لَمْ تَكُنْ لَا يَجُوزُ لِمَا بَيْنَا مِنْ قَبْلُ وَالْمَاعُوذُ مِنَ الْمَالِ يُصْرَفُ مَصَارِفَ الْجِزْيَةِ هذَا إِذَا لَمْ يَنزِلُوا بِسَاحَتِهِمْ بَلْ أَرْسَلُوا رَسُولًا لِأَنَّهُ فِي مَعْنَى الْجِزْيَةِ أَمَّا إِذَا أَحَاطَ الْجَيْشُ بِهِمْ ثُمَّ أَخَذُوا الْمَالَ فَهُوَ غَيْمَةُ بِخَمْسِهَا وَتُقَسَّمُ الْبَاقِي بَيْنَهُمْ لِأَنَّهُ مَاعُوذُ بِالْفَهْرِ مَعْنى
And when the imam sees [benefit in] making peace with the people of war and taking wealth for that, there is no harm in it, because when peace is permissible without wealth, so also with wealth. But this is when the Muslims have a need. As for when there is no need, it is not permissible, as we have previously explained. And the wealth taken is spent in the ways of jizyah. This is when they have not descended into their territory [i.e., the enemy has not been surrounded by the army] but rather they sent a messenger, because it is in the meaning of jizyah. However, when the army has surrounded them and then they take the wealth, it is ghanimah, with its khums [taken] and the rest distributed among them, because it is wealth taken by force in meaning.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of making a peace treaty with disbelievers in exchange for money. The general principle: if peace without payment is allowed, then peace with payment is also allowed, provided there is a genuine need (hajah) of the Muslims. If there is no need, it is not permissible because the purpose of jihad is to elevate Allah's word, not to seek wealth. The money received is treated like jizyah (tax from non-Muslims) if the enemy was not surrounded by the Muslim army and simply sent a messenger to negotiate; it is to be spent on the same categories as jizyah. However, if the Muslim army has surrounded the enemy and then takes money in exchange for lifting the siege, it is considered ghanimah (spoils of war), from which one-fifth (khums) is taken for the stated recipients, and the rest is distributed among the soldiers. This distinction is based on whether the wealth was taken with clear military force (ghanimah) or through a voluntary payment to avoid war (like jizyah).

Key Terms
موادعة (muwāda'ah): A peace treaty or truce with the enemy.
جزیة (jizyah): A per capita tax levied on non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) in an Islamic state.
غنیمة (ghanīmah): Spoils of war taken forcibly from the enemy, subject to khums (one-fifth share) and distribution among soldiers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the wealth taken in exchange for peace become ghanimah?
A) When the enemy sends a messenger without being surrounded
B) When the Muslim army has surrounded the enemy
C) When the imam decides it is ghanimah
D) When the amount exceeds the jizyah rate

Key Takeaway
Peace with payment is permissible only if Muslims have a genuine need; the wealth's treatment depends on whether it was given under siege (ghanimah) or voluntarily (jizyah-like).

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
8 min
Peace with Apostates: The Requirement of Tawba Before Fighting
Ruling on peace with apostates requiring tawba before fighting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making peace with apostates, explain why the Imam must call them to repentance before execution, and identify the evidence from the Quran and Companions' practice.

Core Idea
The Imam must seek repentance from apostates before fighting them, hoping for their return to Islam.

This lesson addresses a key ruling in Hanafi siyar: how the Muslim ruler should deal with apostates who have formed a separate community. The Hanafi school, based on the practice of the Companions and Quranic guidance, requires that the Imam first call them to repentance (tawba) before any military action. This reflects the principle of da'wah and the hope that they may return to Islam. The lesson also explains why jizya cannot be taken from apostates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
Read the first Arabic sentence: the Imam may make a covenant with apostates and delay fighting them. The key reason is that Islam is hoped for from them. Identify that this is a permission (ja'iz) with a condition (hope of return).
Focus on the phrase 'li-anna al-islama marju minhum'.
2
Analyze the Prohibition on Taking Wealth
The text states that no wealth (i.e., jizya) may be taken from apostates in a peace agreement. Understand why: jizya is only from non-Muslims who remain on their religion, but apostates' blood is not protected by any covenant.
This distinguishes apostates from other non-Muslims.
3
Trace the Wujub of Calling to Tawba
From the Urdu commentary, note that the 'hope of Islam' is actualized by demanding tawba. The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) considers this wajib. Identify the Companions' examples: Uthman's letter, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud's action, and Ali's delegation to Nahrawan.
The Companions consistently gave apostates an opportunity to repent before execution.
4
Apply the Quranic Verse (4:137)
The verse is cited about those who repeatedly apostatize and increase in kufr: their repentance is not accepted. The Hanafis derive that such persistent apostates are to be killed without further invitation. Contrast this with first-time apostates who are to be invited to tawba.
This verse is the primary dalil for the ruling on repeat apostates.
5
Conclude the Mufta Bihi Position
Based on all evidence, the mufta bihi position is that the Imam must demand tawba from apostates before killing them. Only upon refusal are they executed. No jizya is accepted from them.
This is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.

( عبد الله بن نواحہ حجر بن و ثال) کو قتل کر دیتا۔ اسی لئے میں (عبد اللہ بن مسعود) نے اسے (عبد اللہ بن نواحہ کو قتل کر دیا۔ .. حضرت براء رضی اللہ عنہ سے مروی ہے کہ حضرت علی المرتضیٰ نے ان کو اہل نہروان کی طرف بھیجا تو انہوں (حضر، براٹی) نے اہل نہروان کو تین بار اسلام کی دعوت دی۔
حضرت ابو موسیٰ اشعری نے مقام کسر فتح کر کے تجیبہ کے ان مرتدوں کو قتل کر دیا جو مشرکین سے مل گئے تھے۔ ان کے بارے میں حضرت عمرؓ نے حضرت انس بن مالک سے گفتگو کرتے وقت فرمایا کہ اگر میں (عمر بن خطاب ) انہیں زندہ گرفتار کر لیتا تو ان پر وہ دروازہ (اسلام ) پیش کرتا جس سے وہ نکلے تھے۔ اگر وہ (مجیبہ کے مرتد ) لوٹ آتے تو ٹھیک ورنہ میں انہیں قید کر دیتا۔ البتہ حضرت عمر رضی اللہ عنہ جیبہ کے مرتدوں کو قتل کرنے کی پاداش میں قاتلوں سے کوئی مواخذہ نہیں کیا۔
جولوگ بار بار مرتد ہو جائیں اور پھر کفر میں بڑھ جائیں تو ایسے مرتدوں کی توبہ قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ قرآن مجید میں مذکور ہے کہ : اِنَّ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا ثُمَّ كَفَرُوا ثُمَّ امَنُوا ثُمَّ كَفَرُوا ثَمَّ ازْدَادُوا كُفْرًا لَّمْ يَكُنِ اللَّهُ لِيَغْفِرَ لَهُمُ الآية (النساء: ۱۳۷) بلاشبہ جولوگ ایمان لائے پھر کا فر ہو گئے پھر ایمان لائے پھر کفر کیا پھر کفر میں بڑھ گئے ان کی تو بہ ہرگز قبول نہ ہوگی۔ ( کما جاء فی الطحاوی) متذکرہ دلائل معروضیہ سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایمان کے بعد کفر اختیار کرنے والے افراد سے پہلے تو بہ کا مطالبہ کیا جائے گا۔ چنانچہ قبولیت کی صورت ان ( مرتدوں ) سے قتل و قتال ممنوع ہو گا۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ مرتدوں سے قبولیت اسلام کی امید پر قتل و قتال میں تاخیر ہوگی مبادا کہ وہ لوگ ( مرد ) اسلام قبول کر لیں۔
As for the apostates, the Imam may make a covenant with them until they consider their situation, because Islam is hoped for from them. So it is permissible to delay fighting them hoping for their Islam. And he should not take wealth from them because it is not permissible to take jizya from them, as will be explained. Translation: And those who apostatized from Islam (then overcame a region and became independent until that region became dar al-harb. But later they asked the Imam of Muslims to make peace, and the Imam also saw benefit in making peace at that time) then the Imam can make peace with them. So that he may consider their matter. Because there remains hope that perhaps these apostates will become Muslims again. So on this hope, it is permissible to delay fighting them. And they cannot be made to pay wealth for peace (although from disbelievers, wealth can be taken for peace, because it is not permissible to take jizya from apostates. Its detail will be explained in the chapter of jizya, Allah willing. Commentary: The discussion of delaying war on hope of accepting Islam. The meaning of hope of accepting Islam in this case is demanding repentance from apostates. Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Abu Yusuf (according to one narration) and Imam Muhammad say that the leader of the Muslim army should demand repentance from the apostate; that is better. If he refuses repentance, the apostate is to be killed. It is narrated from Ubaydullah b. Abdullah b. Utba that some people in Kufa were arrested while preaching the falsehoods of Musaylima al-Kadhdhab. He (Abdullah) wrote to Uthman about them (followers of Musaylima). Uthman replied: Present to them the true religion and the kalima of shahada. Those who accept and disavow Musaylima, do not kill them; those who adhere to the false religion of Musaylima, kill them. It is clear that in the present age, the same ruling applies to the fitna of Qadianiyat, Agha Khaniat, Rafidiat, Baha'iyat, because these people believe in the prophethood (literally or in meaning) of Ghulam Ahmad Qadiani, Agha Khan, the Twelve Imams, Mirza Ali Muhammad Baha, etc., and are persistent in spreading their beliefs. ... Abdullah b. Mas'ud had the believers in Musaylima's prophethood arrested. Some of them repented and returned from Musaylima's prophethood; he released them. Later one of them named Abdullah b. Nawwaha was brought forward; he killed him. People asked: Why two different actions in one case? He said: I was sitting with the Messenger when this man and Hajr b. Waththal came as a delegation. The Messenger said: Do you testify that I am the Messenger of Allah? They said: Do you testify that Musaylima is the messenger of Allah? The Messenger said: I believe in Allah and His messenger. If I killed delegations, I would have killed you two. Therefore I killed him. It is narrated from Bara' that Ali sent him to the people of Nahrawan; he called them to Islam three times. Abu Musa al-Ash'ari conquered Kasr and killed those apostates of Tajiba who had joined the idolaters. Umar said to Anas b. Malik: If I had caught them alive, I would have presented them the door (of Islam) from which they had exited. If they returned (to Islam) then fine, otherwise I would have imprisoned them. However, Umar did not punish those who killed the apostates of Jiba. Those who apostatize repeatedly and then increase in kufr, their repentance is not accepted. Because the Quran says: 'Indeed, those who believe, then disbelieve, then believe, then disbelieve, then increase in disbelief - never will Allah forgive them' (4:137). As in al-Tahawi. From these presented proofs, it is clear that those who choose kufr after iman should first be asked to repent. If they do, then fighting them is prohibited. So it is proven that delay in fighting is on hope of acceptance of Islam, lest they (the men) accept Islam.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is from Kitab al-Siyar on the ruling of peace with apostates. The author states that the Imam may make a covenant (sulh) with apostates, delaying war in hope of their return to Islam. The key point is that no wealth (like jizya) may be taken from them in such a peace, because jizya is only taken from non-Muslims who remain on their religion, not from apostates whose blood is not protected. The Urdu commentary then elaborates: the Imam may accept peace to give time for the apostates to reconsider. It details that seeking repentance (tawba) is obligatory before killing. This is based on the practice of the Companions, as narrated: Uthman ordered that those who repented from following Musaylima be spared, while those who persisted be killed. Abdullah b. Mas'ud killed a persistent apostate, citing the Prophet's incident with the same man. The passage also cites a Quranic verse (4:137) that those who repeatedly apostatize are not forgiven, i.e., their repentance is not accepted. The commentary emphasizes that the initial hope of return justifies delaying war, but only for first-time apostates; repeat offenders face execution without further invitation. This is a clear Hanafi position: the Imam must call apostates to tawba, and only upon refusal are they killed. The authority weight is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, as it follows the established Hanafi rulings.

Key Terms
مُرْتَدّ (murtadd): A person who was Muslim and then left Islam; in siyar, one who has joined a hostile group or established a separate domain.
جِزْيَة (jizya): A poll tax taken from non-Muslims under Islamic rule; not permissible to take from apostates.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on taking jizya from apostates during a peace agreement?
A) It is permissible as a form of peace payment
B) It is not permissible because jizya is only from ahl al-dhimma
C) It is wajib to take jizya from them
D) It is makruh but allowed

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school require the Imam to call apostates to repentance before fighting them, and no jizya may be taken from them; the evidence comes from the Quran (4:137) and the consistent practice of the Companions.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
8 min
Apostates' Property and Peace Payments in Siege
Explains two rulings on apostates' property and paying for peace, with an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to (1) explain why apostates' property taken in a peace deal is not returned, (2) state the condition under which Muslims may pay for peace when besieged, and (3) distinguish between Imam Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on the moment apostates lose ownership of their property.

Core Idea
Apostates' property is non-inviolable upon apostasy; Muslims may only pay for peace to avert total destruction.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents two distinct rulings from the law of war: the treatment of apostates' property in peace settlements, and the permissibility of Muslims paying for a truce when besieged. Underlying the first ruling is a crucial intra-Hanafi debate about the moment an apostate loses ownership of his wealth. Understanding this debate sharpens our grasp of how the Hanafi school derives rulings from the principles of inviolability (isma) and necessity (darura).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage addresses two scenarios: (a) taking wealth from apostates as part of a peace agreement, and (b) Muslims paying wealth to a besieging enemy for a truce. Identify the ruling in each case.
First: the imam may take and not return. Second: generally prohibited, but allowed if destruction is feared.
2
Understand the rationale for apostates' property
The text explains that apostates' wealth is ghayr ma'sum (non-inviolable) because apostasy removes the protection (isma) from the person and his property.
Mal ghayr ma'sum is property that has no protected status.
3
Unpack the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that ownership is lost upon apostasy (suspended), while the Sahibayn hold that ownership remains until death or joining dar al-harb. Determine how each view affects the return of property taken in a peace deal.
The practical consequence: per Abu Hanifa, property taken is not returned; per Sahibayn, it should be returned.
4
Analyse the condition for paying for peace
The imam should not pay for a truce because it implies humiliation and blood money. However, if destruction is certain, it becomes wajib to pay to save lives.
The maxim: 'دفع الهلاك واجب بأي طريق يمكن' (preventing destruction is obligatory by any means possible).
5
Connect the rulings to broader principles
The concept of mal ghayr ma'sum and the darura exception show how Hanafi fiqh balances inviolability and necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هفتم
( کفار کو ) اسلام کے قریب لانا اور عملی طور پر قبولیت اسلام کی راہ ہموار کرنا ہے۔ جب کہ مرتد اسلام میں داخل ہو کر اس ( اسلام ) کی صداقت و سچائی کوعملا وقولا دیکھ چکا ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا سبب کے مفقود ہونے سے نفس جزیہ کا فقدان لازم آئے گا۔ مرتدوں سے مال لے کر صلح کرنے کا حکم
وَلَوْ أَخَذَهُ لَمْ يَرُدَّهُ لِأَنَّهُ مَال غَيْرُ مَعْصُومٍ وَلَوْ حَاصَرَ الْعَدُرُّ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَطَلَبُوا الْمَوَادَعَةَ عَلَى مَالٍ يَدْفَعُهُ المُسْلِمُونَ إِلَيْهِمْ لَا يَفْعَلُ الْإِمَامُ لِمَافِيهِ مِنْ إِعْطَاءِ الدَيَّةِ وَإِلْحَاقِ الْمَذَلَّةِ بِأَهْلِ الْإِسْلَامِ إِلَّا إِذَا خَافَ الْهَلَاكَ لِأَنَّ دَفْعَ الْهَلَاكِ وَاحِبُ بِأي طَرِيقٍ يُمْكِنُ
ترجمہ اور بالفرض اگر مرتدوں سے مال کے عوض صلح کی گئی اور مال لے لیا گیا تو ان کو واپس کرنے کی بھی ضرورت نہیں ہے کیونکہ مرتد کا مال محترم مال نہیں ہوتا ہے اور اگر کافروں نے مسلمانوں کو اپنے محاصرہ میں نے لیا اور یہ خواہش ظاہر کی کہ مسلمان ان سے مال کے بدلہ صلح کر لیں تو امام کو چاہئے کہ وہ اس صلح کو منظور نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ ایسا کرنے سے دیت دینا اور مسلمانوں پر ذلت مسلط ہونے کو تسلیم کر لینا ہو گا۔ البتہ اگر صورت حال ایسی ہوگئی ہو کہ اس کے بغیر سب کی ہلاکت کا خوف ہو تو ( وقتی طور سے ) جائز ہوگی کیونکہ جس طرح ممکن ہو مسلمانوں کو ہلاکت سے بچانا واجب ہے۔ (یعنی خواہ قتال کر کے ہو یا مال دے کر ہو جس طرح بھی ممکن ہو ہلاک ہونے سے بچانا واجب ہے )۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مرتدوں سے صلح کے بدلے میں مال اخذ کر لیا تو وہ مال نا قابل واپسی ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ترک المال کی وجہ سے مرتدوں کا مال باعتبار قیمت کا لعدم متصور ہوگا کیونکہ اس سے مال پر مرتد کی ملکیت باقی نہیں رہتی ۔
مال غیر معصوم کی حقیقت جب لفظ "معصوم کی اضافت ”مال“ کی طرف ہو تو اس سے مراد مال کا قیمتی ہونا ہے۔ اور مال اس وقت قیمتی ہوتا ہے جب وہ (مال) کسی کی ملکیت ہو ۔ اور جو مال کسی کی ملکیت نہ ہو یا کسی وجہ سے اس کی ملکیت زائل ہو چکی ہو تو اسے مال غیر معصوم کہتے ہیں۔ چونکہ مرند نے ترک اسلام کا ارتکاب کیا ہے اس لئے ترک اسلام کے باعث مرتد کے مال سے اس کی ملکیت زائل ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے مرتد کا
مال غیر معصوم متصور ہوتا ہے۔
- البتہ مرتد کا مال ملکیت کے حوالے سے اس وقت تک زوال پذیر رہے گا جب تک کہ وہ (مرند) دوبارہ اسلام قبول نہ کر لے۔ -۲- مرتد کی موت یا قتل یا دار الحرب میں کفار سے ملنے کی صورت میں اس (مرند) کے مال کی ملکیت ختم ہو جاتی ہے۔ متذ کرہ ہر دو صورتوں میں ائمہ فقہاء کے مابین کوئی اختلاف موجود نہیں۔
زوال ملکیت کے اسباب دو ہیں، (1) موت قتل، دار الحرب سے ملنا۔ (۲) ترک اسلام یعنی ارتداد ۔ چنانچہ زوال ملکیت کے اسباب کے حوالے سے امام ابو حنیفہ اور صاحبین (امام ابو یوسف، امام محمد ) کے درمیان اختلاف پایا جاتا ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ مرتد کا زوال ملکیت ارتداد کی بناء پر تحقیق نہیں ہوتا بلکہ مرتد کا مال پر سے ملکیت کا خاتمہ موت یا قتل یا دار الحرب میں مل جانے
كتاب السير
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہفتم کے باعث ہے۔ جبکہ امام ابوحنیفہ کا موقف یہ ہے کہ مال پر سے زوال ملکیت ارتداد ہے۔ لہذا مرتد کی ملکیت اپنے مال پر ظاہری حالت کے پیش نظر موقوف رہے گی ۔ اگر وہ اسلام قبول کرلے تو اس کا مال معصوم ہوگا۔ اگر وہ قبولیت اسلام سے قبل فوت ہوگیا یا قتل ہو گیا یا دار الحرب سے جا ملا تو اس کا مال غیر معصوم متصور ہوگا اگر حالت ارتداد میں مرتدوں سے صلح کے معاوضہ میں مال اخذ کر لیا تو مال کے غیر معصوم ہونے کی وجہ سے انہیں واپس نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے متن میں امام ابوحنیفہ کے موقف کو پیش کر کے یہ ثابت کیا ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کا قول ہی قابل ترجیح ہے۔ بایں وجہ کہ صاحب ہدایہ بذات خود اصحاب ترجیح میں شمار ہوتے ہیں۔ لہذا ان کی رائے امام ابوحنیفہ کے موقف کے حوالے سے راج متصور ہوگی ۔
محاصرے کی حالت میں مرتدوں کا مسلمانوں سے صلح کا عوض طلب کرنا اگر اہل اسلام پر ایسی حالت کا سامنا ہو جائے کہ وہ مرتدوں کے نرغے میں (بحالت محاصرہ) پھنس گئے ہیں اور اسی حالت سے فائدہ اٹھانے کیلئے مسلمانوں سے بعوض صلح مال طلب کریں تو مسلم حکمران کو چاہئے کہ وہ ان ( مرتدوں ) کو صلح پر مبنی مطالبہ ( عوض مال) تسلیم نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ دریں صورت (1 صلح کے بدلے میں دیئے گئے مال کی حیثیت " خون بہا ادا کرنے کے مترادف ہے۔
(۲ بعوض مال صلح کرنا اسلام اور نفس اسلام کی تذلیل ہے۔ اسلام کے حق میں یہ دونوں صورتیں صحیح نہیں ہیں ۔ بایں وجہ کہ ترک اسلام کی صورت میں مرتدوں نے عملاً اسلام کی حقانیت و سچائی کا انکار کر کے ذلت ہم پہنچائی۔ یہ ایک ایسا جرم ہے جو جزیہ اخذ کرنے سے ممانعت کرتا ہے۔ بوقت قبال مرتدوں سے دو مطالبے (۱) اسلام قبول کرو یا (۲) قال کیلئے تیار ہو جاؤ
جزیہ کا مطالبہ نہ کرنا ارتداد کفر کو شدید کرتا ہے۔ کیونکہ جزیہ کی صورت میں کفار کی نہ صرف جان بخشی ہو جاتی ہے بلکہ ان کی فلاح و بہبود
اور قربت اسلام کی برکات سے مستفید ہونے کے مواقع فراہم ہوتے ہیں۔ لیکن مرتدوں کو ان مواقع سے محروم کیا گیا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ارتداد کفر سے بد ترشی ہے۔ اس لئے اگر مسلمان مرتدوں کے محاصرے میں گھر جائیں تو جام شہادت نوش کرنے یا محاصرہ توڑنے کو تربیج دیں۔ جیسا کہ اُحد و حنین اور خندق و تبوک کے غزوات میں کفار کے گھیراؤ میں آنے کی صورت میں اہل اسلام نے قوت ایمانی کے انوارات بکھیرتے ہوئے یا تو انہوں نے اہل کفر کے محاصروں کو توڑا یا پھر جام شہادت نوش کیا۔ بعد ازاں بلاد شام بلاد
روم وغیرہ کے معرکوں میں اہل اسلام نے دین حق کی سربلندی کو بحال رکھتے ہوئے اہل کفر کے محاصروں کو توڑ پھوڑ کے رکھ دیا۔ الغرض کہ محاصرہ اہل کفر کا ہو یا مرتدوں کا انہیں توڑنے کی تدابیر اختیار کی جائیں یا اللہ تعالیٰ کی راہ میں جان عزیز کا نذرانہ پیش کیا جائے ۔ ان (کفار، مرتدین کی طالبہ ( بعوض مال صلح) کو تسلیم نہ کیا جائے تا کہ اسلام اور اہل اسلام کی عظمت و سر بلندی برقرار ہے۔ اگر صلح کے بدلے میں ان (مرتدوں کو مال دے دیا یہ دیت متصور ہوگی۔
Chapter of Siyar. Ashraf al-Bidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume 7. (To bring disbelievers) closer to Islam and practically pave the way for acceptance of Islam. Whereas an apostate, having entered Islam, has seen its truth and sincerity practically and verbally. Therefore, due to the absence of the cause, the loss of jizyah itself is necessary. The ruling on making peace with apostates by taking wealth: And if he took it, he does not return it because it is property not inviolable. And if the enemy besieges the Muslims and they request a truce for a payment that the Muslims give to them, the imam should not do so because of what it involves of giving blood money and inflicting humiliation upon the people of Islam, except if he fears destruction, because preventing destruction is obligatory by any means possible. Translation: And if, hypothetically, peace was made with apostates in exchange for wealth and the wealth was taken, there is no need to return it because the wealth of an apostate is not inviolable. And if disbelievers besiege Muslims and express a desire that the Muslims make peace with them in exchange for wealth, the imam should not accept this peace because doing so would involve giving blood money and accepting humiliation imposed upon Muslims. However, if the situation is such that without it there is fear of total destruction, then it is temporarily permissible because it is obligatory to save Muslims from destruction in any way possible (whether by fighting or by giving wealth, whichever is possible). Explanation: The issue is that if wealth is taken from apostates in exchange for peace, that wealth will be non-returnable because, due to apostasy, the wealth of apostates is considered non-existent in terms of value because ownership of the apostate over his wealth does not remain. The reality of non-inviolable property: When the word 'inviolable' is attributed to 'wealth', it means wealth has value. And wealth has value when it is owned by someone. And wealth that is not owned by anyone or whose ownership has ceased for some reason is called non-inviolable property. Since the apostate has committed apostasy, due to apostasy his ownership over his wealth ceases, so the apostate's wealth is considered non-inviolable. However, the apostate's wealth will remain in a state of suspension regarding ownership until he re-embraces Islam. 2. Upon the apostate's death, killing, or joining the disbelievers in the abode of war, his ownership over his wealth ceases. In both mentioned cases, there is no disagreement among the jurists. The causes of loss of ownership are two: (1) death, killing, or joining the abode of war; (2) abandonment of Islam, i.e., apostasy. Regarding the causes of loss of ownership, there is a disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad). The two companions say that the loss of ownership of the apostate does not actually occur due to apostasy, but rather the termination of the apostate's ownership over his wealth is due to death, killing, or joining the abode of war. While Imam Abu Hanifa's position is that loss of ownership over wealth is due to apostasy. Therefore, the apostate's ownership over his wealth will remain suspended in terms of apparent condition. If he accepts Islam, his wealth becomes inviolable. If he dies before accepting Islam, or is killed, or joins the abode of war, his wealth is considered non-inviolable. If wealth is taken from apostates in exchange for peace during the state of apostasy, it will not be returned to them due to its non-inviolability. The author of Hidayah, by presenting Imam Abu Hanifa's position in the text, has proven that Imam Abu Hanifa's saying is preferable because the author of Hidayah himself is among the people of preference. Therefore, his opinion regarding Imam Abu Hanifa's position is considered preponderant. The apostates demanding payment in exchange for peace from Muslims in a state of siege: If the people of Islam face a situation where they are caught in the siege of apostates, and the apostates, taking advantage of this situation, demand wealth from the Muslims in exchange for peace, then the Muslim ruler should not accept their demand for peace (in exchange for wealth) because in this case (1) the wealth given in exchange for peace is equivalent to paying blood money. (2) Making peace in exchange for wealth is a humiliation of Islam and of Islam itself. Both of these situations are not correct for Islam because in the case of apostasy, the apostates have practically denied the truth and sincerity of Islam and brought humiliation. This is a crime that prohibits taking jizyah. At the time of confrontation, two demands are made from apostates: (1) Accept Islam, or (2) Prepare for war. Not demanding jizyah makes apostasy more severe disbelief because in the case of jizyah, not only do the disbelievers' lives be spared, but opportunities for their welfare and benefiting from the blessings of closeness to Islam are provided. But apostates are deprived of these opportunities. This shows that apostasy is worse than disbelief. Therefore, if Muslims are caught in a siege by apostates, they should either drink the cup of martyrdom or prefer to break the siege. As in the battles of Uhud, Hunayn, Khandaq, and Tabuk, when surrounded by disbelievers, the people of Islam, scattering the lights of faith, either broke the sieges of the disbelievers or drank the cup of martyrdom. Later, in the battles of Syria and Rome, etc., the people of Islam, maintaining the supremacy of the true religion, broke the sieges of the disbelievers. In short, whether the siege is by disbelievers or apostates, measures should be taken to break them, or life should be offered as a sacrifice in the way of Allah. Their demand (for peace in exchange for wealth) should not be accepted so that the greatness and supremacy of Islam and the Muslims remain. If wealth is given to them in exchange for peace, it will be considered blood money.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute embedded in a ruling. It opens with the ruling that if an imam takes wealth from apostates as part of a peace agreement, he does not return it because apostates' property is ghayr ma'sum (non-inviolable). The reason is that apostasy causes the protection of property to cease. Then a second ruling follows: if Muslims are besieged by enemies (kuffar or apostates) and the enemy demands payment for a truce, the imam must not agree except when there is fear of destruction, because paying blood money (diyah) and accepting humiliation are impermissible. The commentary clarifies the concept of 'mal ghayr ma'sum': property that has no protected status because it is not owned by someone with inviolability. An apostate's property becomes non-inviolable upon apostasy, though ownership is suspended until he returns to Islam or dies/joins dar al-harb. The text then presents an ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The Sahibayn hold that ownership does not cease upon apostasy alone, but only upon death, execution, or joining dar al-harb. Imam Abu Hanifa's position is that apostasy itself causes the loss of ownership, but it remains suspended; if the apostate repents, his ownership revives; otherwise, it is definitively lost. The author of the Hidayah (Al-Marghinani) prefers Imam Abu Hanifa's view because he is among the muqallidun (followers) who give tarjih. The practical consequence (thamarah) is that if wealth is taken from apostates in a peace deal, it is not returned according to Abu Hanifa, but would be returned per the Sahibayn. The passage then returns to the siege scenario, emphasizing that paying for peace with apostates is equivalent to paying blood money and humiliates Islam. Since apostates rejected Islam after knowing its truth, they are worse than original disbelievers; hence jizyah is not offered to them—only Islam or war. The author concludes that Muslims should prefer martyrdom or breaking the siege over paying for peace, citing historical battles.

Key Terms
مال غیر معصوم (mal ghayr ma'sum): Property that is not inviolable, meaning it has no protected status because it is not owned by someone whose life and property are protected under Islamic law.
مرتد (murtadd): One who has abandoned Islam after being a Muslim. In this text, his property is considered non-inviolable and he is not entitled to jizyah.
جزیہ (jizyah): Poll tax levied on non-Muslims under Muslim rule. In this passage, it is mentioned that apostates are not offered jizyah; only the choice of Islam or war.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition may the imam agree to pay wealth to apostates for a truce?
A) When the apostates promise to return to Islam
B) When the imam fears the destruction of the Muslim community
C) When the amount is small and insignificant
D) When the apostates agree to pay jizyah

Key Takeaway
An apostate's property loses inviolability upon apostasy (per Abu Hanifa); Muslims may only pay for peace to avert certain destruction.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules

Paying Ransom to Apostates During Siege: Default Prohibition and Necessity Exception
Ruling with proof on ransom to apostates during siege

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paying ransom to apostates during a siege and apply the exception of necessity using the Quranic principle of idtirar.

Core Idea
Default: no ransom to apostates. Exception: pay only to save Muslim lives—necessity overrides the prohibition.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the rule that paying ransom to apostates during a siege is normally forbidden because it degrades Islam and is like paying diyah for unprotected blood. However, the text also presents a critical exception: when Muslim lives are in danger, the payment becomes permissible under the principle of necessity. Understanding this balance between honoring Islamic supremacy and preserving life is essential for applying the law of siyar correctly.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on apostate's property and blood
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that apostasy removes ownership; the apostate's property and blood become non-inviolable (ghayr ma'sum). This foundational view affects the ruling on paying them.
2
Identify the default ruling on paying ransom
The text states that the Muslim ruler should not accept the apostates' demand for payment because it would be equivalent to paying diyah for someone whose blood is not protected and it degrades Islam.
Default ruling: haram
3
Understand the reasoning: analogy to diyah and degradation
Paying ransom is like paying blood money for apostates, for whom diyah is not obligatory. It also humiliates Islam by giving consideration to those who rejected it.
4
Recognize the exception: necessity (idtirar)
The text explicitly allows payment when there is genuine fear that Muslims will be killed or destroyed. The Quranic verse 2:173 is cited to justify necessity overriding the prohibition.
Exception: ja'iz (permissible) and potentially wajib
5
Apply the conditions for diyah to confirm the default
Diyah requires the slain to be ma'sum al-dam and mutaqawwim. Apostates lack both, so no diyah is due, reinforcing the prohibition against paying them.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہفتم کے باعث ہے۔ جبکہ امام ابوحنیفہ کا موقف یہ ہے کہ مال پر سے زوال ملکیت ارتداد ہے۔ لہذا مرتد کی ملکیت اپنے مال پر ظاہری حالت کے پیش نظر موقوف رہے گی ۔ اگر وہ اسلام قبول کرلے تو اس کا مال معصوم ہوگا۔ اگر وہ قبولیت اسلام سے قبل فوت ہوگیا یا قتل ہو گیا یا دار الحرب سے جا ملا تو اس کا مال غیر معصوم متصور ہوگا اگر حالت ارتداد میں مرتدوں سے صلح کے معاوضہ میں مال اخذ کر لیا تو مال کے غیر معصوم ہونے کی وجہ سے انہیں واپس نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے متن میں امام ابوحنیفہ کے موقف کو پیش کر کے یہ ثابت کیا ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کا قول ہی قابل ترجیح ہے۔ بایں وجہ کہ صاحب ہدایہ بذات خود اصحاب ترجیح میں شمار ہوتے ہیں۔ لہذا ان کی رائے امام ابوحنیفہ کے موقف کے حوالے سے راج متصور ہوگی ۔
محاصرے کی حالت میں مرتدوں کا مسلمانوں سے صلح کا عوض طلب کرنا اگر اہل اسلام پر ایسی حالت کا سامنا ہو جائے کہ وہ مرتدوں کے نرغے میں (بحالت محاصرہ) پھنس گئے ہیں اور اسی حالت سے فائدہ اٹھانے کیلئے مسلمانوں سے بعوض صلح مال طلب کریں تو مسلم حکمران کو چاہئے کہ وہ ان ( مرتدوں ) کو صلح پر مبنی مطالبہ ( عوض مال) تسلیم نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ دریں صورت (1 صلح کے بدلے میں دیئے گئے مال کی حیثیت " خون بہا ادا کرنے کے مترادف ہے۔
(۲ بعوض مال صلح کرنا اسلام اور نفس اسلام کی تذلیل ہے۔ اسلام کے حق میں یہ دونوں صورتیں صحیح نہیں ہیں ۔ بایں وجہ کہ ترک اسلام کی صورت میں مرتدوں نے عملاً اسلام کی حقانیت و سچائی کا انکار کر کے ذلت ہم پہنچائی۔ یہ ایک ایسا جرم ہے جو جزیہ اخذ کرنے سے ممانعت کرتا ہے۔ بوقت قبال مرتدوں سے دو مطالبے (۱) اسلام قبول کرو یا (۲) قال کیلئے تیار ہو جاؤ
جزیہ کا مطالبہ نہ کرنا ارتداد کفر کو شدید کرتا ہے۔ کیونکہ جزیہ کی صورت میں کفار کی نہ صرف جان بخشی ہو جاتی ہے بلکہ ان کی فلاح و بہبود
اور قربت اسلام کی برکات سے مستفید ہونے کے مواقع فراہم ہوتے ہیں۔ لیکن مرتدوں کو ان مواقع سے محروم کیا گیا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ارتداد کفر سے بد ترشی ہے۔ اس لئے اگر مسلمان مرتدوں کے محاصرے میں گھر جائیں تو جام شہادت نوش کرنے یا محاصرہ توڑنے کو تربیج دیں۔ جیسا کہ اُحد و حنین اور خندق و تبوک کے غزوات میں کفار کے گھیراؤ میں آنے کی صورت میں اہل اسلام نے قوت ایمانی کے انوارات بکھیرتے ہوئے یا تو انہوں نے اہل کفر کے محاصروں کو توڑا یا پھر جام شہادت نوش کیا۔ بعد ازاں بلاد شام بلاد
روم وغیرہ کے معرکوں میں اہل اسلام نے دین حق کی سربلندی کو بحال رکھتے ہوئے اہل کفر کے محاصروں کو توڑ پھوڑ کے رکھ دیا۔ الغرض کہ محاصرہ اہل کفر کا ہو یا مرتدوں کا انہیں توڑنے کی تدابیر اختیار کی جائیں یا اللہ تعالیٰ کی راہ میں جان عزیز کا نذرانہ پیش کیا جائے ۔ ان (کفار، مرتدین کی طالبہ ( بعوض مال صلح) کو تسلیم نہ کیا جائے تا کہ اسلام اور اہل اسلام کی عظمت و سر بلندی برقرار ہے۔ اگر صلح کے بدلے میں ان (مرتدوں کو مال دے دیا یہ دیت متصور ہوگی۔
وجوب دیت کی شرائط
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہفتم
پہلی شرط مقتول معصوم الدم ہو ۔ یعنی ایسا شخص جس کا خون بہانا اسلام میں حرام ہو۔ چنانچہ حربی (جنگ کرنے والا کافر ) ، باغی ، مرتد ، محصن زانی مستوجب قصاص پر مشتمل افراد کے خون بہانے سے دیت واجب نہیں ہوتی۔
.
دوسری شرط مقتول متقوم ( قدر و قیمت کا حامل ) ہو۔ جبکہ مرتد ترک اسلام کے ارتکاب کی پاداش میں مال و جان سمیت قدرو قیمت کا حامل (متقوم ) نہیں۔ اگر محاصرے کے وقت مرتدوں نے مال کے بدلے میں صلح کا مطالبہ کیا اور اہل اسلام کے سربراہ نے اسے تسلیم کر لیا تو اس صورت اہل اسلام کا صلح کے بدلے میں مال دینا دیت (خون بہا) متصور ہوگا۔ جبکہ مرتد کے خون پر دیت واجب نہیں ۔ البذا مرتدوں کے محاصرے کی صورت میں بعوض مال صلح کا مطالبہ تسلیم کر ناصحیح اقدام نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ قال کے وقت مرتدوں کو قتل کرنا " اسلام" کی عظمت و غلبہ دوبالا کرتا ہے اگر مرتدوں کے ہاتھوں محاصرے میں گھرے ہوئے مسلمانوں اور دیگر اہل اسلام کی قتل و غارت کا خوف ہو تو اس صورت میں ان (مرتدوں) سے مال کے بدلے میں صلح کا مطالبہ تسلیم کرنا جائز ہے۔ حتی الامکان کوشش یہ ہو کہ اہل اسلام کو ہلاکت سے بچایا جائے ۔ دریں صورت صلح کے بدلے میں مال دینا مسلمانوں کو قتل و غارت سے بچانے کی غرض سے ہوگا ۔ اس لئے کہ انہیں (مسلمانوں کو ) ہلاکت سے بچانا واجب ہے۔ اور مذکورہ وجوبی امر ( مسلمانوں کو ہلاکت سے بچانا) کسی بھی تدبیر سے ممکن ہوا سے سرانجام دیا جائے گا۔ بایں وجہ کہ مرتدوں کے مد مقابل اہل اسلام کا خون معصوم و متقوم ( قدر و قیمت کا حامل ہے۔ فَمَنِ اضْطُرَّ غَيْرَ بَاغِ وَلَا عَادٍ فَلَا إِثْمَ عَلَيْهِ ( البقرة :١٣)
Book of Siyar. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 7. The reason is that Imam Abu Hanifa's position is that apostasy removes ownership from property. Therefore, the apostate's ownership of his property is suspended in view of the apparent situation. If he accepts Islam, his property becomes inviolable (ma'sum). If he dies before accepting Islam, or is killed, or joins dar al-harb, his property is considered non-inviolable (ghayr ma'sum). If during apostasy, property is taken from apostates as consideration for peace (sulh), it will not be returned to them due to the property being non-inviolable. The author of Hidayah presented Imam Abu Hanifa's position in the text and proved that Imam Abu Hanifa's statement is preferable. Because the author of Hidayah himself is among those who prefer. Hence his opinion regarding Imam Abu Hanifa's position will be considered strong (rajih).

During siege, if apostates ask Muslims for a consideration for peace (sulh), and the Muslims find themselves trapped under siege by apostates, and they ask for property in return for peace, the Muslim ruler should not accept their demand for peace (for property). Because in that case: (1) The property given in return for peace is equivalent to paying blood money (diyah). (2) Making peace in return for property is a degradation of Islam and the essence of Islam. Both these situations are not valid for Islam. Because by leaving Islam, the apostates have practically denied the truth and reality of Islam and brought disgrace. This is a crime that prohibits taking jizyah. At the time of confrontation, two demands are made from apostates: (1) Accept Islam, or (2) Prepare for war.

Not demanding jizyah makes apostasy worse than kufr. Because in the case of jizyah, not only are the lives of disbelievers spared, but opportunities for their welfare and benefiting from the blessings of nearness to Islam are provided. But apostates are denied these opportunities. From this it is known that apostasy is worse than disbelief. Therefore, if Muslims are besieged by apostates, they should prefer to drink the cup of martyrdom or break the siege. As in the battles of Uhud, Hunayn, Khandaq, and Tabuk, when the Muslims were surrounded by disbelievers, they either broke the siege or drank the cup of martyrdom. Later, in the battles of Syria, Rome, etc., the Muslims maintained the supremacy of the true religion and dismantled the sieges of the disbelievers. In short, whether it is a siege by disbelievers or apostates, measures should be taken to break it, or a sacrifice of dear life should be offered in the path of Allah. Their demand (for property in return for peace) should not be accepted so that the greatness and supremacy of Islam and the Muslims remain. If they give property to apostates in return for peace, it will be considered diyah (blood money).

Conditions for the obligation of diyah: First condition: The slain person must be inviolable blood (ma'sum al-dam), i.e., a person whose bloodshed is prohibited in Islam. Thus, diyah is not obligatory for killing a harbi (warring disbeliever), a rebel (baghi), an apostate (murtadd), a muhsan adulterer liable to capital punishment, etc. Second condition: The slain person must be of value (mutaqawwim). While an apostate, due to committing apostasy, is not of value (mutaqawwim) including his property and life. If during siege, apostates demand peace in return for property and the leader of the Muslims accepts it, then the Muslims giving property in return for peace will be considered diyah. While diyah is not obligatory for the blood of an apostate. Therefore, in the case of siege by apostates, accepting their demand for peace in return for property would not be a correct measure. Because at the time of war, killing apostates enhances the greatness and dominance of Islam. If there is fear of killing and destruction of Muslims and other Muslims besieged by apostates, then in that case, accepting their demand for peace in return for property is permissible. Efforts should be made to save Muslims from destruction. In that case, giving property in return for peace is for the purpose of saving Muslims from killing and destruction. Because saving them from destruction is obligatory. And this obligatory matter (saving Muslims from destruction) will be carried out by whatever means possible. Because the blood of the Muslims facing the apostates is inviolable and of value. "But whoever is forced [by necessity], neither desiring [it] nor transgressing [the limit], there is no sin upon him." (Al-Baqarah: 173)
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the permissibility of paying ransom to apostates during siege. The commentary begins by explaining Imam Abu Hanifa's position on the property of an apostate: upon apostasy, ownership is suspended; if the apostate returns to Islam, his property becomes inviolable (ma'sum), but if he dies, is killed, or joins hostile territory, it becomes non-inviolable (ghayr ma'sum). Therefore, property taken from apostates as peace consideration is not returned. The author of Hidayah presents Abu Hanifa's view as preferable. The main ruling: when Muslims are besieged by apostates who demand property in return for peace, the Muslim ruler should not accept, because it would be equivalent to paying diyah for apostates whose blood is not protected, and it degrades Islam. However, an exception is made when there is fear of Muslim casualties: then it becomes permissible to pay to save Muslim lives, based on the Quranic verse (2:173) permitting necessity. The conditions for diyah are also discussed: the slain must have inviolable blood and be of value; apostates lack both, so diyah is not due for them. Thus, the default ruling is prohibition, but necessity allows it.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): A person who renounces Islam after being Muslim.
معصوم الدم (ma'sum al-dam): A person whose blood is inviolable, i.e., it is prohibited to kill them without legal cause.
متقوم (mutaqawwim): Having legal value in Islamic law; property or person that is considered valuable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition is it permissible for a Muslim ruler to pay ransom to apostates during a siege?
A) When the apostates demand it.
B) When there is a genuine fear of Muslim casualties.
C) When the ruler wants to avoid war.
D) When the apostates offer jizyah.

Key Takeaway
Paying ransom to apostates is normally prohibited, but necessity (idtirar) permits it when Muslim lives are in genuine danger.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
8 min
Prohibition of Selling Weapons to Harbi Enemies
Ruling with proof on sale of weapons to harbi enemies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibition of selling weapons to harbi enemies, apply qiyas to horses and iron, and distinguish the exception for food and clothing based on nass.

Core Idea
Selling weapons to harbi enemies is haram; food and clothing are halal by nass.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi siyar: the prohibition of selling weapons and war materials to those at war with Muslims. We will study the textual proof, the rational analogy (qiyas) extending the ruling to horses and iron, and the important exception for food and clothing, which is based on a specific prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that it is not permissible to sell weapons to harbi enemies or carry weapons to their territory. This establishes a clear prohibition (haram).
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The primary proof is a hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited selling weapons to warring disbelievers and carrying them to them. This is a zanni al-thubut hadith but qati al-dalala due to the explicit prohibition (nahi).
Hadith reported by al-Bazzar and mentioned by al-Bukhari in ta'liq form.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the imperative form of prohibition (nahi) indicates haram. The hadith directly forbids the act, so the ruling is established as haram.
No need for further interpretation.
4
Extend the ruling by qiyas
The illa (effective cause) is strengthening the enemy against Muslims. This illa is present in selling horses and iron, so by qiyas jali, those are also prohibited.
Qiyas is applied because the illa is clear and shared.
5
Identify the exception and its proof
Food and clothing follow a different ruling: they are permissible to trade with harbi enemies. This exception is not based on qiyas but on a specific text (nass) – the Prophet ordered Thumamah to supply food to Makkans who were at war.
When nass exists, qiyas is abandoned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حر بی کافروں کو ہتھیار بیچنے کا حکم
وَلَا يَنبَغِى أَنْ تُبَاعَ السّلاحُ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ وَلَا يُحَهَرُ إِلَيْهِمْ لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ نَهَى عَنْ بَيْعِ السّلاحِ مِنَ أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ وَحَمْلِهِ إِلَيْهِمْ وَلِأَنَّ فِيهِ تَقُويَتَهُمْ عَلَى قِتَالِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ فَيُمْنَعُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ وَكَذَا الْكُرَاعُ لِمَانِيَّنَا وَكَذَا الحَدِيدُ لِأَنَّهُ أَصْلُ الصَّلَاح وَكَذَا بَعْدَ المُوادَعَةِ لِأَنَّهَا عَلَى شَرَفِ النَّقْضِ أَو الإِنْقِضَاءِ فَكَانُوا عَلَيْنَا وَهَذَا هُوَ الْقِيَاسُ فِي الطَّعَامِ وَالتَّوْبِ إِلا أَنا عَرَفْنَاهُ بِالنَّصِ فَإِنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَمَرَ تُمَامَةَ أَنْ تَمِيرَ أَهْلَ مَكَّةَ وَهُمْ حَرْبٌ عَلَيه ترجمہ اور حربی کافروں کے ہاتھ ہتھیار نہیں بیچنا چاہئے اور تاجر حضرات بھی اپنا دفاعی سامان تجارت ان کے علاقوں میں نہ لے جائیں کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حربی کافروں کے ہاتھ ہتھیار بیچنے اور ان کی طرف لے جانے سے بھی منع فرمایا ہے ۔ بزار نے اس کی روایت کی ہے اور بخاری نے اسے تعلیقا بیان کیا ہے اور اس دلیل سے بھی منع ہے کہ ایسا کرنے سے حربیوں کو مسلمانوں کے خلاف لڑنے کے لئے طاقت اور تقویت پہنچانی ہوتی ہے اور اسی دلیل سے ان کے ہاتھ گھوڑے ( اور سواری کے دوسرے سامان ) بیچنے کی ممانعت کا حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے اور یہی حکم لوہا بیچنے کا بھی ہوگا۔ کیونکہ تمام ہتھیاروں کا مادہ یہی ہے۔ ہی طرح یہی حکم صلح کے بعد بھی ان چیزوں کو حربیوں کے ہاتھ بیچنا یا وہاں صرف لے جانے کا بھی ہوگا کیونکہ مصالحت کا معاملہ تو بے اعتبار اور غیر یقینی ہوتا ہے یعنی کسی بھی وقت یہ مصالحت ٹوٹ سکتی ہے یا اپنی مدت پر جا کر ختم ہو سکتی ہے۔ اس طرح بالا آخر ہمارا ہی نقصان ہوگا۔ اور ہتھیاروں پر غلوں اور کپڑوں کا قیاس بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔ لیکن نص سے نہیں اس کا حکم واضح طور پر معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ان سے غلے اور کپڑے کا معاملہ کر ناصحیح ہوتا ہے ۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے
Ruling on selling weapons to warring disbelievers. It is not proper to sell weapons to those at war (ahl al-harb) and they should not be carried to them. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited selling weapons to warring disbelievers and carrying them to them. And because it strengthens them against fighting the Muslims, so it is prevented. Similarly, horses (al-kura') [in our view?] and similarly iron, because it is the basic material of weapons. And similarly after a peace treaty (muwada'ah), because it is on the verge of being broken or expiring, so they are against us. And this is the analogy (qiyas) applied to food and clothing, except we know it by text (nass). For he (peace be upon him) ordered Thumamah to supply food to the people of Makkah while they were at war with him. Translation: And it is not proper to sell weapons to warring disbelievers, and merchants should not take their defensive trade goods to their territories. Because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prohibited selling weapons to warring disbelievers and carrying them to them. Al-Bazzar narrated it and al-Bukhari mentioned it in a suspended form. And for this reason also it is prohibited, because it gives the warring disbelievers strength and power to fight the Muslims. And for the same reason, the prohibition of selling horses (and other riding animals) to them is established. And the same ruling applies to selling iron, because it is the raw material for all weapons. Similarly, the same ruling applies after a peace treaty, because the treaty is unreliable and uncertain—it may break at any time or expire after its term. Thus, ultimately it would be to our detriment. And analogy could also be applied to food and clothing, but from the text (nass) it is clearly known that trading in food and clothing with them is correct. Because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ordered Thumamah to supply food to the people of Makkah while they were at war with him.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the prohibition of selling weapons and war materials to harbi (warring) disbelievers. The commentary begins by stating that it is not permissible to sell weapons to them or carry weapons to their territory. The proof is a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibiting such sales, and the rational reason is that it strengthens the enemy against Muslims. The ruling extends to horses (used in warfare) and iron (the raw material for weapons) by qiyas (analogy). The prohibition applies even after a peace treaty, as such treaties are unstable and may be broken. An exception is made for food and clothing: based on a specific text (nass)—the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered Thumamah to supply food to the people of Makkah when they were at war—it is permissible to trade in food and clothing with them, as these do not directly aid in warfare. The passage is incomplete, ending mid-sentence, but the ruling is clear.

Key Terms
حربی (harbi): A disbeliever who is in a state of war with Muslims, as opposed to a dhimmi or musta'mim.
سلاح (silah): Weapons and arms used for warfare.
كراع (kura'): Horses and other beasts used for war, such as cavalry mounts.
نص (nass): An explicit text from the Quran or Sunnah that provides a clear ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for exempting food and clothing from the prohibition of selling to harbi enemies?
A) Qiyas on weapons
B) Istihsan (juristic preference)
C) A specific hadith (nass) where the Prophet allowed supplying food to Makkans
D) Ijma' (consensus)

Key Takeaway
Selling weapons and war materials to harbi enemies is prohibited by text and analogy, but food and clothing are allowed due to a specific prophetic precedent.

Validity of Aman from a Free Muslim
Ruling on aman from a single free Muslim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on aman given by a free Muslim and identify the primary proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
A single free Muslim's aman binds the entire Muslim community.

This passage establishes that any free Muslim—man or woman—can grant safe-conduct (aman) to an enemy, and once given, no other Muslim may fight those protected. The ruling is based on a prophetic hadith about the equality of Muslim blood and the binding nature of their covenants. We will walk through the textual proof and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is granting aman by a free Muslim. The ruling: it is valid (sahih) and binding on all Muslims.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'The blood of Muslims are equal, and the lowest of them strives to fulfil their covenant.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The term 'the lowest of them' (أدناهم) includes even a single person, proving that one individual's covenant is binding on all.
4
Analyse the rational argument
The text adds that the person granting aman is from the fighting people, so enemies fear him, and that aman is indivisible like faith.
5
Note the scope
The aman can be given to a single person, a group, or even a fortified city. It is not limited to a specific number.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِذَا امَنَ رَجُل حُرٌّ أَوِ امْرَأَةٌ حُرَّةٌ كَافِرًا أَوْ جَمَاعَةً أَوْ أَهْلَ حِصْنٍ أَوْ مَدِينَةٍ صَحَّ أَمَانُهُمْ وَلَمْ يَكُنْ لِأَحَدٍ مِّنَ الْمُسْلِمِيْنَ قِتَالُهُمْ وَالْأَصْلُ فِيهِ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الْمُسْلِمُونَ تَتَكَافَأُ دِمَاؤُهُمْ وَيَسْعَى بِذِمَّتِهِمْ أَدْنَاهُمْ أَى أَقَلَّهُمْ وَهُوَ الْوَاحِدُ وَلِأَنَّهُ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْقِتَالِ فَيَخَافُونَهُ إِذْ هُوَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْمَنْعَةِ فَيَتَحَقَّقُ الْاِمَانُ مِنْهُ لِمُلَافَاتِهِ مَحَلَّهُ ثُمَّ يَتَعَدّى إِلَى غَيْرِهِ وَلِأَنَّ سَبَبَهُ لَا يَتَجَزَّأُ وَهُوَ الْإِيْمَانُ وَكَذَا الْأَمَانُ لَا يَتَجَزَّأُ فَيَتَكَامَلُ كَوِلَايَةِ الْإِنكَاحِ
When a free man or a free woman gives aman to a disbeliever, or a group, or the people of a fort, or a city, their aman is valid, and it is not permissible for any of the Muslims to fight them. The basis for this is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The blood of Muslims are equal, and the lowest of them strives to fulfil their covenant' – i.e., the least of them, and that is one person. And because he is from the fighting people, so they fear him, as he is from the people of protection, so the aman from him is realized as it meets its place (the one from whom fear is felt). Then it extends to others because its cause (iman) is indivisible, and likewise aman is indivisible, so it is complete like the authority of marriage.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that a single free Muslim (man or woman) can grant aman (safe-conduct) to an enemy, whether an individual, a group, or a fortified place. Once granted, it is binding on all Muslims; no one may fight those who have been given aman. The proof is the hadith: 'The blood of Muslims are equal, and the lowest of them strives to fulfil their covenant' – meaning that even the most humble Muslim's guarantee is binding on the entire community. The text then presents a rational proof (qiyas): the person giving aman is from the 'people of fighting' (ahl al-qital), so enemies fear him; this fear is the basis of aman. Since aman is indivisible (like faith itself), it extends to all Muslims. An analogy is drawn to the authority of marriage (wilayat al-inkah), which is also not divisible.

Key Terms
امان (aman): Safe-conduct or pledge of protection given to an enemy, guaranteeing security from attack.
ذمة (dhimma): Covenant of protection; the obligation to ensure safety.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary basis (al-asl) for the ruling that a single Muslim's aman is binding?
A) Consensus of the Companions
B) The hadith that the blood of Muslims are equal and the lowest can fulfil their covenant
C) Analogy to the validity of marriage contracts
D) The rational argument that aman is indivisible

Key Takeaway
A single free Muslim's aman is valid and binding on all Muslims, based on the prophetic hadith about the equality of Muslim blood.

Imam's Authority to Revoke an Aman Causing Harm
Imam's authority to revoke aman for harm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which an Imam may revoke an aman given by himself or by a soldier, and explain the difference based on harm versus consideration of benefit.

Core Idea
An aman can be broken by the Imam if it causes harm, but a soldier who gave aman with good reason may be excused.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a critical exception to the general sanctity of aman (safe conduct). While aman is normally binding, the law recognizes that circumstances may render it harmful to the Muslim community. Here, the author explains the Imam's authority to revoke an aman and the treatment of a soldier who acted without consultation versus one who acted in good faith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving aman to an enemy. The general ruling is that it is valid and binding. However, the passage introduces an exception.
The base ruling is from earlier context: aman is sahih (valid).
2
Locate the exception
The exception is triggered by 'mafsadah' (harm). If the aman causes harm to the Muslims, the Imam may revoke it and inform the enemy.
The term 'mafsadah' is key—it must be a clear detriment to the community.
3
Compare the two sub-cases
Two scenarios are compared: (1) The Imam himself gave aman, then sees maslahah in breaking it. (2) A soldier gave aman during a siege, and it is harmful.
In both, the Imam can revoke. The difference lies in disciplining the soldier.
4
Analyze the soldier's excuse
If the soldier acted with 'nazar' (consideration of benefit) and delay would have lost that benefit, he is excused. Otherwise, he is disciplined for acting independently.
This shows the balance between authority and initiative in jihad.
5
Derive the principle
The overarching principle: The Imam's authority overrides a subordinate's aman if harm is present, but the subordinate's sincerity matters.
This is a Hanafi rule; other schools may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ إِلَّا أَنَّ يَكُونَ فِي ذَلِكَ مَفْسَدَةٌ فَيُسْدِي إِلَيْهِمْ كَمَا إِذَا أَمَّنَ الْإِمَامُ بِنَفْسِهِ ثُمَّ رَأَى الْمَصْلَحَةَ فِي النَّبْذِ وَقَدْ بَيَّنَّاهُ وَلَوْ حَاصَرَ الْإِمَامُ حِصْنًا وَأَمَّنَ وَاحِدٌ مِنَ الْجَيْشِ وَفِيهِ مَفْسَدَةٌ يَنْبُذُ الْإِمَامُ الْأَمَانَ لِمَنْ آمَنَ وَيُؤَدِّبُهُ الْإِمَامُ لِافْتِيَاتِهِ عَلَى رَأْيِهِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا كَانَ فِيهِ نَظَرٌ لِأَنَّهُ رُبَّمَا تَفُوتُ الْمَصْلَحَةُ بِالتَّأْخِيرِ فَكَانَ مَعْذُورًا
He said: Except that if in that there is harm, then he conveys to them [the breaking of the aman], just as when the Imam himself has given aman and then sees that the benefit is in abandoning it, and we have explained this. And if the Imam is besieging a fort and one of the army gives aman and in it there is harm, the Imam breaks the aman for those who were given aman and disciplines him for acting independently against his opinion, contrary to the case when there is consideration of benefit, because perhaps the benefit would be lost by delay, so he is excused.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage introduces an exception to the general ruling: if giving aman causes harm (mafsadah) to the Muslims, then the Imam may revoke the aman and inform the enemy. Two cases are compared: (1) If the Imam himself gave aman and later sees that breaking it is better, he can do so. (2) If a soldier gives aman during a siege and it is harmful, the Imam can break it and discipline the soldier for acting without consultation. However, if the soldier's action was based on a valid benefit (nazar) and delay would cause loss of that benefit, the soldier is excused. The commentary (tashrih) adds the story of Umm Hani, who gave protection to her brother-in-law during the conquest of Makkah; her brother wanted to kill him, but the Prophet upheld her aman because there was no harm. It also notes that a child or insane person's aman is not valid by consensus, but a slave's aman is valid according to the majority.

Key Terms
مفسدة (mafsadah): Harm or detriment to the Muslim community that outweighs the benefit of the aman.
نظر (nazar): Consideration of benefit (maslahah); acting based on perceived public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when can a soldier who gave aman be excused from discipline when the Imam revokes it?
A) If the soldier is of high rank.
B) If the soldier acted with nazar (consideration of benefit) and delay would lose the benefit.
C) If the soldier apologizes.
D) If the aman was given before the siege began.

Key Takeaway
A Muslim Imam may revoke a harmful aman, but a soldier who gave aman with sincere consideration of benefit is not disciplined even if the aman is cancelled.

Why a Dhimmi Cannot Grant Aman
States that a dhimmi cannot give aman to enemies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a dhimmi granting aman and explain the two reasons given in the text.

Core Idea
A dhimmi cannot grant aman because he is under suspicion and has no authority over Muslims.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a free Muslim can grant aman. Here, the Hidayah turns to the case of a dhimmi, a non-Muslim citizen of the Islamic state. Can he grant aman? The ruling is clear: no, for two reasons. Let's examine them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The subject is the aman (safe passage) given by a dhimmi. The ruling is that it is not permissible (la yajuz).
This means the aman is invalid (batil) and the act is prohibited (haram) for the dhimmi.
2
Extract the first reason
The text says 'because he is suspected of being with them' (mutahham). This means the dhimmi is suspected of sympathizing with the enemy due to shared disbelief, so his guarantee is unreliable.
Suspicion here is a legal presumption, not necessarily proven bias.
3
Extract the second reason
The text says 'and also because he has no authority over the Muslims' (la wilayata lahu ala al-muslimin). A dhimmi cannot bind Muslims to a commitment because he is not in a position of authority over them.
Wilayah over Muslims is exclusive to free Muslims, as established earlier.
4
Understand the implications
Because the aman is invalid, the Muslim community is not bound by it. The enemy remains a legitimate target unless aman is given by a proper authority (a free Muslim).
This ruling protects the integrity of Muslim security decisions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَمَانُ ذِمِّيٍّ لِأَنَّهُ مُتَّهَمٌ بِهِمْ وَكَذَا لَا وِلَايَةَ لَهُ عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ
And the aman of a dhimmi is not permissible because he is suspected of being with them, and also because he has no authority over the Muslims.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This is a short ruling stating that a dhimmi (a non-Muslim living under Muslim protection) cannot grant aman to an enemy. Two reasons are given: (1) The dhimmi is suspected of sympathizing with the enemy (since he shares their disbelief), so his aman is not reliable. (2) A dhimmi has no authority (wilayah) over Muslims, so he cannot bind them. The Hanafi school thus excludes dhimmis from the category of those who can grant aman, which is reserved for free Muslims (as per the previous ruling).

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection (dhimma) of the Islamic state, who pays jizyah.
أمان (aman): Safe passage or protection granted to an enemy, making his life and property inviolable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a dhimmi's aman invalid?
A) Because dhimmis are not Muslims and cannot represent the Muslim community
B) Because they are suspected of being with the enemy and have no authority over Muslims
C) Because they have not paid jizyah
D) Because they are not allowed to interact with enemies

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi cannot grant aman because he is suspect and lacks authority over Muslims; only free Muslims have this capacity.

Ruling on Aman Given by a Captive or Trader
States the invalidity of aman from a captive or trader, with reasons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the invalidity of aman given by a Muslim captive or trader and explain the three reasons (illal) for this ruling.

Core Idea
Aman requires the giver to be feared; a captive or trader is under enemy control, so his aman is invalid.

Aman (safe passage) is a key concept in Islamic international law, but not every Muslim can validly grant it. This lesson examines a specific exclusion: Muslim captives and traders in enemy territory. The Hanafi school provides clear reasoning for why their aman is ineffective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the granting of aman (safe passage) by a specific category of Muslims: a captive (aseer) or a trader (tajir) who enters enemy lands. The ruling is that such aman is invalid (la yajuz).
The text states 'wa la aseer wa la tajir' meaning 'and not a captive nor a trader' — i.e., their aman is not valid.
2
Extract the first reason: lack of fear
The text says 'li'anahuma maqhooran tahta aydihim fala yakhafunahu' — both are subdued under the enemy's control, so the enemy does not fear them. Aman is based on the fear that the granter can cause harm if the aman is violated.
The underlying illah (effective cause) is the absence of shawkah (power/authority) that would make the enemy fear retaliation.
3
Extract the second reason: coercion
The text says 'li'anahuma yujbaran alayhi' — both are forced into giving aman. A coerced contract is devoid of genuine consent and thus lacks legal benefit.
Coercion (ikrah) invalidates consent; aman is a contract that requires voluntary offer.
4
Infer the third reason: susceptibility to hostage-taking
The text begins the third reason: 'li'anahum kullama ishtadda al-amru alayhim yajiduna asiran aw tajiran' — whenever the situation becomes severe for the enemy, they can find a captive or trader (to use as a hostage). This further undermines any security promised by the aman.
The passage is cut off, but the implication is that the enemy can easily seize the granter, nullifying the protection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا أَسِيرُ وَلَا تَاجِرُ يَدْخُلُ عَلَيْهِمْ لِأَنَّهُمَا مَقْهُورَانِ تَحْتَ أَيْدِيهِمْ فَلَا يَخَافُونَهُ وَالْأَمَانُ يَخْتَصُّ بِمَحَلِّ الْخَوْفِ وَلِأَنَّهُمَا يُجْبَرَانِ عَلَيْهِ فَيَعْرَى الْأَمَانُ عَنِ الْمَصْلَحَةِ وَلِأَنَّهُمْ كُلَّمَا اشْتَدَّ الْأَمْرُ عَلَيْهِمْ يَجِدُونَ أَسِيرًا أَوْ تَاجِرًا ...
He said: And no captive (aseer) or trader (tajir) who enters upon them [can give aman] because both are subdued under their control, so they do not fear him, and aman is specific to the place of fear. And because both are forced into it, so the aman is devoid of benefit, and because whenever the situation becomes severe for them, they find a captive or trader...
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This ruling states that a Muslim captive (aseer) or a Muslim trader (tajir) who enters enemy territory cannot give valid aman. The reasons: (1) They are under the enemy's control (maqhooran), so the enemy does not fear them; aman is based on the fear that the one giving it can cause harm. (2) They are coerced (yujbaran) into giving it, so their aman lacks genuine benefit. (3) If the enemy faces difficulty, they can seize the captive or trader as a hostage, negating any sense of security. The passage appears to be cut off, but the reasoning is clear.

Key Terms
أسير (aseer): A Muslim prisoner of war held by the enemy.
تاجر (tajir): A Muslim merchant who travels to enemy lands for trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a captive's or trader's aman invalid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because they are not free Muslims
B) Because they are under enemy control and thus not feared
C) Because they lack faith
D) Because they are not soldiers

Key Takeaway
A captive or trader cannot give valid aman because they lack the power and free will that aman requires.

When the Imam May Nullify Aman for Public Harm
Explains when the imam can nullify aman given by himself or a soldier.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on nullifying aman when it causes mafsada and explain the imam's disciplinary authority over unauthorized grants of aman.

Core Idea
The imam may nullify aman if it harms Muslims, but must inform the enemy first.

Aman (safe conduct) is a solemn covenant, but it is not absolute when Muslim interests are at stake. The Hanafi school empowers the imam to break an aman that causes mafsada (harm) to the community, provided he notifies the enemy. Additionally, if a soldier grants aman without permission and it harms Muslims, the imam can nullify it and discipline the soldier—unless acting quickly served a greater benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
The passage begins with an exception: if granting aman leads to mafsada, the imam must inform the enemy. This establishes that harm overrides the default inviolability of aman.
2
Analyze the Case of the Imam's Own Aman
When the imam himself grants aman and later sees harm, he can break it after notification. This shows that even the imam's own act is revisable for public interest.
3
Analyze the Case of a Soldier's Unauthorized Aman
If a soldier grants aman without consulting the imam and it causes harm, the imam nullifies it and disciplines the soldier for overstepping. However, if the soldier's action brought an immediate benefit that would otherwise be lost, he is excused.
The distinction hinges on whether the soldier acted prematurely or with valid maslaha.
4
Examine the Dalil
The proof is the hadith of Umm Hani (RA), who gave aman during the conquest of Mecca. The Prophet (SAW) confirmed her aman, showing that aman from a valid grantor (including women) is binding unless harmful.
The hadith is narrated in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
5
Consider Related Rulings on Grantors
The commentary notes that aman from a child or insane person is invalid by consensus, but from a slave is valid according to the majority. This clarifies who can give valid aman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ فِي ذَلِكَ مَفْسَدَةٌ فَيُسْدِي إِلَيْهِمْ كَمَا إِذَا أَمَّنَ الْإِمَامُ بِنَفْسِهِ ثُمَّ رَأَى الْمَصْلَحَةَ فِي النَّقْضِ وَقَدْ بَيَّنَّاهُ وَلَوْ حَاصَرَ الْإِمَامُ حِصْنًا وَأَمَّنَ وَاحِدٌ مِنَ الْجَيْشِ وَفِيهِ مَفْسَدَةٌ يَنْقُضُ الْإِمَامُ الْأَمَانَ لِمَا عِنْدَنَا وَيُؤَدِّبُهُ الْإِمَامُ لِافْتِيَاتِهِ عَلَى رَأْيِهِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا كَانَ فِيهِ نَظَرٌ لِأَنَّهُ رُبَّمَا تَفُوتُ الْمَصْلَحَةُ بِالتَّأْخِيرِ فَكَانَ مَعْذُورًا
ترجمہ البتہ اگر آزاد مرد یا آزاد عورت کے اس طرح پناہ دینے میں اسلام کے حق میں کوئی خرابی ہو تو امام فی الفور کافروں کو اس عہد کے توڑنے کی خبر دیدے۔ جیسے کہ امام نے بذات خود کسی کو پناہ دی اور بعد میں اسے احساس ہوا کہ اس امان سے مسلمانوں کا نقصان ہے اس لئے اس عہد کو توڑ ڈالنے کے لئے کافروں کو اطلاع دیتا ہے اور اگر امام نے دشمن کے کسی قلعہ کا محاصرہ کیا اسی وقت لشکر میں سے کسی نے ان لوگوں کو امان دے دی حالانکہ امان دینے سے مسلمانوں کا نقصان ہو تو امام اس امان کو توڑ کر کفار کو اس سے مطلع کر دے۔ ساتھ ہی اس لشکری کو ایسا کرنے پر کچھ سزا بھی دے۔ کیونکہ اس نے امام کی رائے کے خلاف اپنی رائے کوترجیح دی۔ ہاں اگر اس کے امان دینے میں عام مصلحت بھی نظر آ جائے تو اسے سزادی جائے ۔ کیونکہ کسی کی تاخیر میں بعض موقع میں اصل مصلحت ختم ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے اس کو جلد بازی کرنے پر معذور سمجھا جائے گا۔
تشریح اگر امام کے علاوہ دوسرا کوئی لشکری امام سے مشورہ کئے بغیر از خود کسی کو پناہ دے اور اس میں عام مسلموں کا نقصان ہو تو امام اسے رد کر سکتا ہے اور اس شخص کو کچھ سزا بھی دے سکتا ہے لیکن اگر نقصان نہ ہو تو اس امان کو بحال رکھ سکتا ہے۔ چنانچہ حضرت ام ہانی رضی اللہ عنہا نے اپنے کسی دیور (شوہر کے بھائی) کو پناہ دے دی تھی۔ مگر ان کے اپنے بھائی نے اس کے خلاف اپنی بہن سے کہا کہ میں تو اس شخص کو قتل کر کے رہوں گا۔ اس لئے انہوں نے آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم سے اپنے بھائی کے خلاف شکایت کی تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ تم نے جسے پناہ دی ہے میں نے اسے بحال رکھ کر خود بھی اسے پناہ دیدی ہے۔ رواہ البخاری و مسلم اور حضرت ام ہانی نے عبداللہ بن ابی ربیعہ اور حارث بن ہشام دو دیوروں (پہلے شوہر کے دو بھائیوں کو پناہ دی تھی ۔ یہ واقعہ فتح مکہ کا ہے۔ معلوم ہونا چاہئے کہ بچہ اور دیوانہ کی پناہ بالا جماع صحیح نہیں ہے لیکن غلام کا پناہ دینا جمہور کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔
He said: Except that if there is harm in that, then he informs them, as when the imam himself grants aman and later sees benefit in breaking it—and we have explained it. And if the imam besieges a fort and one of the army grants aman and there is harm in it, the imam breaks the aman according to us, and the imam disciplines him for acting without his opinion, unlike when there is consideration, because perhaps the benefit may be lost by delay, so he is excused.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the imam's authority over aman (safe conduct) granted to enemy combatants. The passage opens with a general principle: if granting aman leads to mafsada (harm) for the Muslims, the imam must notify the enemy before breaking the covenant. The example given is when the imam himself grants aman and later realizes harm. Similarly, if a soldier grants aman without consultation and it harms Muslims, the imam may nullify it and discipline the soldier for overstepping his authority. However, if there is a valid maslaha (benefit) in the soldier's action—for instance, if waiting for permission would cause the opportunity to be lost—then the soldier is excused. The subsequent Urdu commentary (Tashrih) reinforces this: the imam can reject an unauthorized aman if it causes harm, but if no harm, he may uphold it. It cites the incident of Umm Hani (RA) who gave aman to her brother-in-law; the Prophet (SAW) confirmed her aman, showing that a woman's aman is valid and the imam can confirm it. Additionally, the commentary notes that a child or insane person's aman is invalid by consensus, while a slave's aman is valid according to the majority (jumhur). This lesson thus establishes the conditions under which aman can be given and overridden, emphasizing the imam's role in safeguarding Muslim interests.

Key Terms
الأمان (al-amān): Safe conduct or amnesty granted to an enemy combatant, ensuring their safety from attack.
مفسدة (mafsadah): Harm or detriment to the interests of the Muslim community.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can an imam nullify an aman given by a soldier?
A) If the soldier is a slave
B) If the aman harms Muslims
C) If the aman was given without the imam's permission
D) If the enemy is powerful

Key Takeaway
Aman is binding, but the imam may nullify it with notification if it causes harm to Muslims; unauthorized aman with harm is nullified and the soldier disciplined, unless acting quickly served a greater benefit.
